缩略语表

List of Abbreviations

前言

Foreword

前言

Preface

不读书的方式

Ways of Not Reading

I. 你不知道的书

I. Books You Don’t Know

（读者将会看到，正如穆齐尔的角色所展示的那样，与保持我们对书籍的整体看法相比，阅读任何特定的书籍都是浪费时间）

(in which the reader will see, as demonstrated by a character of Musil’s, that reading any particular book is a waste of time compared to keeping our perspective about books overall)

II. 你读过的书籍

II. Books You Have Skimmed

（我们和瓦莱里一样，都认为只要浏览过一本书就足以写一篇文章，而对于某些书，不这样做甚至可能是不合适的）

(in which we see, along with Valéry, that it is enough to have skimmed a book to be able to write an article about it, and that with certain books it might even be inappropriate to do otherwise)

III. 你听说过的书

III. Books You Have Heard Of

（翁贝托·埃科在其中表明，完全没有必要手拿一本书就能详细地谈论它，只要你听和读别人对它的评论就可以了）

(in which Umberto Eco shows that it is wholly unnecessary to have held a book in your hand to be able to speak about it in detail, as long as you listen to and read what others say about it)

IV. 你忘记的书

IV. Books You Have Forgotten

（其中，我们与蒙田一起提出了这样的问题：一本你读过却完全忘记的书，甚至你忘记自己读过的书，是否还是一本你读过的书）

(in which, along with Montaigne, we raise the question of whether a book you have read and completely forgotten, and which you have even forgotten you have read, is still a book you have read)

文学对抗

Literary Confrontations

V. 社会遭遇

V. Encounters in Society

（格雷厄姆·格林在其中描述了一个噩梦般的场景，主人公发现自己面对着满满一礼堂的崇拜者，他们不耐烦地等待着他讲述自己还没读过的书）

(in which Graham Greene describes a nightmarish situation where the hero finds himself facing an auditorium full of admirers impatiently waiting for him to speak about books that he hasn’t read)

VI. 与教授的邂逅

VI. Encounters with Professors

（我们与西非的蒂夫人族一致确认，完全没有必要打开一本书来发表开明的观点，即使你在此过程中惹恼了专家）

(in which we confirm, along with the Tiv tribe of western Africa, that it is wholly unnecessary to have opened a book in order to deliver an enlightened opinion on it, even if you displease the specialists in the process)

VII. 与作家的邂逅

VII. Encounters with the Writer

（皮埃尔·西尼亚克证明，在作家面前注意自己的言行很重要，尤其是当他本人没有读过他所著的书时）

(in which Pierre Siniac demonstrates that it may be important to watch what you say in the presence of a writer, especially when he himself hasn’t read the book whose author he is)

VIII. 与心爱之人的邂逅

VIII. Encounters with Someone You Love

（从中我们可以看到，比尔·默里和他的土拨鼠，通过谈论某人喜欢的书（即使他或她自己没有读过）来吸引某人的理想方式是让时间停止）

(in which we see, along with Bill Murray and his groundhog, that the ideal way to seduce someone by speaking about books he or she loves without having read them yourself would be to bring time to a halt)

行为方式

Ways of Behaving

IX. 不感到羞耻

IX. Not Being Ashamed

（其中确认，就大卫·洛奇的小说而言，谈论一本你没读过的书的首要条件是不要感到羞耻）

(in which it is confirmed, with regard to the novels of David Lodge, that the first condition for speaking about a book you haven’t read is not to be ashamed)

X. 实施你的想法

X. Imposing Your Ideas

（巴尔扎克证明，将你的观点强加于书本的关键之一是要记住书本不是一个固定的物体，即使用绳子将它绑起来也不足以阻止它的运动）

(in which Balzac proves that one key to imposing your point of view on a book is to remember that the book is not a fixed object, and that even tying it up with string will not be sufficient to stop its motion)

XI. 发明书籍

XI. Inventing Books

（在阅读 S seki 时，我们听从了一只猫和一位戴金边眼镜的艺术家的建议，他们各自在不同的领域中宣扬发明的必要性）

(in which, reading Sseki, we follow the advice of a cat and an artist in gold-rimmed spectacles, who each, in different fields of activity, proclaim the necessity of invention)

XII. 谈论你自己

XII. Speaking About Yourself

（我们与奥斯卡·王尔德一致认为，阅读一本书的适当时间是十分钟，十分钟之后，您就会忘记，阅读这本书主要是为您撰写自传找借口）

(in which we conclude, along with Oscar Wilde, that the appropriate time span for reading a book is ten minutes, after which you risk forgetting that the encounter is primarily a pretext for writing your autobiography)

结语

Epilogue

我从来没有读过一本必须评论的书；它会让你产生偏见。

I never read a book I must review; it prejudices you so.

-奥斯卡·王尔德

—OSCAR WILDE

前言

Foreword

皮埃尔·巴亚尔将他的读者——我这个读者——置于一个独特的矛盾境地。刚刚读完他诙谐幽默的《如何谈论你没读过的书》后，我发现我根本没有理由读这本书。但是，如果没有读过这本书，我怎么会知道我也可以浏览一下，或者可能在某个地方听说过，或者可能完全根据其他读者对这本书的评论，根据文化中流传的对一部作品的既定看法来形成对这本书的理解呢？此外，没有读过这本书不应该——皮埃尔·巴亚尔向我保证——阻止我自信而博学地谈论它，甚至阻止我写这些简短的介绍性赞赏的话。但是，如果没有巴亚尔的明智建议，我怎么会知道这一点呢？我只能在他睿智而原始的著作中找到这些建议。

PIERRE BAYARD PUTSHIS readers—this reader—in a uniquely paradoxical position. Having just read his witty How to Talk About Books You Haven’t Read, I have now discovered that there was no reason for me to have read it in the first place. But without having read it, how would I have known that I could just as well have skimmed it, or perhaps heard about it somewhere, or possibly formed a sense of the book based entirely on what other readers have said about it, on the sort of received opinions about a work that float around in the culture? In addition, not having read the book shouldn’t—or so Pierre Bayard has assured me—prevent me from talking confidently and learnedly about it, or even from writing these brief, introductory words of appreciation. But how would I have known that without Bayard’s sage advice, which I could only have found in his wise and original volume?

无论如何，我很高兴我读了拜亚的书。如果我读得太快，我可能会错过他给我们举出的文学双关语的激动人心的例子，保罗·瓦莱里在赞扬马塞尔·普鲁斯特和阿纳托尔·法朗士的同时，明确表示他几乎没有读过他们的作品。如果我没有读过拜亚，我就不会下定决心不仅要读——而且要重读——格雷厄姆·格林的《第三人》 ，以及蒙田哀叹记忆力衰退及其对他阅读和记住所读内容的能力的影响的文章。劳拉·博汉南试图与一群西非部落成员讨论《哈姆雷特》，我不会如此开心，他们的反应既有趣又有启发性，与她所期待的对莎士比亚普遍性的即时、跨文化认可不同步。我也不会很高兴地发现，拜尔给那些遇到自己没有读过书的作家的人的建议非常令人满意地证实了我的观察和经验：“赞美它，但不要详述。作家并不期望对他的书进行总结或理性分析，甚至不希望你尝试这样做。他只希望你在保持最大程度的模糊性的同时，告诉他你喜欢他写的东西。”

In any case, the fact remains that I am very glad I did read Bayard’s book. Had I skimmed it too rapidly, I might have missed the chapter in which he gives us the thrilling examples of literary doublespeak with which Paul Valéry eulogized Marcel Proust and Anatole France while making it quite clear that he had hardly read a word of their work. Had I not read Bayard, I would not have found myself determined not only to read—but to reread—Graham Greene’s The Third Man, as well as the essay in which Montaigne lamented his failing memory and its effect on his ability to read and retain what he had read. I would not have been so thoroughly entertained by Laura Bohannan’s attempt to discuss Hamlet with a group of West African tribesmen whose responses were hilariously and informatively out of synch with the instant, cross-cultural recognition of Shakespeare’s universality that she expected. Nor would I have been so pleased to discover that Bayard’s advice to those who meet writers of books they have not read confirms, so very gratifyingly, my own observation and experience: “Praise it without going into detail. An author does not expect a summary or a rational analysis of his book, and would even prefer you not to attempt such a thing. He expects only that, while maintaining the greatest possible degree of ambiguity, you will tell him that you like what he wrote.”

读过这些段落后，我只能希望自己说得没有太含糊，我最喜欢皮埃尔·巴亚尔对不读书的可允许性、重要性和绝对必要性的巧妙思考，因为它在我们不知不觉中变成了对阅读心理学和文学目的的研究，成为了对阅读乐趣和我们不能没有阅读的所有理由的赞美诗。

Having read such passages, I can only hope that I am not being insufficiently ambiguous when I say that what I liked best about Pierre Bayard’s sly meditation on the permissibility, the importance, and the sheer necessity of not reading is how, without our quite being aware of it, it becomes a study of the psychology of reading and of the purposes of literature, and a hymn to the pleasures of reading and to all the reasons why we cannot live without it.

—弗朗辛·普罗斯

—Francine Prose

前言

Preface

我出生在一个很少读书的环境里，从读书中获得的乐趣很少，而且也没有时间投入到读书中，所以我经常发现自己处于一种微妙的境地，不得不表达对没有读过的书的想法。

BORN INTO A MILIEU where reading was rare, deriving little pleasure from the activity, and lacking in any case the time to devote myself to it, I have often found myself in the delicate situation of having to express my thoughts on books I haven’t read.

因为我在大学教文学，所以事实上无法避免评论那些我大部分时间甚至都没有打开过的书。确实，我的大多数学生也是如此，但是如果他们中哪怕有一个人读过我正在讨论的文本，那么我的课堂随时都有可能被打乱，我也会感到羞辱。

Because I teach literature at the university level, there is, in fact, no way to avoid commenting on books that most of the time I haven’t even opened. It’s true that this is also the case for the majority of my students, but if even one of them has read the text I’m discussing, there is a risk that at any moment my class will be disrupted and I will find myself humiliated.

此外，我经常被要求讨论我书籍和文章中的出版物，因为这些出版物大多与他人的书籍和文章有关。这种做法甚至更加成问题，因为与口头陈述不同（口头陈述可能包含不准确的内容，但不会造成任何后果），书面评论会留下痕迹，可以验证。

In addition, I am regularly called on to discuss publications in my books and articles, since these for the most part concern the books and articles of others. This exercise is even more problematic, since unlike spoken statements—which can include imprecisions without consequence—written commentaries leave traces and can be verified.

由于这种极为常见的情况，我相信自己有能力，即使不能就这一主题提供任何真正的教训，至少也能传达对非读者体验的更深刻理解，并对这一禁忌话题进行思考。

As a result of such all-too-familiar situations, I believe I am well positioned, if not to offer any real lesson on the subject, at least to convey a deeper understanding of the non-reader’s experience and to undertake a meditation on this forbidden subject.

很少有文章赞美不读书的优点，这并不奇怪。事实上，要描述你在这方面的经历（我将在这里尝试这样做），需要一定的勇气，因为这样做不可避免地会与一系列内在的限制相冲突。其中至少有三个是至关重要的。

It is unsurprising that so few texts extol the virtues of non-reading. Indeed, to describe your experience in this area, as I will attempt here, demands a certain courage, for doing so clashes inevitably with a whole series of internalized constraints. Three of these, at least, are crucial.

这些限制中的第一个可以称为阅读的义务。我们仍然生活在一个社会中，尽管它可能正在衰落，但阅读仍然是一种崇拜的对象。这种崇拜尤其适用于一些经典文本——列表因你所处的圈子而异——如果你想被认真对待，实际上就必须读过这些文本。

The first of these constraints might be called the obligation to read. We still live in a society, on the decline though it may be, where reading remains the object of a kind of worship. This worship applies particularly to a number of canonical texts—the list varies according to the circles you move in—which it is practically forbidden not to have read if you want to be taken seriously.

第二个限制与第一个类似，但又截然不同，可以称为彻底阅读的义务。如果不读书会被人反对，那么快速阅读或略读几乎同样糟糕，尤其是这样说。例如，文学知识分子承认他们只是翻阅了普鲁斯特的作品，而没有完整地读过它，这几乎是不可想象的——尽管大多数人确实如此。

The second constraint, similar to the first but nonetheless distinct, might be called the obligation to read thoroughly. If it’s frowned upon not to read, it’s almost as bad to read quickly or to skim, and especially to say so. For example, it’s virtually unthinkable for literary intellectuals to acknowledge that they have flipped through Proust’s work without having read it in its entirety—though this is certainly the case for most of them.

第三个限制与我们讨论书籍的方式有关。在我们的文化中，人们有一种心照不宣的理解，即一个人必须读过一本书才能准确地谈论它。然而，根据我的经验，完全有可能就一本你没读过的书进行一场引人入胜的对话——包括，也许尤其是与另一个也没读过这本书的人。

The third constraint concerns the way we discuss books. There is a tacit understanding in our culture that one must read a book in order to talk about it with any precision. In my experience, however, it’s totally possible to carry on an engaging conversation about a book you haven’t read— including, and perhaps especially, with someone else who hasn’t read it either.

此外，正如我将要指出的，如果你没有读完整本书，甚至没有打开过它，那么有时更容易公正地评价一本书。在这本书中，我将强调阅读的风险——这种风险经常被低估——对于任何打算谈论书籍的人来说，尤其是对于那些计划评论书籍的人来说。

Moreover, as I will argue, it is sometimes easier to do justice to a book if you haven’t read it in its entirety—or even opened it. Throughout this book, I will insist on the risks of reading—so frequently underestimated—for anyone who intends to talk about books, and even more so for those who plan to review them.

这种压制性的义务和禁令制度的结果是，在我们实际阅读的书籍问题上产生了普遍的虚伪。除了金融和性之外，我知道很少有私人生活的领域像它们一样难以获得准确的信息。

The effect of this repressive system of obligations and prohibitions has been to generate a widespread hypocrisy on the subject of books that we actually have read. I know few areas of private life, with the exception of finance and sex, in which it’s as difficult to obtain accurate information.

在专家中，撒谎是常态，我们撒谎的程度与所讨论书籍的重要性成正比。虽然我自己读的书相对较少，但我对某些书很熟悉——这里我再次想到普鲁斯特——我能够判断我的同事在谈论他的作品时是否说的是实话，并且知道事实上，他们很少说真话。

Among specialists, mendacity is the rule, and we tend to lie in proportion to the significance of the book under consideration. Although I’ve read relatively little myself, I’m familiar enough with certain books—here, again, I’m thinking of Proust—to be able to evaluate whether my colleagues are telling the truth when they talk about his work, and to know that in fact, they rarely are.

我们对别人说的这些谎言首先就是我们对自己说的谎言，因为我们甚至难以承认我们没有读过那些被认为必不可少的书。在这里，就像在生活的许多其他领域一样，我们表现出惊人的能力来重建过去以更好地符合我们的愿望。

These lies we tell to others are first and foremost lies we tell ourselves, for we have trouble acknowledging even to ourselves that we haven’t read the books that are deemed essential. And here, just as in so many other domains of life, we show an astonishing ability to reconstruct the past to better conform to our wishes.

我们谈论书籍时撒谎的倾向是人们不读书的耻辱感的必然结果，而这种耻辱感又源于（毫无疑问）根植于儿童早期的一整套焦虑。因此，如果我们希望学会如何从谈论我们没读过的书的谈话中毫发无损地脱身，就必须分析承认不读书所引起的无意识内疚感。本书的目标就是帮助人们减轻这种内疚感，至少在一定程度上是这样。

Our propensity to lie when we talk about books is a logical consequence of the stigma attached to non-reading, which in turn arises from a whole network of anxieties rooted (no doubt) in early childhood. If we wish, then, to learn how to emerge unscathed from conversations about books we haven’t read, it will be necessary to analyze the unconscious guilt that an admission of non-reading elicits. It is to help assuage such guilt, at least in part, that is the goal of this book.

反思未读的书及其引发的讨论就更加困难了，因为“不读书”这个概念本身就很模糊，所以当我们说读过一本书时，我们往往很难知道我们是否在撒谎。这个问题本身就意味着我们可以在阅读和不阅读之间划一条清晰的界线，而事实上，我们接触文本的许多方式介于两者之间。

It is all the more difficult to reflect on unread books and the discussions they engender because the concept of non-reading is itself unclear, and so it is often hard to know whether we’re lying or not when we say that we’ve read a book. The very question implies that we can draw a clear line between reading and not reading, while in fact many of the ways we encounter texts sit somewhere between the two.

在我们仔细阅读过的书和我们从未听说过的书之间，存在着一系列值得我们关注的层次。对于我们可能读过的书，我们必须考虑阅读的含义，这个术语可以指代多种实践。相反，许多我们似乎没有读过的书却对我们产生了影响，因为它们的声誉在社会上广为传播。

Between a book we’ve read closely and a book we’ve never even heard of, there is a whole range of gradations that deserve our attention. In the case of books we have supposedly read, we must consider just what is meant by reading, a term that can refer to a variety of practices. Conversely, many books that by all appearances we haven’t read exert an influence on us nevertheless, as their reputations spread through society.

阅读与不阅读之间界限的不确定性将促使我更广泛地思考我们与书籍的互动方式。因此，我的探究将不仅限于开发逃避尴尬的文学冲突的技巧。通过分析这些情况，我还将尝试阐明一种真正的阅读理论——一种摒弃我们认为阅读是一个简单、无缝过程的形象，而是包容阅读的所有断层线、不足和近似值。

The uncertainty of the border between reading and not reading will lead me to reflect more generally on the ways we interact with books. Thus my inquiry will not be limited to developing techniques for escaping awkward literary confrontations. By analyzing these situations, I will also attempt to articulate a genuine theory of reading—one that dispenses with our image of it as a simple, seamless process and, instead, embraces all its fault lines, deficiencies, and approximations.

这些评论顺理成章地引出了本书的组织结构。我将从第一部分开始描述不读书的主要类型——正如我们将看到的，不读书远远超出了不打开书本的行为。在不同程度上，我们浏览过的书、听说过的书和我们忘记的书也属于不读书这一丰富的类别。

These remarks bring us logically to the organization of this book. I will begin in the first section by describing the principal kinds of non-reading—which, as we will see, goes far beyond the act of leaving a book unopened. To varying degrees, books we’ve skimmed, books we’ve heard about, and books we have forgotten also fall into the rich category that is non-reading.

第二部分将专门分析我们可能会谈论自己没有读过的书的具体情况。残酷的生活给我们带来了大量这样的情况，而列举所有这些情况超出了本项目的范围。但一些重要的例子——有时是伪装成我自己的经历——可能让我们发现一些模式，我将借鉴这些模式来推进我的论点。

A second section will be devoted to analyzing concrete situations in which we might find ourselves talking about books we haven’t read. Life, in its cruelty, presents us with a plethora of such circumstances, and it is beyond the scope of this project to enumerate them all. But a few significant examples— sometimes borrowed, in disguised form, from my own experience—may allow us to identify some patterns that I will draw on in advancing my argument.

第三部分也是最重要的部分是我写这本书的动机。它包括一系列简单的建议，这些建议是我一生不读书时收集的。这些建议旨在帮助任何遇到这些社交困境的人尽可能好地解决它，甚至从中受益，同时也允许他或她深入反思阅读行为。

The third and most important section is the one that motivated me to write this book. It consists of a series of simple recommendations gathered over a lifetime of non-reading. This advice is intended to help anyone who encounters one of these social dilemmas to resolve it as well as possible, and even to benefit from the situation, while also permitting him or her to reflect deeply on the act of reading.

这些开场白不仅旨在解释这本书的总体结构，也是为了提醒我们，我们所有传统的书籍引用方式都与真理有着特殊的关系。为了触及问题的本质，我认为我们必须大大改变我们谈论书籍的方式，甚至改变我们用来描述书籍的具体词语。

These opening remarks are intended not only to explain the general structure of this book, but also to remind us of the peculiar relation to truth that infuses all our traditional ways of referring to books. To get to the heart of things, I believe we must significantly modify how we talk about books, even the specific words we use to describe them.

根据我的一般论点，即“已读书籍”的概念是模糊的，从现在开始，我将通过缩写系统表明我对所引用的每本书的个人了解程度。1这一系列指示将在我们进行过程中得到澄清，旨在补充传统上出现在脚注中的指示，这些指示用于指示作者理论上已阅读的书籍（同上，同上等）。事实上，正如我将通过自己的案例揭示的那样，作者经常提到我们知之甚少的书籍，因此，我将尝试通过具体说明我对每本书的了解来打破对阅读的错误表述。

In keeping with my general thesis, which posits that the notion of the book-that-has-been-read is ambiguous, from this point forward I will indicate the extent of my personal knowledge of each book I cite, via a system of abbreviations.1 This series of indications, which will be clarified as we go, is intended to complete those that traditionally appear in footnotes, and that are used to designate the books the author theoretically has read (op. cit., ibid., etc.). In fact, as I will reveal through my own case, authors often refer to books of which we have only scanty knowledge, and so I will attempt to break with the misrepresentation of reading by specifying exactly what I know of each book.

我将用第二组指标来补充第一组指标，表达我对所引用书籍的看法，无论这些书籍是否经过我的手。2既然我会争辩说评价一本书并不需要读过它，那么，毕竟，我没有理由不对我遇到的任何作品做出判断，即使我以前从未听说过它们。3

I will complement this first series of indications with a second series conveying my opinion of the books being cited, whether or not they have ever passed through my hands.2 Since I will argue that evaluating a book does not require having read it, there is, after all, no reason for me to refrain from passing judgment on whatever works I come across, even if I have never heard of them before.3

这种新的符号系统——我希望有一天能被广泛采用——旨在不断提醒我们，我们与书籍的关系并不是某些批评家让我们想象的连续而同质的过程，也不是某种透明的自我知识的场所。我们与书籍的关系是一个被记忆的幽灵所困扰的阴暗空间，书籍的真正价值在于它们能够召唤这些幽灵。



This new system of notations—which I hope will one day be widely adopted—is intended as a ongoing reminder that our relation to books is not the continuous and homogeneous process that certain critics would have us imagine, nor the site of some transparent self-knowledge. Our relation to books is a shadowy space haunted by the ghosts of memory, and the real value of books lies in their ability to conjure these specters.



1.前四章将解释所用的四个缩写。UB 表示我不熟悉的书籍；SB 表示我浏览过的书籍；HB 表示我听说过的书籍；FB 表示我忘记的书籍（参见缩写列表）。这些缩写并不相互排斥。每个书名都会给出指示，并且只在第一次提及时给出。

1. The four abbreviations used will be explained in the first four chapters. UB designates books unknown to me; SB, books I have skimmed;HB, books I have heard of; FB, books I have forgotten (see the list of abbreviations). These abbreviations are not mutually exclusive. An indication is given for every book title, and only at its first mention.

2 . 使用的缩写为 ++（极度正面评价）、+（正面评价）、-（负面评价）和 --（极度负面评价）。请参阅缩写列表。

2. The abbreviations used are ++ (extremely positive opinion), + (positive opinion), - (negative opinion), and -- (extremely negative opinion). See the list of abbreviations.

3.可以看出，这种符号系统的价值还在于它省略了 RB（已读过的书）和 NRB（未读过的书）等符号，这些符号本来是人们所期望的，但永远不会被使用。书籍正是与这种人为的区分相对立的，这种区分传达了一种阅读的形象，让人很难思考我们实际的阅读体验。

3. It will be observed that this system of notations is valuable as well for its omissions, specifically RB (book that has been read) and NRB (book that has not been read), the very notations one might have expected, which will never be used. It is precisely in opposition to this kind of artificial distinction that the book is organized, a distinction conveying an image of reading that makes it hard to think about the way we actually experience it.

不读书的方式

Ways of Not Reading

你不知道的书

I

Books You Don’t Know

（读者将会看到，正如穆齐尔的角色所展示的那样，与保持我们对书籍的整体看法相比，阅读任何特定的书籍都是浪费时间）

(in which the reader will see, as demonstrated by a character of Musil’s, that reading any particular book is a waste of time compared to keeping our perspective about books overall)

不读书的方法不止一种，其中最激进的就是根本不打开一本书。对于任何一位读者来说，无论他多么专注，这种完全的禁欲必然适用于几乎所有已出版的书籍，因此，事实上，这构成了我们与书籍建立联系的主要方式。我们一定不要忘记，即使是一位博览群书的人，也只能接触到现存书籍的极小部分。因此，除非他完全放弃一切对话和写作，否则他将永远不得不表达自己对未读过的书的想法。

THERE IS MORE THAN one way not to read, the most radical of which is not to open a book at all. For any given reader, however dedicated he might be, such total abstention necessarily holds true for virtually everything that has been published, and thus in fact this constitutes our primary way of relating to books. We must not forget that even a prodigious reader never has access to more than an infinitesimal fraction of the books that exist. As a result, unless he abstains definitively from all conversation and all writing, he will find himself forever obliged to express his thoughts on books he hasn’t read.

如果我们将这种态度推向极端，就会出现绝对不读书的人，他们从不打开书本，却了解书本，并毫不犹豫地谈论它们。《没有个性的人》1中的图书管理员就是这种情况，他是穆齐尔小说中的次要人物，但他激进的立场和捍卫立场的勇气使他成为我们论证中不可或缺的一部分。

If we take this attitude to the extreme, we arrive at the case of the absolute non-reader, who never opens a book and yet knows them and talks about them without hesitation. Such is the case of the librarian in The Man Without Qualities,1 a secondary character in Musil’s novel, but one whose radical position and courage in defending it make him essential to our argument.

穆齐尔的小说发生在上世纪初，一个名叫卡卡尼亚的国家，这是对奥匈帝国的戏仿。一个名为“平行行动”的爱国运动组织成立，旨在为即将到来的皇帝登基周年举办盛大的庆祝活动，旨在为世界其他国家树立救赎的榜样。

Musil’s novel takes place at the beginning of the last century in a country called Kakania, a parody of the Austro-Hungarian Empire. A patriotic movement, known as Parallel Action, has been founded to organize a lavish celebration of the upcoming anniversary of the emperor’s reign, a celebration that is intended to serve as a redemptive example for the rest of the world.

穆齐尔将“平行行动”的领导人描绘成许多可笑的木偶，他们都在寻找一种“救赎理念”，他们用最模糊的措辞不断地唤起这种理念——事实上，他们既不知道这种理念是什么，也不知道这种理念如何在他们的国家之外发挥救赎作用。

The leaders of Parallel Action, whom Musil depicts as so many ridiculous marionettes, are thus all in search of a “redemptive idea,” which they evoke endlessly yet in the vaguest of terms—for indeed, they have neither the slightest inkling of what the idea might be nor how it might perform its redemptive function beyond their country’s borders.

在该运动的领导人中，最可笑的是施图姆将军（德语中意为“哑巴”）。施图姆决心在其他人之前发现救赎的理念，作为对他心爱的女人——狄奥蒂玛的献礼，狄奥蒂玛在《平行行动》中也扮演着重要角色：

Among the movement’s leaders, one of the most ridiculous is General Stumm (which means “mute” in German). Stumm is determined to discover the redemptive idea before the others as an offering to the woman he loves—Diotima, who is also prominent within Parallel Action:

“你还记得吧，”他说，“我下定决心要找到狄奥蒂玛想要的那个伟大的救赎想法，并把它献给她。事实证明，有很多伟大的想法，但只有其中一种才是最伟大的——这很合乎逻辑，不是吗？——所以问题在于把它们排序。” 2

“You remember, don’t you,” he said, “that I’d made up my mind to find that great redeeming idea Diotima wants and lay it at her feet. It turns out that there are lots of great ideas, but only one of them can be the greatest—that’s only logical, isn’t it?—so it’s a matter of putting them in order.”2

将军对于思想及其运用经验甚少，更不用说开发新思想的方法了，他决定前往皇家图书馆——这个新思想的源泉——“了解对手的资源”并以最高效的方式发现“救赎思想”。

The general, a man of little experience with ideas and their manipulation, never mind methods for developing new ones, decides to go to the imperial library—that wellspring of fresh thoughts—to “become informed about the resources of the adversary” and to discover the “redemptive idea” with utmost efficiency.

参观图书馆让这位对书籍了解不多的人陷入了深深的痛苦之中。作为一名军官，他习惯于处于主导地位，但在这里，他发现自己面对的是一种没有地标、没有任何东西可以依靠的知识：

The visit to the library plunges this man of limited familiarity with books into profound anguish. As a military officer, he is used to being in a position of dominance, yet here he finds himself confronted with a form of knowledge that offers him no landmarks, nothing to hold on to:

“我们在那座巨大的图书馆里列队行进，我不介意告诉你我并没有特别不知所措；那些书排得并不比阅兵式上的驻军糟糕。尽管如此，过了一会儿，我还是忍不住开始在脑子里计算起来，得到了一个意想不到的答案。你知道，我一直在想，如果我每天读一本书，这自然会很累，但我总有一天会读完，然后，即使我不得不跳过几本，我也可以在知识世界中占据一定的地位。但是，你猜图书管理员会对我说些什么呢？我们一直走着，看不到尽头，我问他这个疯狂的图书馆里有多少本书？三百五十万，他告诉我。我们刚刚得到了七十万左右，但我一直在脑子里计算着这些数字；我就不告诉你细节了，但我后来在办公室用铅笔和纸核实了一下：我需要一万年的时间才能完成我的计划。” 3

“We marched down the ranks in that colossal store house of books, and I don’t mind telling you I was not particularly overwhelmed; those rows of books are not particularly worse than a garrison on parade. Still, after a while I couldn’t help starting to do some figuring in my head, and I got an unexpected answer. You see, I had been thinking that if I read a book a day, it would naturally be exhausting, but I would be bound to get to the end sometime and then, even if I had to skip a few, I could claim a certain position in the world of the intellect. But what do you suppose the librarian said to me, as we walked on and on, without an end in sight, and I asked him how many books they had in this crazy library? Three and a half million, he tells me. We had just got to the seven hundred thousands or so, but I kept on doing these figures in my head; I’ll spare you the details, but I checked it out later in the office, with pencil and paper: it would take me ten thousand years to carry out my plan.”3

面对无限多的书籍，我们多少会觉得根本不应该读书。面对如此庞大的书籍数量，几乎全部都是未知的，我们怎么能逃避这样的结论：即使一生的阅读也是完全徒劳的？

This encounter with the infinity of available books offers a certain encouragement not to read at all. Faced with a quantity of books so vast that nearly all of them must remain unknown, how can we escape the conclusion that even a lifetime of reading is utterly in vain?

阅读首先是非阅读。即使对最热爱阅读的人来说，拿起书本并打开书本的行为也掩盖了同时发生的反向动作：不自觉地不拿起和打开宇宙中所有其他书籍的行为。

Reading is first and foremost non-reading. Even in the case of the most passionate lifelong readers, the act of picking up and opening a book masks the countergesture that occurs at the same time: the involuntary act of not picking up and not opening all the other books in the universe.

如果《没有个性的人》提出了文化素养如何与无限相交的问题，那么它也提出了一个可能的解决方案，即帮助施图姆将军的图书管理员所采用的解决方案。这位图书管理员找到了一种方法，让他在图书馆的数百万册书籍中（如果不是在世界上所有的书籍中）找到自己的位置。他的技巧非常简单，非常了不起：

If The Man Without Qualities brings up the problem of how cultural literacy intersects with the infinite, it also presents a possible solution, one adopted by the librarian helping General Stumm. This librarian has found a way to orient himself among the millions of volumes in his library, if not among all the books in the world. His technique is extraordinary in its simplicity:

“当我没有放开他时，他突然站了起来，穿着颤颤巍巍的裤子，慢慢地、非常强调地说道，好像是时候说出最终的秘密了：‘将军，’他说，‘如果您想知道我怎么知道这里的每一本书，我可以告诉您！因为我从来没有读过任何一本书。’” 4

“When I didn’t let go of him he suddenly pulled himself up, rearing up in those wobbly pants of his, and said in a slow, very emphatic way, as though the time had come to give away the ultimate secret: ‘General,’ he said, ‘if you want to know how I know about every book here, I can tell you! Because I never read any of them.’ ”4

将军对这位不同寻常的图书管理员感到惊讶，他警惕地避免阅读，并不是因为缺乏文化，而恰恰相反，是为了更好地了解他的书籍：

The general is astonished by this unusual librarian, who vigilantly avoids reading not for any want of culture, but, on the contrary, in order to better know his books:

“我告诉你，这几乎是太多了！但当他看到我如此震惊时，他解释了自己。‘优秀图书管理员的秘诀是，除了标题和目录，他不会阅读他负责的文献以外的任何内容。任何放任自己开始读书的人都会迷失自己作为图书管理员的定位，’他解释道。‘他注定会失去洞察力。’

“It was almost too much, I tell you! But when he saw how stunned I was, he explained himself. ‘The secret of a good librarian is that he never reads anything more of the literature in his charge than the titles and the table of contents. Anyone who lets himself go and starts reading a book is lost as a librarian,’ he explained. ‘He’s bound to lose perspective.’

“那么，”我喘着气说道，“你从来没有读过一本书吗？”

‘So,’ I said, trying to catch my breath, ‘you never read a single book?’

“从不。只看目录。”

‘Never. Only the catalogs.’

“但你不是博士吗？”

‘But aren’t you a Ph.D.?’

“当然是了。我在大学里教书，是图书馆学的特聘讲师。你知道，图书馆学是一门可以授予学位的专业，”他解释道。“将军，你认为有多少种系统可以用于书籍的整理和保存、书名的编目、纠正书名页上的印刷错误和错误信息等？” 5



‘Certainly I am. I teach at the university, as a special lecturer in Library Science. Library Science is a special field leading to a degree, you know,” he explained. “How many systems do you suppose there are, General, for the arrangement and preservation of books, cataloging of titles, correcting misprints and misinformation on title pages, and the like?’ ”5



因此，穆齐尔笔下的图书管理员不去接触他所管理的书籍，但他并不像人们想象的那样对这些书籍漠不关心或充满敌意。相反，正是他对书籍的热爱——对所有书籍的热爱——促使他谨慎地远离这些书籍，因为他担心对其中一本书的兴趣过浓会导致他忽视其他书籍。

Musil’s librarian thus keeps himself from entering into the books under his care, but he is far from indifferent or hostile toward them, as one might suppose. On the contrary, it is his love of books—of all books—that incites him to remain prudently on their periphery, for fear that too pronounced an interest in one of them might cause him to neglect the others.

在我看来，穆齐尔笔下的图书管理员的智慧就在于保持视角。事实上，他对图书馆的评价可能也适用于一般的文化素养：一味钻研书籍的人放弃了真正的修养，甚至放弃了阅读本身。因为考虑到现存的书籍数量，必然需要在整体观点和每本书之间做出选择，而所有的阅读都是在浪费精力，试图掌握整体是困难且耗时的。

To me, the wisdom of Musil’s librarian lies in this idea of maintaining perspective. What he says about libraries, indeed, is probably true of cultural literacy in general: he who pokes his nose into a book is abandoning true cultivation, and perhaps even reading itself. For there is necessarily a choice to be made, given the number of books in existence, between the overall view and each individual book, and all reading is a squandering of energy in the difficult and time-consuming attempt to master the whole.

这一立场的智慧首先在于它重视整体性，它建议，要想真正有文化，我们应该追求全面性，而不是积累孤立的知识。此外，对整体性的追求改变了我们看待每本书的方式，使我们能够超越其个性，关注其与其他书籍之间的关系。

The wisdom of this position lies first of all in the importance it accords to totality, in its suggestion that to be truly cultured, we should tend toward exhaustiveness rather than the accumulation of isolated bits of knowledge. Moreover, the search for totality changes how we look at each book, allowing us to move beyond its individuality to the relations it enjoys with others.

真正的读者应该努力把握这些关系，穆齐尔的图书管理员也深有体会。因此，与他的许多同事一样，他对书籍的兴趣远大于对有关书籍的书籍的兴趣：

These are the relations that a true reader should attempt to grasp, as Musil’s librarian well understands. As a result, like many of his colleagues, he is less interested in books than in books about books:

“我又说了一会儿，我需要一种时间表，这样我就能把各个方向的各种想法联系起来——这时，他变得非常有礼貌，这绝对是不礼貌的，他提出带我去目录室，让我自己搜索，尽管这是违反规定的，因为只有图书管理员才能使用。所以我真的发现自己进入了至圣所。感觉就像进入了一个巨大的大脑。想象一下，被那些书架完全包围，书架上摆满了书，到处都是梯子，所有的书架和图书馆桌子上都堆满了目录和书目，所有知识的集中地，你知道吗，没有一本有意义的书可读，只有关于书的书。” 6

“I went on a little longer about needing a kind of timetable that would enable me to make connections among all kinds of ideas in every direction—at which point he turns so polite it’s absolutely unholy, and offers to take me into the catalog room and let me do my own searching, even though it’s against the rules, because it’s only for the use of the librarians. So I actually found myself inside the holy of holies. It felt like being inside an enormous brain. Imagine being totally surrounded by those shelves, full of books in their compartments, ladders all over the place, all those book stands and library tables piled high with catalogs and bibliographies, the concentrate of all knowledge, don’t you know, and not one sensible book to read, only books about books.”6

有教养的人应该关注的重点其实是这些联系和关联，而不是某一本书，就像铁路扳道工应该关注火车之间的关系——即火车的交叉和换乘——而不是任何特定车队的内容。穆齐尔的大脑形象有力地强调了这一理论，即思想之间的关系远比思想本身重要。

Rather than any particular book, it is indeed these connections and correlations that should be the focus of the cultivated individual, much as a railroad switchman should focus on the relations between trains—that is, their crossings and transfers—rather than the contents of any specific convoy. And Musil’s image of the brain powerfully underscores this theory that relations among ideas are far more important than the ideas themselves.

您可能会对图书管理员声称不读书的说法提出异议，因为他对有关书籍的书籍（称为目录）非常感兴趣。但这些书籍具有相当特殊的地位，实际上只不过是清单。它们也是书籍之间关系的视觉表现——对于任何真正关心书籍、热爱书籍并希望一次掌握所有书籍的人来说，这些关系都应该引起浓厚的兴趣。

You could quibble with the librarian’s claim not to read any books, since he takes a close interest in the books about books known as catalogs. But these have a rather particular status and in fact amount to no more than lists. They are also a visual manifestation of the relations among books—relations that should be of keen interest to anyone who truly cares about books, who loves them enough to want to master all of them at once.

视角这一概念在图书馆员的推理中占据着核心地位，在实践层面上对我们也有相当大的影响。正是对这一概念的直觉把握，让某些享有特权的人能够毫发无损地摆脱那些否则会被指责为文化缺陷的情况。

The idea of perspective so central to the librarian’s reasoning has considerable bearing for us on the practical level. It is an intuitive grasp of this same concept that allows certain privileged individuals to escape unharmed from situations in which they might otherwise be accused of being flagrantly culturally deficient.

有教养的人知道（不幸的是，没有教养的人不知道），文化首先是一种取向问题。有教养不在于读过哪本书，而在于能否在书本中找到自己的方向，这需要你知道它们构成一个系统，并能够将每个元素与其他元素联系起来。书本的内部不如其外部重要，或者，如果你愿意的话，书本的内部就是其外部，因为一本书中重要的是与它一起的书。

As cultivated people know (and, to their misfortune, uncultivated people do not), culture is above all a matter of orientation. Being cultivated is a matter not of having read any book in particular, but of being able to find your bearings within books as a system, which requires you to know that they form a system and to be able to locate each element in relation to the others. The interior of the book is less important than its exterior, or, if you prefer, the interior of the book is its exterior, since what counts in a book is the books alongside it.

因此，一个有文化的人是否读过一本书并不重要，因为尽管他不确切知道这本书的内容，但他可能知道它的位置，或者换句话说，它与其他书籍的关系。一本书的内容和它的位置之间的区别是根本性的，因为正是这一点让那些不受文化影响的人能够毫无困难地谈论任何话题。

It is, then, hardly important if a cultivated person hasn’t read a given book, for though he has no exact knowledge of its content, he may still know its location, or in other words how it is situated in relation to other books. This distinction between the content of a book and its location is fundamental, for it is this that allows those unintimidated by culture to speak without trouble on any subject.

比如，我从未“读过”乔伊斯的《尤利西斯》，7而且很可能我永远也不会读。因此，这本书的“内容”对我来说基本上是陌生的——是它的内容，而不是它的位置。当然，一本书的内容很大程度上就是它的位置。这意味着当谈话中提到《尤利西斯》时，我会感到非常舒服，因为我可以相对准确地将它与其他书籍进行比较。例如，我知道这是《奥德赛》的复述，8它的叙述采取了意识流的形式，它的情节发生在都柏林的一天之中，等等。因此，我经常发现自己毫无顾忌地提到乔伊斯。

For instance, I’ve never “read” Joyce’s Ulysses,7 and it’s quite plausible that I never will. The “content” of the book is thus largely foreign to me—its content, but not its location. Of course, the content of a book is in large part its location. This means that I feel perfectly comfortable when Ulysses comes up in conversation, because I can situate it with relative precision in relation to other books. I know, for example, that it is a retelling of the Odyssey,8 that its narration takes the form of a stream of consciousness, that its action unfolds in Dublin in the course of a single day, etc. And as a result, I often find myself alluding to Joyce without the slightest anxiety.

更妙的是，正如我们在分析阅读话题背后的权力关系时所看到的，我可以毫无羞愧地提到我没有读过乔伊斯的作品。我的知识图书馆和所有图书馆一样，都是由空白和空白组成的，但实际上这并不是什么大问题：它藏书丰富，任何特定的空白几乎都看不见。

Even better, as we shall see in analyzing the power relations behind how we talk about reading, I am able to allude to my non-reading of Joyce without any shame. My intellectual library, like every library, is composed of gaps and blanks, but in reality this presents no real problem: it is sufficiently well stocked for any particular lacuna to be all but invisible.

尽管表面上如此，但关于一本书的大多数论述并不是关于这本书本身，而是关于我们文化当时所依赖的更大的一套书籍。真正重要的是这套书籍，我以后将称之为集体图书馆，因为在所有关于书籍的讨论中，我们对这个集体图书馆的掌握至关重要。但这种掌握是对关系的掌握，而不是对任何一本孤立的书籍的掌握，它很容易容纳对整体很大一部分的无知。

Most statements about a book are not about the book itself, despite appearances, but about the larger set of books on which our culture depends at that moment. It is that set, which I shall henceforth refer to as the collective library, that truly matters, since it is our mastery of this collective library that is at stake in all discussions about books. But this mastery is a command of relations, not of any book in isolation, and it easily accommodates ignorance of a large part of the whole.

因此，可以说，一本书一旦进入我们的感知领域，就不再是未知的，几乎对它一无所知也不应该成为想象或讨论它的障碍。对于一个有教养或好奇心的人来说，即使只是瞥一眼书名或封面，也会唤起一系列图像和印象，这些图像和印象会迅速凝聚成初步的看法，而整个文化所代表的整套书籍会促成这种看法。因此，对于不读书的人来说，即使是与一本书最短暂的接触也可能是真正个人化的开始，我们遇到的任何一本不知名的书都会在那一瞬间成为一本知名的书。

It can be argued, then, that a book stops being unknown as soon as it enters our perceptual field, and that to know almost nothing about it should be no obstacle to imagining or discussing it. To a cultivated or curious person, even the slightest glance at a book’s title or cover calls up a series of images and impressions quick to coalesce into an initial opinion, facilitated by the whole set of books represented in the culture at large. For the non-reader, therefore, even the most fleeting encounter with a book may be the beginning of an authentic personal appropriation, and any unknown book we come across becomes a known book in that instant.

穆齐尔笔下的图书管理员的不读书行为与众不同之处在于，他的态度不是被动的，而是主动的。如果许多有教养的人不读书，相反，如果许多不读书的人有教养，那是因为不读书不仅仅是没有读书。它是一种真正的活动，它包括采取一种立场来面对保护你免于被淹没的浩瀚书海。基于这一点，它值得捍卫，甚至值得传授。

What distinguishes the non-reading of Musil’s librarian is that his attitude is not passive, but active. If many cultivated individuals are non-readers, and if, conversely, many nonreaders are cultivated individuals, it is because non-reading is not just the absence of reading. It is a genuine activity, one that consists of adopting a stance in relation to the immense tide of books that protects you from drowning. On that basis, it deserves to be defended and even taught.

当然，在外行人看来，有时不读书与不读书几乎无法区分；我承认，一个人不读书和另一个人不读书最相似。但如果我们观察这两个人面对一本书时的情况，他们的行为差异及其潜在动机就会一目了然。

To the unpracticed eye, of course, the absence of reading may be almost indistinguishable at times from non-reading; I will concede that nothing more closely resembles one person not reading than a second person not reading either. But if we watch as these two people are confronted with a book, the difference in their behavior and its underlying motivation will be readily apparent.

在第一种情况下，不读书的人对书不感兴趣，但这里的书既指内容，又指位置。对他来说，书与其他书的关系和书的主题一样无关紧要，他一点也不担心，对一本书感兴趣会让人觉得他鄙视其他书。

In the first case, the person not reading is not interested in the book, but book is understood here both as content and location. The book’s relationship to others is as much a matter of indifference to him as its subject, and he is not in the least concerned that in taking an interest in one book, he might seem to disdain the rest.

在第二种情况下，不读书的人会像穆齐尔的图书管理员一样放弃读书，以便掌握书的精髓，了解书与整个图书馆的契合之处。这样做，他绝不会对书不感兴趣——恰恰相反。正是因为他了解内容和位置之间的联系，他才选择不读书，他的智慧比许多读者更高明，也许经过深思熟虑，他对书本身的尊重也更高。



In the second case, the person not reading abstains, like Musil’s librarian, in order to grasp the essence of the book, which is how it fits into the library as a whole. In so doing, he is hardly uninterested in the book—to the contrary. It is because he understands the link between content and location that he chooses not to read, with a wisdom superior to that of many readers, and perhaps, on reflection, with greater respect for the book itself.

你读过的书籍

II

Books You Have Skimmed

（我们和瓦莱里一样，都认为只要浏览过一本书就足以写一篇文章，而对于某些书，不这样做甚至可能是不合适的）

(in which we see, along with Valéry, that it is enough to have skimmed a book to be able to write an article about it, and that with certain books it might even be inappropriate to do otherwise)

整体视角的概念不仅仅适用于将一本书放在集体图书馆中；它同样适用于将每一段书放在一本书中。有修养的读者会发现，他所培养的图书馆定位技能在一本书中同样有效。文化素养意味着能够快速地了解一本书，这并不需要读完整本书——事实上恰恰相反。人们甚至可以说，你在这方面的能力越强，就越不需要读任何一本书。

THE IDEA OF OVERALL PERSPECTIVE has implications for more than just situating a book within the collective library; it is equally relevant to the task of situating each passage within a book. The cultivated reader will find that the orientation skills he has developed with regard to the library function just as well within a single volume. Being culturally literate means being able to get your bearings quickly in a book, which does not require reading the book in its entirety—quite the opposite, in fact. One might even argue that the greater your abilities in this area, the less will it be necessary to read any book in particular.

《没有个性的人》中图书管理员的态度代表了少数人所持的极端立场，即使是那些反对阅读的人，因为最终选择从不阅读是相当困难的。更常见的情况是，读者并不完全避开书籍，但满足于浏览它们。此外，英雄图书管理员的行为在这方面有些模棱两可，因为尽管他小心翼翼地不打开任何书籍，但他仍然对书名和目录感兴趣，因此无论他是否愿意，都会对作品产生印象。

The attitude of the librarian in The Man Without Qualities represents an extreme position held by few people, even among those opposed to reading, for in the end it is quite difficult to choose never to read at all. More common is the case of the reader who does not shun books entirely, but is content to skim them. The behavior of the heroic librarian is somewhat ambiguous in this regard, moreover, since although he is careful not to open any books, he is still interested in their titles and tables of contents, and so develops an impression of the work whether he means to or not.

略读书籍而不真正阅读它们，丝毫不会妨碍你对它们进行评论。这甚至可能是吸收书籍的最有效方式，既尊重其内在的深度和丰富性，又不会迷失在细节中。无论如何，这就是不读书的大师保罗·瓦莱里的观点和公开的做法。

Skimming books without actually reading them does not in any way prevent you from commenting on them. It’s even possible that this is the most efficient way to absorb books, respecting their inherent depth and richness without getting lost in the details. Such, in any case, was the opinion—and the declared practice—of that master of non-reading Paul Valéry.

在那些警告过阅读风险的作家中，瓦莱里占据着重要的地位，他曾用一部分作品谴责这种危险的行为。特斯特先生是瓦莱里笔下典型的主人公，他住在一间没有书的公寓里。在这方面，他（和许多其他人一样）很可能是以这位作家为原型的，这位作家毫不掩饰自己读书不多：“起初，我厌恶阅读，甚至把我最喜欢的书分给我的朋友。在经历了严重的阅读阶段之后，我不得不买回几本。但我不怎么读书，因为我在作品中寻找的是能够促进或阻碍我自己活动的东西。” 1

In the gallery of writers who have warned of the risks of reading, Valéry occupies a significant place, having devoted a portion of his work to denouncing this dangerous activity. Monsieur Teste, the Valéryan hero par excellence, lives in an apartment empty of books. Quite plausibly he is modeled in this regard (as in many others) on the writer, who makes no secret of the fact that he does not read much: “Initially, I took an aversion to reading and even divided up among my friends the books I liked best. I was obliged to buy several of them back later on, after the acute phase. But I am not much of a reader, since what I look for in a work is what will enable or impede an aspect of my own activity.”1

这种对书籍的不信任首先是针对传记的。瓦莱里通过质疑将作品与作者紧密联系在一起的普遍做法，在文学批评界获得了一定的声誉。十九世纪的批评传统是坚持认为对作者的了解可以提高对作品的了解，因此要尽可能多地收集有关作者的信息。

This mistrust of books was directed first and foremost against biography. Valéry achieved a certain fame in the world of literary criticism by calling into question the common practice of linking a work closely to its author. It was conventional in nineteenth-century criticism to maintain that knowledge of the author enhanced that of the work, and thus to amass as much information about him as possible.

瓦莱里打破了这一批评传统，认为尽管表面上如此，但作者无法解释自己的作品。作品是创作过程的产物，这一过程发生在作家身上，但超越了他自己，将作品简化为创作行为是不公平的。因此，要理解文本，收集有关作者的信息毫无意义，因为归根结底，作者只是文本的一个临时庇护所。

Breaking with that critical tradition, Valéry posited that despite appearances, an author is in no position to explain his own work. The work is the product of a creative process that occurs in the writer but transcends him, and it is unfair to reduce the work to that act of creation. To understand a text, therefore, there is little point in gathering information about the author, since in the final analysis he serves it only as a temporary shelter.

瓦莱里远非他那个时代唯一一位主张将作品与作者分开的作家。在他死后出版的著作《反圣伯夫》2中，普鲁斯特提出了这样的理论：文学作品是不同于我们所知的人的自我的产物；在《追忆似水年华》 3中，他通过贝戈特这个人物阐述了这一理论。但瓦莱里并不满足于将作者从文学批评领域中剔除；为了利用自己的优势，他还试图将作者从文本中剔除。

Valéry was far from the only writer of his era to advocate a separation between the work and its author. In his posthumously published book Against Sainte-Beuve,2 Proust advanced the theory that a literary work is the product of a different self from the person we know; in A la recherche de temps perdu,3 he illustrated this theory through the character of Bergotte. But Valéry was not satisfied with eliminating the author from the domain of literary criticism; pressing his advantage, he sought to drive him out of the text as well.

尽管瓦莱里读书不多，但这并不妨碍他对自己知之甚少的作家形成准确的见解，并对这些作家进行详细的讨论。

Though Valéry did not read much, this did not prevent him from having precise opinions on the authors about whom he knew so little, and discussing these authors at length.

和大多数谈论普鲁斯特的人一样，瓦莱里从未读过普鲁斯特的作品。但与大多数人不同，他对此并不感到困扰，在普鲁斯特去世后不久的 1923 年 1 月《新法兰西评论》上，他以平静的玩世不恭态度开始了对普鲁斯特的致敬，他写道：

Like most people who talk about Proust, Valéry had never read him. But unlike most, he was unfazed by this fact, and with serene cynicism he began his tribute to Proust in the January 1923 issue of the Nouvelle Revue Française, shortly after the writer’s death, with these words:

尽管我几乎没读过马塞尔·普鲁斯特的巨作，尽管小说家的艺术本身就是一门我难以想象的艺术，但从我抽出时间阅读的那几本《追忆似水年华》中，我清楚地意识到，文学刚刚遭受了多么沉重的损失；而且损失的不仅仅是文学，还有那个由每个时代赋予时代真正价值的人组成的秘密社团。4

Although I have scarcely read a single volume of Marcel Proust’s great work, and although the very art of the novelist is an art that I find inconceivable, I am nevertheless well aware, from the little of the Recherche du temps perdu that I have found time to read, what an exceptionally heavy loss literature has just suffered; and not only literature but still more that secret society composed of those who in every age give the age its real value.4

随着介绍的继续，他的无耻丝毫没有减弱的迹象，为了证明他对所讨论的作者缺乏了解，他只能求助于安德烈·纪德和莱昂·都德的正面评价（更重要的是，趋同的评价）：

His shamelessness shows no signs of abating as the introduction continues, for in justifying his lack of knowledge of the author he is discussing, he is reduced to taking refuge in the favorable (and, more important, convergent) assessments of André Gide and Léon Daudet:

无论如何，即使我从未读过普鲁斯特的巨作，但两个像纪德和莱昂·都德这样思想迥异的人都同意其重要性，这一事实本身就足以消除任何疑虑；这种意外的一致意见只有在几乎确定的情况下才会出现。我们可以放心；如果他们同时宣布这一事实，那一定是阳光普照。5

In any case, even if I had never read a line of Proust’s vast work, the mere fact that two people with minds as different as Gide and Léon Daudet were agreed about its importance would have been sufficient to allay any doubts; such unexpected agreement could only occur in the case of a virtual certainty. We can be easy in our minds; the sun must be shining if they both proclaim the fact at the same time.5

因此，其他人的观点是形成自己观点的必要前提。事实上，你甚至可以完全依赖他们，甚至可能不需要阅读文本的任何一行——有人认为瓦莱里就是这种情况。这种盲目依赖其他读者的问题在于，正如瓦莱里承认的那样，很难对文本做出任何具体的评论：

Other people’s views are thus an essential prerequisite to forming an opinion of your own. In fact, you might even be able to rely on them entirely, to the point—one assumes that such was the case for Valéry—that it might be unnecessary to read a single line of the text. The trouble with this blind reliance on other readers is, as Valéry acknowledges, that it is then hard to comment on the text with any specificity:

其他人会以权威和洞察力谈论普鲁斯特作品的力量和微妙之处。还有一些人会告诉我们，是什么样的人构思了这部作品，并把它带到了辉煌的结局；我自己只是在很多年前瞥见了他。因此，我只能提出一个没有分量、几乎不值得记录的观点。让它成为一种致敬，成为一座将永存的坟墓上一朵凋谢的花。6

Others will speak with authority and penetration of the power and subtlety of Proust’s work. Still others will tell us what manner of man it was who conceived the work and brought it to a glorious conclusion; I myself merely caught a glimpse of him many years ago. I can therefore only put forward a view without weight and barely worth recording. Let it be no more than a tribute, a fading flower on a tomb that will endure.6

如果我们可以相信瓦莱里的真诚并且能够忽略他的愤世嫉俗，我们很可能会承认，下面关于普鲁斯特的几页并非毫无道理，证明了一些我们将会一次又一次观察到的东西：为了准确地谈论它，根本不需要熟悉你正在谈论的内容。

If we can credit Valéry for his sincerity and manage to look past his cynicism, we are likely to concede that the several pages on Proust that follow are not without truth, demonstrating something we will have occasion to observe again and again: it is not at all necessary to be familiar with what you’re talking about in order to talk about it accurately.

介绍之后，瓦莱里的文章分为两部分。第一部分主要讨论小说，在这里，我们可以感觉到作者并不急于提出任何具体的观点。由此我们得知，小说的目的是“向我们传达一个或几个想象中的‘生活’，小说以人物的形式设定这些生活，这些生活的时间和地点是确定的，他们的冒险经历是规划好的”——这一特点使小说有别于诗歌，并允许对其进行总结和翻译，而不会造成太大的损失。这些评论在许多小说中都是正确的，但实际上几乎不适用于普鲁斯特，因为他的作品很难总结。但瓦莱里在文章的第二部分表现出了更大的灵感。

After the introduction, Valéry’s article is divided into two sections. The first deals with the novel in general, and here one can sense that the author is in no rush to offer any specific observations. We thus learn that the novel is intent on “conveying to us one or several imaginary ‘lives,’ which it institutes as characters, whose time and place are determined, whose adventures are formulated”—a characteristic that distinguishes it from poetry and allows it to be summarized and translated without great loss. These remarks, true enough in the case of many novels, are in fact hardly applicable to Proust, whose work is hard to summarize. But Valéry shows greater inspiration in the second part of his text.

本节专门讨论普鲁斯特，很难完全避免提到他。瓦莱里在更广泛的写作趋势的背景下提到了他（“普鲁斯特将如此松散和简单的结构变成了最非凡的叙述”），然后根据明显的普鲁斯特观点，梳理出作者的特殊性，即他的作品探索了“最小的形象在作者的本质中唤起的过多的回响”。7 专注于普鲁斯特利用形象的无限联想的习惯有两个好处。首先，你不需要读过普鲁斯特的作品就能意识到这一点；你只需打开他的作品的任何一页就能观察到这种技巧的作用。其次，这是一个战略选择，因为它证明了瓦莱里自己的方法是正确的，因为普鲁斯特从最小的细节中得出联想的习惯似乎鼓励评论家对普鲁斯特的作品也这样做，而不是真正阅读它。

This section is devoted to Proust, whom it is difficult to avoid mentioning entirely. Valéry brings him up in the context of a broader trend in writing (“Proust turned such a loose and simple structure to the most extraordinary account”), but then teases out the author’s specificity, based on the manifestly Proustian notion that his work explores the “overabundance of echoes that the least image awakened in the author’s very substance.”7 There are two advantages to concentrating on the Proustian habit of playing on an image’s infinite associations. First of all, you don’t need to have read Proust to be aware of it; you need merely open his work to any page to observe this technique in action. Second, it is a strategic choice in that it justifies Valéry’s own approach, since Proust’s habit of drawing associations from the smallest detail might seem to encourage a critic to do likewise with Proust’s work, as opposed to actually reading it.

瓦莱里敏锐地解释说，普鲁斯特作品的价值在于它非凡的可随意翻开任意一页的能力：

Shrewdly, Valéry explains that the value of Proust’s work lies in its remarkable ability to be opened at random to any page:

他作品的趣味在于每一个片段。我们可以随心所欲地打开这本书；它的生命力并不取决于之前发生的事情，也不取决于某种后天获得的幻觉；它取决于文本组织本身的活性属性。8

The interest of his work lies in each fragment. We can open the book wherever we choose; its vitality does not depend on what went before, on a sort of acquired illusion; it depends on what might be called the active properties of the very tissue of the text.8

瓦莱里的天才之举在于，他不读书的做法实际上是作者的必然选择，不读普鲁斯特的作品就是他能给予普鲁斯特的最大赞美。因此，当他在文章的结尾（向那些很快就会无人理解的“难懂的作者”致敬）时，他几乎毫不掩饰地表示，在完成了批评任务后，他比以往任何时候都更不想读普鲁斯特的作品。

Valéry’s stroke of genius lies in showing that his method of non-reading is actually necessitated by the author, and that abstaining from reading Proust’s work is the greatest compliment he can give him. Thus, as he concludes his article (with a tribute to “difficult authors” who will soon be understood by no one), he barely conceals that, having accomplished his critical task, he has no more intention of reading Proust than ever.

如果说对普鲁斯特的致敬让瓦莱里得以阐述自己的阅读观念，那么，普鲁斯特的主要同时代人之一阿纳托尔·法朗士则为瓦莱里提供了借口，让他展示自己作为批评家的全部才能，而这种批评既不依赖于作者也不依赖于文本。

If his tribute to Proust allowed Valéry to illustrate his conception of reading, it was one of Proust’s major contemporaries, Anatole France, who gave Valéry the pretext to show his full powers as a critic depended neither on author nor text.

1925年，法兰西学院邀请瓦莱里填补阿纳托尔·法朗士留下的空缺，因此，瓦莱里不得不对他致以崇高的敬意。瓦莱里极力避免履行他在致辞开头为自己列出的责任：

In 1925, the Académie Française invited Valéry to fill the chair left vacant by Anatole France, and in the way of things, Valéry was therefore forced to eulogize him. Valéry diligently avoided following the responsibility he outlined for himself in the opening of his address:

死者只有最后一个选择：生者。我们的思想是他们获得光明的唯一途径。他们教会了我们很多东西，他们似乎为了我们而屈服，放弃了他们的优势，他们理应被虔诚地召唤到我们的记忆中，并被邀请通过我们的话语畅饮生命之水。9

The dead have but one last resort: the living. Our thoughts are their only access to the light of day. They who have taught us so much, who seem to have bowed out for our sake and forfeited to us their advantages, ought by all rights to be reverently summoned to our memories and invited to drink a draught of life through our words.9

如果阿纳托尔·法朗士希望活在别人的心中，他最好找一些其他的颂扬者，而不是瓦莱里。瓦莱里在演讲中用尽了所有的才智，以便不向法国致敬。他的演讲是对他前任的无休止的背信弃义的讽刺，几乎毫不掩饰地是赞美：

If he had hoped to live on in the thoughts of others, Anatole France would have done well to find some other eulogizer than Valéry, who employs all of his ingenuity in the oration so as not to pay tribute to France. His speech is an endless series of perfidious jabs at his predecessor, barely disguised as compliments:

公众对我杰出的前任给予了他们沙漠中的水源，感激不尽。与各方发展的高度复杂和爆炸性的风格相比，他写作的节奏感却令人感到惊喜。流畅、清晰和简单，普通人的守护神，仿佛又回到了人间。那些喜欢那种不需要太多思考就能给他们带来乐趣的写作的人立刻就喜欢上了他的作品，他的魅力在于它完全不做作的外观，它的清澈有时让人思考得更深，但没有什么神秘之处：然而，他的作品仍然非常可读，即使不是完全令人放心。他完美地掌握了轻描淡写最严肃的想法和问题的艺术。他的书中没有任何东西会给人带来丝毫困难，除非奇迹本身就是没有遇到困难。10

The public could not thank my illustrious predecessor enough for giving them water in the desert. By contrast with the highly complex and explosive styles being developed on all sides, the measured cadences of his writing proved mildly and agreeably surprising. It was as though fluency, clarity, and simplicity, the patron goddesses of the average man, had returned to earth. Those who prefer the sort of writing that gives them pleasure without requiring much thought took an immediate fancy to his work, whose seductive charm lay in its totally unaffected appearance, whose limpidity sometimes allowed a deeper thought, but nothing to mystify: his work remains, however, unfailingly readable, if not wholly reassuring. He perfected the art of brushing lightly over the most serious ideas and problems. Nothing in his book gives the least difficulty unless it be the wonder itself of encountering none.10

很难想象在这么少的几行文字中，会有如此密集的有害暗示。弗朗斯的作品被连续描述为“温和”、“令人愉快”、“令人耳目一新”、“有分寸”和“简单”，这些词在文学批评中通常不被视为赞美。更重要的是，弗朗斯的作品很容易取悦所有人，这也是最关键的一点。人们可以不假思索地品味它，因为思想只是被“一带而过”——瓦莱里补充道：

It is hard to imagine a denser assemblage of injurious implications in so few lines. France’s work is successively characterized as “gentle,” “agreeable,” “refreshing,” “measured,” and “simple,” terms that in literary criticism do not generally pass for compliments. What is more, and this is the kicker, France’s work is apt to please everyone. It can be savored mindlessly, since ideas are only “brushed over”—an evaluation to which Valéry adds:

这种明晰感创造了一种令人愉悦的幻觉，让我们觉得我们可以轻松地丰富自己，毫无痛苦地获得快乐，毫不费力地理解，享受一场免费的表演，还有什么比这种幻觉更珍贵呢？

What could be more precious than the delectable illusion, created by such clarity, that we are enriching ourselves with ease, deriving pleasure without pain, comprehending without giving our attention, enjoying a free show?

那些为我们解除思想负担、巧妙地为事物的复杂性编织出明亮面纱的作家是值得祝福的。11



Blessed are those writers who relieve us of the burden of thought, and who dexterously weave a luminous veil over the complexity of things.11



如果瓦莱里对法国的赞美是一场旷日持久的恶语，那么它最残酷的成就可能就是含糊其辞；瓦莱里似乎想传达的是，阅读阿纳托尔·法朗士的作品会背叛他的低评价。不仅没有提到书名，而且他的演讲中甚至没有提到过任何一部法国作品。

If Valéry’s tribute to France is a protracted exercise in nastiness, its most brutal achievement may be its vagueness; it is as though Valéry wished to convey that to read Anatole France’s work at all would be a betrayal of his low opinion. Not only are no titles mentioned, but his speech is unblemished by even a single allusion to any of France’s works.

更糟糕的是，瓦莱里非常小心，从不提及他准备占据的座位的人的名字，而是通过迂回曲折或以名字戏谑的方式指认他：“只有在法国，他才有可能出现，甚至可以被想象，因为他采用了法国的名字。” 12

Worse yet, Valéry is careful never to mention the name of the individual whose chair he is preparing to occupy, designating him through circumlocution or allusively by way of a play on his name: “He himself could have been possible and even conceivable only in France, whose name he adopted as his own.”12

瓦莱里拒绝给人留下他读过阿纳托尔·法朗士的印象，这或许也是他指责这位同行的最大错误：他读得太多了。瓦莱里将法朗士描述为一位“无限的读者”——这话出自瓦莱里之口，听起来像是一种侮辱——与他在学院的继任者相反，法朗士倾向于沉迷于书籍：

Valéry’s refusal to give the impression that he has read Anatole France may also be a function of the greatest fault he imputes to his fellow author: that he read too much. He characterizes France as an “infinite reader”—which, coming from Valéry, sounds like an insult—who, in opposition to his successor in the Académie, was inclined to lose himself among books:

先生们，我必须说，光是想到世界各地堆积如山的大量印刷品就足以动摇最坚强的心。没有什么比浏览一座巨大图书馆的镀金墙壁更能让人心烦意乱和失去平衡了，没有什么景象比那些书堆、那些沿着码头升起的知识产物的护墙、数以百万计的书籍和小册子像垃圾一样沉没在塞纳河岸边，被时间的洪流抛弃在那里，从而净化了我们的思想，更让人心痛。13

I must say, gentlemen, that the mere thought of all those immense stacks of printed pages mounting throughout the world is enough to shake the stoutest heart. There is nothing more likely to confuse and unbalance the mind than scanning the gilt-lined walls of a huge library, no sight could be more painful to the mind than those shoals of volumes, those parapets of intellectual produce that rise along the quais, the millions of tomes and pamphlets foundered on the bank of the Seine like waste, abandoned there by the stream of time thus purging itself of our thoughts.13

他暗示，过度阅读剥夺了法国的原创性。事实上，在瓦莱里看来，阅读对作家来说最大的风险就是让他屈从于他人：



This excessive reading, he implies, stripped France of originality. Indeed, in Valéry’s eyes, such is the principal risk of reading to the writer—that of subordinating him to others:



先生们，您那位博学而敏锐的同事，面对庞大的数字，并没有感到这种不安。他头脑更清醒。与那些容易晕头转向、厌恶统计数字的人不同，他不需要采取读书量极少的预防措施。他非但没有感到压抑，反而被这些财富所激励，自由地利用这些财富来指导和维持自己的艺术，并取得了令人满意的结果。

Your learned and subtle colleague, gentlemen, did not feel this unease in the face of great numbers. He had a stronger head. Unlike those who are subject to statistical vertigo and revulsion, he did not need to take the precaution of reading very little. Far from being oppressed, he was stimulated by all this wealth, freely drawing upon it to direct and sustain his own art, with happy results.

不止一位评论家严厉而天真地批评他，说他知识渊博，却对自己所知道的东西毫不知情。他应该做什么？他做了什么以前没有做过的事？没有什么比作家必须做到的绝对新颖的标准更新颖了。14

More than one critic has taken him to task rather harshly, and naïvely, for being so knowledgeable and for not being unaware of what he knew. What was he supposed to do? What did he do that had not always been done? Nothing is newer than the standard of absolute newness imposed as an obligation on writers.14

这段话的关键是与弗朗斯的做法截然相反的条件，即“不知道自己知道什么”。文化素养本身就存在消失在别人的书中的风险，如果我们要创作自己的作品，就必须摆脱这种风险。弗朗斯从未开辟出自己的道路，他完美地体现了阅读可能造成的危害；因此，瓦莱里不仅小心翼翼地从不引用或提及他的作品，甚至从不提及他的名字，这不足为奇，仿佛单凭这一点就会诅咒瓦莱里同样贬低自我。

Key to this passage is the condition, so antithetical to France’s way of proceeding, of “being unaware of what you know.” With cultural literacy comes the inherent threat of vanishing in other people’s books, a threat it is vital to escape if we are to create any work of our own. France, who never managed to blaze a path of his own, perfectly epitomizes the damage that stands to be done by reading; small wonder, then, that Valéry is careful not only never to quote or evoke his work, but never even to say his name, as though this alone might curse Valéry with a similar diminution of self.

这些对普鲁斯特和阿纳托尔·法朗士的“赞美”的问题在于，它们实际上使瓦莱里关于作家的所有其他作品都令人怀疑，迫使我们质疑他是否读过他们的作品，或者只是粗略地浏览过。一旦瓦莱里承认他几乎不读书，却毫不犹豫地提出自己的意见，即使是他最无害的批评声明也会变得可疑。

The problem with these “tributes” to Proust and Anatole France is that in effect they cast doubt on all of Valéry’s other writing about writers, forcing us to question whether he has read their work or barely skimmed it. Once Valéry acknowledges that he hardly reads at all and yet doesn’t hesitate to offer his opinion, even his most innocuous critical declarations become suspect.

他对本世纪上半叶法国文学界第三大人物亨利·柏格森的赞美，几乎不能让我们安心。这篇题为《论柏格森》的文章摘自 1941 年 1 月在法兰西学院为纪念这位哲学家去世而发表的演讲。它以对柏格森之死和葬礼的回忆开始，这颇为传统，然后开始列举他的品质，用最呆板的术语来描述：

The tribute he offers to the third great name of French letters in the first half of the century, Henri Bergson, is hardly calculated to set our minds at ease. This text, entitled “A Discourse on Bergson,” is drawn from a lecture delivered at the Académie Française in January 1941, on the occasion of the philosopher’s death. It begins, rather traditionally, with an evocation of Bergson’s death and funeral, before launching into a list of his qualities, described in the most wooden terms imaginable:

他是我们学会的骄傲。无论我们是否被他的形而上学所吸引，无论我们是否跟随他一生致力于的深刻研究，以及他思想的真正创造性发展，他的思想变得越来越大胆和独立，我们都在他身上看到了最高智商美德的最真实典范。15

He was the pride of our Society. Whether or not we were attracted by his metaphysics, whether or not we had followed him in the profound researches to which he devoted the whole of his life, and in the truly creative evolution of his thought, which became steadily bolder and more independent, we possessed in him the most authentic example of the highest intellectual virtues.15

经过这样的介绍，人们会期望这些赞美会得到一些解释，而且——为什么不呢？——瓦莱里可能会阐明他与柏格森的观点之间的联系。但这种幻想很快就会消失，因为下面这段话开头的公式通常是用来评论那些尚未阅读的文本的：

One would expect, after such an introduction, that these compliments might receive a bit of justification, and—why not?—that Valéry might specify his positions in relation to those of Bergson. But this illusion is swift to evaporate, for the formula that begins the following paragraph is one customarily reserved for commentaries on texts that have not been read:

我不打算讨论他的哲学。现在不是进行研究的时候，因为研究需要深入，只有在更光明的日子里，通过充分和不受约束的思考才能进行。16

I do not propose to discuss his philosophy. This is not the moment to undertake an examination which would need to be searching and which could only be so if it were done in the light of brighter days and by means of the full and unfettered exercise of thought.16

就瓦莱里而言，我们完全可以担心，他拒绝考察柏格森的哲学，这不仅是象征意义上的，也是字面意义上的。文章的其余部分远不能让人放心：

We may well fear, in the case of Valéry, that his refusal to examine Bergson’s philosophy is not just figurative but literal. The remainder of the text is far from reassuring:

柏格森先生所研究的那些非常古老且因此而非常困难的问题，即时间、记忆以及最重要的生命进化问题，通过他得到了一个新的开端，而五十年前在法国出现的哲学地位也发生了显著的变化。17

The very ancient and for that reason very difficult problems with which M. Bergson dealt, those of time, memory, and above all the evolution of life, were through him given a new beginning, and the position of philosophy as it appeared in France fifty years ago has undergone a remarkable change.17

说柏格森研究过时间和记忆——哪个哲学家没有研究过呢？——很难说这是对他作品原创性的描述，即使是简洁的描述。除了几行关于柏格森和康德对立的内容外，其余文本非常模糊，尽管它完美地描述了柏格森，但它同样适用于许多其他哲学家：

Saying that Bergson worked on time and memory—what philosopher has not?—can hardly be passed off as a description, even a succinct one, of his work in its originality. With the exception of a few lines on the opposition between Bergson and Kant, the rest of the text is so vague that, although it describes Bergson perfectly well, it could equally apply to many other philosophers:

柏格森是一位高尚、纯洁、卓越的思想家典范，也许是最后一批全身心、深刻、高尚地致力于思考的人之一。在这个时代，世界思考和沉思的次数越来越少，随着每一天的流逝，文明进一步沦为我们对其丰富多彩的财富和自由丰富的智力成果的记忆和遗迹，而贫穷、苦难和各种限制阻碍和压抑了一切智力活动。柏格森似乎已经属于过去的时代，他的名字是欧洲思想史上最后一个伟大的名字。18

A very lofty, very pure and superior exemplar of the thinking man, and perhaps one of the last men who will have devoted himself exclusively, profoundly, and nobly to thinking, in a period when the world thinks and meditates less and less, when, with each day that passes, civilization is further reduced to the memories and vestiges we keep of its multifarious riches and its free and abundant intellectual production, while poverty, suffering, and restrictions of every kind discourage and depress all intellectual enterprise, Bergson seems already to belong to a past age and his name to be the last great name in the history of the European mind.18

我们看到，瓦莱里无法抗拒以恶意的语调结束这本书，热情洋溢的短语“欧洲思想史上最后一个伟大的名字”只能勉强缓和之前那句话的严厉性，后者诚恳地将柏格森归入“过去的时代”。读到这些话，我们完全可以认识到瓦莱里对书籍的热爱，我们可能会担心，他选择强调这位哲学家在思想史中的过时地位，是为了省去阅读他任何一部作品的麻烦。

As we see, Valéry is unable to resist ending on a malevolent note, the warmhearted phrase “the last great name in the history of the European mind” mitigating only with difficulty the harshness of the one preceding it, which cordially consigns Bergson to “a past age.” Reading these words, in full recognition of Valéry’s passion for books, one may well worry that he chose to emphasize the philosopher’s outmoded position within the history of ideas in order to dispense with opening any of his works.

这种不参考作者或文本的批评做法绝不荒谬。在瓦莱里看来，它基于一种理性的文学观念，其主要观点之一是，不仅作者无用，作品本身也有点多余。

This practice of criticism without reference to author or text is in no way absurd. In Valéry’s case, it is based on a reasoned conception of literature, one of whose principal ideas is that not only is the author useless, but the work itself is really a bit gratuitous as well.

这部作品的尴尬首先可能与瓦莱里的整个文学观念有关，他将其称为亚里士多德等人的诗学。他最关心的是发展文学的普遍规律。因此，每篇文本的立场都变得模棱两可：它可以作为诗学阐述中的一个例子，但与此同时，它也可以被放在一边，以实现对整体的看法。

This embarrassment around the work may be related first of all to Valéry’s whole notion of literature, what he calls, following Aristotle and others, a poetics. More than anything, he is concerned with developing the general laws of literature. It follows that the position of each text becomes ambiguous: it can serve as an example within the elaboration of that poetics, to be sure, but at the same time it is also just what may be put aside to achieve a view of the whole.

因此，我们可以跟随威廉·马克思的观点，认为瓦莱里感兴趣的不是具体的作品，而是它的“理念”：

We may thus follow William Marx in noting that what interests Valéry is less a specific work than its “idea”:

正如学术批评力求积累尽可能多的文献，并赋予文学以外的资料（信件、私人文件等）以最重要的意义，瓦莱里式的批评力求将其对象限制到最大程度，以至于在其观察领域中，除了作品本身，它不再保留任何东西，甚至比作品更少的东西：作品的简单理念。19

Just as academic criticism sought to accumulate the greatest number of documents possible and accorded to extra-literary sources (correspondences, private papers, etc.) preeminent importance in its efforts, criticism in the mode of Valéry sought to limit its object to the maximum extent possible, to the point where it no longer retained in its field of observation anything but the work itself, or even less than the work: the simple idea of the work.19

根据这个模型，如果我们不太接近这个概念，我们就更有可能理解这个“不如作品”的想法，因为这样我们就会面临迷失于细节的风险。从极端的角度看，文本的有趣之处——不是作品本身，而是它与其他作品共有的品质——可能最好由评论家在作品面前闭上眼睛，思考它可能是什么来感知。基于这些理由，任何过于专注的阅读，甚至所有的阅读，都是我们对一本书最深刻理解的障碍。

According to this model, we have all a greater likelihood of grasping this idea, this “less than the work,” if we do not get too close to it, where we risk getting lost in its details. To take this theory to its extreme, what is interesting about a text—which is not the work itself, but the qualities it shares with others— might be best perceived by a critic who closes his eyes in the presence of the work and thinks, instead, about what it may be. On these grounds, any overly attentive reading, if not indeed all reading, is an obstacle to our deepest understanding of a book.

瓦莱里通过这种距离诗学为我们与书籍互动的最常见方式之一提供了合理的依据：略读。当我们手里拿着一本书时，我们很少会从头到尾读完它，即使我们能做到。大多数时候，我们对待书籍的方式就像瓦莱里建议对待普鲁斯特的方式一样：我们略读它们。

With this poetics of distance, Valéry offers rational grounds for one of our most common ways of interacting with books: skimming. When we have a book in our hands, it is rare that we read it from cover to cover, assuming such a feat is possible at all. Most of the time, we do with books what Valéry recommends doing with Proust: we skim them.

浏览或翻阅书籍的概念至少可以从两种不同的意义上来理解。在第一种情况下，浏览是线性的。读者从开头开始阅读，然后开始跳过行或页，无论成功与否，他都会读到结尾。在第二种情况下，浏览是迂回的：读者不是按顺序阅读，而是漫无目的地浏览作品，有时从结尾开始。第二种方法并不比第一种方法更能体现读者的恶意。它只是我们与书籍建立联系的习惯方式之一。

The notion of skimming or flipping through books can be understood in at least two different senses. In the first case, the skimming is linear. The reader begins the text at the beginning, then starts skipping lines or pages as, successfully or not, he makes his way toward the end. In the second case, the skimming is circuitous: rather than read in an orderly fashion, the reader takes a stroll through the work, sometimes beginning at the end. This second method implies no more ill will on the part of the reader than does the first. It simply constitutes one of our habitual ways of relating to books.

但这种发现模式的丰富性明显扰乱了阅读与不阅读之间的区别，甚至扰乱了阅读的概念。我们该把那些花了一定时间（甚至几个小时）阅读一本书却没有完全读完的人的行为归入哪一类？如果他们愿意讨论这本书，那么说他们在谈论一本他们没有读过的书公平吗？对于那些像穆齐尔的图书管理员一样，停留在书本边缘的人，我们可能会提出同样的问题。我们可能想知道，谁是更好的读者——深入阅读作品却无法定位的人，还是不深入阅读任何一本书，但浏览所有书籍的人？

But the fertility of this mode of discovery markedly unsettles the difference between reading and non-reading, or even the idea of reading at all. In which category do we place the behavior of those who have spent a certain amount of time on a book—hours, even—without reading it completely? Should they be inclined to discuss it, is it fair to say of them that they are talking about a book they haven’t read? The same question may be raised with regard to those who, like Musil’s librarian, remain in the margins of the book. Who, we may wonder, is the better reader—the person who reads a work in depth without being able to situate it, or the person who enters no book in depth, but circulates through them all?

正如我们所见，很难——而且情况只会变得更糟——界定什么是不读书，或者什么是读书。似乎大多数情况下，至少对于我们特定文化中的核心书籍，我们的行为处于某种中间地带，以至于很难判断我们是否读过它们。

As we see, it is difficult—and things will only get worse— to delimit just what non-reading is, or indeed reading, for that matter. It appears that most often, at least for the books that are central to our particular culture, our behavior inhabits some intermediate territory, to the point that it becomes difficult to judge whether we have read them or not.

和穆齐尔一样，瓦莱里鼓励我们以集体图书馆而非单本书的角度来思考。对于一个真正的读者，一个关心能够反思文学的人，重要的不是任何一本具体的书，而是所有书的总和。只关注一本书会让我们有可能忽视整体，以及每本书在更大范围内所体现的品质。

Just as Musil does, Valéry prompts us to think in terms of a collective library rather than a solitary book. For a true reader, one who cares about being able to reflect on literature, it is not any specific book that counts, but the totality of all books. Paying exclusive attention to an individual volume causes us to risk losing sight of that totality, as well as the qualities in each book that figure in the larger scheme.

但瓦莱里更进一步，他鼓励我们以同样的态度对待每一本书，保持对这本书的宽广视野，并与对书籍整体的广泛看法相辅相成。在寻求这种视角的过程中，我们必须防止迷失在任何个别段落中，因为只有与书保持合理的距离，我们才有可能体会到它的真正含义。



But Valéry goes further, inviting us to adapt that same attitude to each book, maintaining a broad perspective over it that works in tandem with a broad view of books as a group. In our quest for this perspective, we must guard against getting lost in any individual passage, for it is only by maintaining a reasonable distance from the book that we may be able to appreciate its true meaning.
