III

你听说过的书

III

Books You Have Heard Of

（翁贝托·埃科在其中表明，完全没有必要手拿一本书就能详细地谈论它，只要你听和读别人对它的评论就可以了）

(in which Umberto Eco shows that it is wholly unnecessary to have held a book in your hand to be able to speak about it in detail, as long as you listen to and read what others say about it)

这一理论的逻辑含义是，文化素养涉及在集体图书馆中定位书籍和在每本书中定位自己的双重能力，即最终不需要接触过一本书就能了解它并表达你对这个主题的想法。阅读行为与实体书籍无关；重要的是相遇，这可能很容易涉及非物质对象。

THE LOGICAL IMPLICATION of this theory—that cultural literacy involves the dual capacity to situate books in the collective library and to situate yourself within each book—is that it is ultimately unnecessary to have handled a book to have a sense of it and to express your thoughts on the subject. The act of reading is disassociated from the material book; the important thing is the encounter, which might just as easily involve an immaterial object.

除了实际阅读一本书之外，还有另一种方法可以对书中的内容形成清晰的理解：我们可以阅读或聆听其他人对这本书的描述或评论。这种策略（您可能还记得，瓦莱里在普鲁斯特的案例中自由运用了这种策略）可以为您节省大量时间。当一本书丢失或消失时，或者，正如我们将看到的，当寻找这本书危及想要阅读它的人的生命时，这种方法也是必要的。

Besides actually reading a book, there is, after all, another way to develop quite a clear sense of its contents: we can read or listen to what others write or say about it. This tactic (which, as you may recall, Valéry freely employed in the case of Proust) can save you a lot of time. It can also be necessary when a book is lost or has disappeared, or, as we shall see, when the quest for it imperils the life of the person wishing to read it.

事实上，大多数时候，我们接触到的大多数书籍都是这样的。我们谈论的许多书籍，在某些情况下，在我们的生活中发挥了重要作用，实际上从未经过我们的手（尽管我们有时可能相信事实并非如此）。但是，其他人在文本或对话中与我们或彼此谈论这些书籍的方式，让我们能够对其内容形成一个概念，甚至对它们形成一个合理的看法。

This is, in fact, the extent to which we have access to most books, most of the time. Many of the books we are led to talk about, and which have, in certain cases, played important roles in our lives, have never actually passed through our hands (although we may sometimes be convinced of the contrary). But the way other people talk to us or to each other about these books, in their texts or conversations, allows us to forge an idea of their contents, and even to formulate a reasonable opinion of them.

在《玫瑰之名》1这部以中世纪为背景的小说中，翁贝托·埃科描述了一位名叫巴斯克维尔的威廉的修道士和一个名叫阿德索的年轻人——多年后，阿德索写下了这个故事，此时他自己已经是一位老人——来到意大利北部的一座修道院进行调查，那里发生了一起可疑的死亡事件。

In The Name of the Rose,1 a novel set in the Middle Ages, Umberto Eco describes how a monk named William of Baskerville, accompanied by a young man named Adso— who writes the story many years later, when he himself is an old man—arrives to conduct an investigation in an abbey in northern Italy, where a suspicious death has occurred.

修道院的中心建有一座巨大的图书馆，形状像迷宫，藏书量是整个基督教世界最大的。这座图书馆在宗教界占有重要地位，因此在小说中也占有重要地位——它既是学习和反思的地方，也是整个阅读禁令体系的核心，因为只有经过授权，僧侣才能获得书籍。

At the center of the abbey an immense library has been built in the form of a labyrinth; its holdings are the largest in all of Christendom. This library occupies a major place within the religious community and thus within the novel—both as a place of study and reflection, and as at the heart of a whole system of interdictions governing the right to read, since books are delivered to the monks only after authorization.

在寻找谋杀案真相的过程中，巴斯克维尔发现自己与宗教裁判所及其强大的代表伯纳德·圭展开了竞争。圭坚信这些罪行是异教徒所为，具体来说，是敌视教皇的教派创始人多尔奇诺的信徒所为。圭通过严刑拷打，从几位僧侣那里逼迫他们供认支持他的观点。与此同时，巴斯克维尔仍然不相信他的推理是否准确。

In his search for the truth about the murders, Baskerville finds himself in competition with the Inquisition and its formidable representative, Bernard Gui, who is convinced that the crimes are the work of heretics—specifically, the adepts of Dolcino, the founder of a sect hostile to the papacy. Through torture, Gui wrests from several monks confessions that support his views. Baskerville, meanwhile, remains unconvinced of the accuracy of his reasoning.

事实上，巴斯克维尔得出了不同的结论。他认为这些死亡与异端没有直接关系，僧侣们被杀是因为试图阅读图书馆内一本被严密看管的神秘书籍。他逐渐对这本书的内容以及看管人诉诸谋杀的原因有了概念。在小说的最后几页，他与凶手的激烈对抗引发了图书馆的大火，僧侣们付出了巨大的代价才将图书馆从毁灭中拯救出来。

Indeed, Baskerville has arrived at a different conclusion. He believes that the deaths have no direct relation to heresy, and that the monks have been killed for having attempted to read a mysterious book guarded jealously within the library. He gradually formulates an idea of the contents of the book and the reasons why its guardian has resorted to murder. His violent confrontation with the murderer, in the last pages of the novel, sets off a massive fire in the library, which the monks save from destruction only at great cost.

在最后一幕中，调查员与凶手面对面。凶手原来是豪尔赫，修道院最年长的僧侣之一，但已经失明。豪尔赫祝贺巴斯克维尔解开了谜团，并似乎承认了自己的失败，将导致如此多死亡的书籍交给了他。这本书内容丰富，包括阿拉伯语文本、叙利亚语文本、对《西普里亚尼二世》的解读——这是对《圣经》的模仿——以及第四个希腊语文本，即谋杀案的罪魁祸首。

In this final scene, then, the investigator comes face-to-face with the murderer. This turns out to be Jorge, one of the oldest monks in the abbey, who has lost his sight. Jorge congratulates Baskerville for having solved the mystery and, apparently admitting his defeat, hands him the book that has led to so many deaths. A heterogeneous volume, the book includes an Arabic text, a Syrian text, an interpretation of the Coena Cypriani2—a parody of the Bible—and a fourth text in Greek, the one responsible for the murders.

这本书隐藏在其他书籍之中，是亚里士多德著名的《诗学》已丢失的第二卷。3在这本当时尚未列入书目中的第二卷中，据说这位希腊哲学家继续了他对文学的思考，这次探索的是笑的主题。

This book, hidden among the others, is the lost second volume of Aristotle’s celebrated Poetics.3 In this second volume, which at the time was not yet listed in bibliographies, the Greek philosopher is known to have continued his reflections on literature, this time exploring the theme of laughter.

豪尔赫对巴斯克维尔的指控做出了奇怪的回应。他没有阻止调查员查阅这本书，而是挑战他阅读。巴斯克维尔同意了，但首先采取了预防措施，戴上了一副手套。戴上手套后，他打开书，发现了他认为造成多人死亡的文字的前几行：

Jorge responds strangely to Baskerville’s accusations. Rather than preventing the investigator from consulting the book, he instead challenges him to read it. Baskerville agrees, but first takes the precaution of arming himself with a pair of gloves. Thus equipped, he opens the book to discover the first lines of a text that he believes to have claimed several victims:

在第一本书中，我们讨论了悲剧，并看到了悲剧如何通过唤起怜悯和恐惧，产生宣泄，净化这些情感。正如我们承诺的那样，我们现在将讨论喜剧（以及讽刺和哑剧），并看看喜剧如何通过激发荒谬的乐趣，达到净化这种激情的目的。我们在《灵魂之书》中已经说过，这种激情最值得考虑，因为人类——在所有动物中——是唯一能够笑的人。然后，我们将定义喜剧模仿的行为类型，然后我们将研究喜剧激发笑声的手段，这些手段是行为和言语。我们将展示行为的荒谬性是如何从将最好的比作最坏的，反之亦然的比较中产生的[……]然后，我们将展示言语的荒谬性是如何从对不同事物的相似词和对相似事物的不同词的误解中产生的，等等。4

In the first book we dealt with tragedy and saw how, by arousing pity and fear, it produces catharsis, the purification of those feelings. As we promised, we will now deal with comedy (as well as with satire and mime) and see how, in inspiring the pleasure of the ridiculous, it arrives at the purification of that passion. That such passion is most worthy of consideration we have already said in the book on the soul, inasmuch as—alone among the animals—man is capable of laughter. We will then define the types of actions of which comedy is the mimesis, then we will examine the means by which comedy excites laughter, and these means are actions and speech. We will show how the ridiculousness of actions is born from the likening of the best to the worst and vice versa [ . . . ] We will then show how the ridiculousness of speech is born from the misunderstandings of similar words for different things and different words for similar things, etc.4

似乎可以证实，尤其是考虑到亚里士多德对其他书名的引用，这部神秘的作品确实是《诗学》的第二卷。读完第一页并将其翻译成拉丁文后，巴斯克维尔试图翻阅后面的页面。但他遇到了一个材料上的困难，因为破损的书页粘在一起，戴着手套也无法将它们分开。豪尔赫劝他继续翻阅这本书，但巴斯克维尔坚决拒绝这样做。

It would seem to be confirmed, especially given the evocation of other titles by Aristotle, that this mysterious work is indeed the second volume of the Poetics. After reading the first page and translating it into Latin, Baskerville attempts to leaf through the following pages. But he encounters a material difficulty, since the deteriorated pages are stuck to each other and he cannot separate them while wearing gloves. Jorge exhorts him to keep leafing through the book, but Baskerville firmly refuses to do so.

他明白，要想继续翻书，就必须脱下手套，弄湿指尖，而这样做会毒死自己，就像其他太接近真相的僧侣一样。豪尔赫决定通过在书的上半部分（读者放手指的地方）涂毒来消灭麻烦的研究人员。这是一场典型的谋杀，受害者毒死自己，直到他违反豪尔赫的禁令继续读书。

He has understood that to keep turning the pages, he would have to take off his gloves and moisten his fingertips, and that in so doing he would poison himself, just as the other monks who had come too close to the truth. Jorge has decided to dispatch troublesome researchers by applying poison to the upper part of the book, where the reader places his fingers. It is an exemplary murder, in which the victim poisons himself to the very extent that he violates Jorge’s ban and continues to read.

但为什么要系统地处决那些对亚里士多德《诗学》第二卷感兴趣的人呢？当威廉质问他时，豪尔赫证实了这位僧侣侦探的直觉。谋杀是为了防止僧侣们了解这本书的内容。这本书并没有谴责笑声，而是将其尊为值得研究的对象——而对豪尔赫来说，笑声与信仰是对立的。通过保留将任何事物变成嘲笑对象的权利，它开辟了怀疑之路，而怀疑是启示真理的敌人：

But why systematically execute those who are interested in the second volume of Aristotle’s Poetics? When William questions him, Jorge confirms what the monk-detective has intuited. The murders were committed to prevent the monks from gaining knowledge of the contents of this book. Rather than condemning laughter, the book dignifies it as an object worthy of study—and to Jorge, laughter is antithetical to faith. By reserving the right to turn anything into an object of derision, it opens the path to doubt, which is the enemy of revealed truth:

“但是，在讨论笑声时，什么让你感到害怕？你不能通过消除书籍来消除笑声。”

“But what frightened you in this discussion of laughter? You cannot eliminate laughter by eliminating the book.”

“当然不是。但笑是软弱、腐败、我们肉体的愚蠢。它是农民的娱乐，是醉汉的放纵；甚至教会也明智地允许在盛宴、狂欢节、集市上，在白天的污秽中释放幽默，分散人们对其他欲望和野心的注意力……然而，笑仍然是卑鄙的，是为简单的人辩护，是为平民亵渎的神秘……但在这里，在这里”——乔治用手指敲着威廉拿着的书旁边的桌子——“在这里，笑的功能被颠倒了，它被提升为艺术，世界学者的大门向它敞开，它成为哲学和完美神学的对象。” 5

“No, to be sure. But laughter is weakness, corruption, the foolishness of our flesh. It is the peasant’s entertainment, the drunkard’s license; even the church in her wisdom has granted the moment of feast, carnival, fair, this diurnal pollution that releases humors and distracts from other desires and other ambitions . . . Still, laughter remains base, a defense for the simple, a mystery desecrated for the plebeians [ . . . ] But here, here”—now Jorge struck the table with his finger, near the book William was holding open—“here the function of laughter is reversed, it is elevated to art, the doors of the learned of the world are opened to it, it becomes the object of philosophy and of perfect theology.”5

因此，笑声对信仰是一种威胁，因为它是各种怀疑的载体。这种威胁更为严重，因为这本书的作者是亚里士多德，他在中世纪的影响相当大：

Laughter is thus a threat to faith in that it serves as a vehicle for various forms of doubt. This threat is all the more significant in that the book’s author is Aristotle, whose influence was considerable in the Middle Ages:

“还有很多其他的书谈论喜剧，还有很多赞美笑声的书。为什么这本书让你如此害怕？”

“There are many other books that speak of comedy, many others that praise laughter. Why did this one fill you with such fear?”

“因为它是哲学家写的。那人的每一本书都摧毁了基督教几个世纪以来积累的一部分知识。教父们已经说出了关于圣言力量的一切需要知道的事情，但波爱修斯只需要对哲学家进行解释，圣言的神圣奥秘就变成了人类对类别和三段论的拙劣模仿。《创世纪》一书讲述了关于宇宙组成的需要知道的事情，但重新发现哲学家的物理学就足以将宇宙重新构想为沉闷而黏糊糊的物质[...]哲学家的每一句话，现在甚至圣人和先知都向他发誓，都颠覆了世界的形象。但他并没有成功颠覆上帝的形象。如果这本书成为...成为解释的对象，我们就跨越了最后的界限。” 6

“Because it was by the Philosopher. Every book by that man has destroyed a part of the learning that Christianity had accumulated over the centuries. The fathers had said everything that needed to be known about the power of the Word, but then Boethius had only to gloss the Philosopher and the divine mystery of the Word was transformed into a human parody of categories and syllogism. The book of Genesis says what has to be known about the composition of the cosmos, but it sufficed to rediscover the Physics of the Philosopher to have the universe reconceived in terms of dull and slimy matter [ . . . ] Every word of the Philosopher, by whom now even saints and prophets swear, has overturned the image of the world. But he has not succeeded in overturning the image of God. If this book were to become . . . had become an object for interpretation, we would have crossed the last boundary.”6

因此，对于豪尔赫来说，不仅仅是笑声，亚里士多德的认可也构成了对宗教的威胁，并使得谋杀合理化。在这样一位地位显赫的哲学家的支持下，笑声是有益的（或者说无害的）这一理论有可能被广泛传播，这可能会潜移默化地破坏基督教教义。从豪尔赫的角度来看，阻止僧侣获得这本书是一种虔诚的行为，值得牺牲一些生命。他们的生命是拯救真正信仰并保护其免受质疑的代价。

So it is not laughter alone, but the stamp of Aristotle’s approval that, for Jorge, constitutes a danger for religion and justifies the murders. With the backing of a philosopher of such stature, the theory that laughter is beneficent—or simply not harmful—risks being broadly disseminated, which might subliminally undermine Christian doctrine. From Jorge’s point of view, keeping the book out of the hands of the monks is a pious deed well worth a few victims. Their lives are the price paid for rescuing true faith and protecting it from interrogation.

巴斯克维尔是如何得出真相的？直到最后一幕，他才拿到这本书——而且，在这一幕中，他注意不与它有任何直接的身体接触——更不用说读过它了。但尽管如此，他还是形成了相对准确的印象，以至于他能够向豪尔赫描述它的内容：

How did Baskerville arrive at the truth? He has not held the book in his hands until this last scene—in which, moreover, he takes care not to have any direct physical contact with it— and much less has he read it. But he has, all the same, formed a relatively exact sense of it, so much so that he is able to describe its contents to Jorge:

“渐渐地，第二本书在我心中成型了，这是必然的。我几乎可以告诉你所有内容，而不用读那些本想毒害我的页面。喜剧诞生于 komai——也就是农民村庄——作为饭后或宴会后的欢乐仪式。喜剧讲述的不是名人和权贵，而是卑鄙可笑的生物，尽管并不邪恶；它不会以主角的死亡而结束。它通过展示普通人的缺点和恶习来达到荒谬的效果。在这里，亚里士多德认为笑的倾向是一种向善的力量，它也可以具有教育价值：通过诙谐的谜语和意想不到的隐喻，虽然它告诉我们的事情与事实不同，好像它在撒谎，但它实际上迫使我们更仔细地审视它们，它让我们说：啊，事情就是这样，我不知道[……]是吗？” 7

“Gradually, this second book took shape in my mind as it had to be. I could tell you almost all of it, without reading the pages that were meant to poison me. Comedy is born from the komai—that is, from the peasant villages—as a joyous ceremony after a meal or a feast. Comedy does not tell of famous and powerful men, but of base and ridiculous creatures, though not wicked; it does not end with the death of the protagonists. It achieves the effect of the ridiculous by showing the defects and vices of ordinary men. Here Aristotle sees the tendency to laughter as a force for good, which can also have an instructive value: through witty riddles and unexpected metaphors, though it tells us things differently from the way they are, as if it were lying, it actually obliges us to examine them more closely, and it makes us say: Ah, this is just how things are, and I didn’t know it [ . . . ] Is that it?”7

因此，人们可以相对准确地谈论一本自己从未拿过的书（“我几乎可以告诉你所有内容”），在触摸书籍会致命的情况下，这一点尤为有趣。我们之所以有这种能力，是因为每本书都受某种逻辑支配，瓦莱里对这种逻辑如此感兴趣，以至于他抛弃了其他一切，全心全意地接受它。亚里士多德的书首先是他《诗学》的延伸，巴斯克维尔对《诗学》非常了解。巴斯克维尔直觉地知道了第二本书的主题，并知道了第一本书的轨迹，因此能够预测这本禁书的大致轮廓。

It is possible, then, to speak with relative precision (“I could tell you almost all of it”) about a book one has never held in one’s hands, a point of no small interest in a case where touching the book would be fatal. We derive this ability from the fact that every book is governed by a certain logic, that logic so interesting to Valéry that he embraced it to the exclusion of all else. Aristotle’s book functions first of all as an extension of his Poetics, which Baskerville knows well. Having intuited the subject of the second book, and knowing the trajectory of the first one, Baskerville is able to predict the forbidden book’s general outlines.

这本书遵循第二种逻辑，即其内部发展，巴斯克维尔也能够根据亚里士多德的其他书籍重建这种逻辑。一本书的发展方式从来都不是完全独特的。同一作者的所有作品都呈现出或多或少可察觉的结构相似性，除了明显的差异之外，它们暗中共享一种共同的现实排序方式。

The book obeys a second kind of logic, that of its internal development, which Baskerville is also able to reconstitute based on Aristotle’s other books. A book’s means of progression is never completely idiosyncratic. All works by the same author present more or less perceptible similarities of structure, and beyond their manifest differences, they secretly share a common way of ordering reality.

但第三个同样重要的因素，并非作品本身，而是外在的，它使我们能了解亚里士多德这本书的内容——即它所引起的反应。一本书不仅限于它本身，从传播的那一刻起，它还包括它所激发的交流。观察这些交流，即使不是真正阅读它，也相当于接触了这本书。

But a third and equally important element, this one not intrinsic to the work, but external, makes it possible to gain a sense of the contents of Aristotle’s book—namely, the reactions that it has provoked. A book is not limited to itself, but from the moment of dissemination also encompasses the exchanges it inspires. To observe these exchanges, then, is tantamount to gaining access to the book, if not actually to reading it.

正是通过这样的交流，巴斯克维尔才知道亚里士多德这本书的内容。当豪尔赫惊讶而钦佩地问他如何重现一本他从未拿过的书时（“还不错”，他说8），巴斯克维尔解释说，他的灵感来自维南提乌斯进行的研究，维南提乌斯是一位被谋杀的僧侣，他在巴斯克维尔之前就开始了探索，并留下了一些线索：

It is through just such exchanges that Baskerville has come to know the contents of Aristotle’s book. When Jorge, in astonishment and admiration (“Not bad,” he says8), asks him how he reconstituted a book he has never held in his hands, Baskerville explains that his inspiration was the research conducted by Venantius, the murdered monk who preceded him in his quest and left certain clues behind:

“[维南提乌斯留下的几条笔记帮助了我。] 起初我不明白它们的意义。但其中提到了一块在平原上滚动的无耻石头，还有从地上歌唱的蝉，还有古老的无花果树。我已经读过类似的东西：我在过去几天里证实了这一点。这些是亚里士多德在《诗学》第一卷和《修辞学》中使用的例子。9然后我想起塞维利亚的伊西多尔将喜剧定义为讲述处女和爱情的东西……” 10

“[I was helped by several notes left by Venantius.] At first I didn’t understand their significance. But there were references to a shameless stone that rolls over the plain, and to cicadas that will sing from the ground, to venerable fig trees. I had already read something of the sort: I verified it during these past few days. These are examples that Aristotle used in the first book of the Poetics, and in the Rhetoric.9 Then I remembered that Isidore of Seville defines comedy as something that tells of stupra virginum et amores meretricum . . .”10

通过这些关于这本书的书面交流（维南提乌斯的笔记），以及口头交流（那些接触过这本神秘书籍的人的评论，有时他们并没有意识到），以及对它的反应（当然，从谋杀案开始），巴斯克维尔在这本书落入他手中之前，对它有了越来越清晰的了解，甚至足以在它不在的时候重新创作它。无论这本书有多么新颖和丑闻，它和其他书一样，并不是一个孤立的物品，而是集体图书馆不可或缺的一部分。

Through these written exchanges about the book (Venantius’s notes), but also through spoken exchanges (comments by those who approached the mysterious book, sometimes without realizing it), and reactions to it (beginning, of course, with the murders), Baskerville has gained an increasingly clear sense of the volume before it enters his possession, enough, even, to re-create it in its absence. However original and scandalous it might be, this book, like any other, is not an isolated object but part and parcel of the collective library.

此外，这本书是集体图书馆的代表作，它势必会破坏集体图书馆的基础，而豪尔赫正是因为这个原因才诉诸谋杀。这本书首先对修道院的图书馆构成了威胁，因为它有可能吸引僧侣们前往文化这个发现和毁灭的场所。但从豪尔赫的角度来看，亚里士多德的第二卷也危及了另一个没有围墙的图书馆——人类的集体图书馆。我们对该图书馆中其他书籍的阅读，从《圣经》开始，将永远受到亚里士多德作品的影响。在将所有书籍联系在一起的无尽链条中，一本书就有能力取代其他每一本书。

This book, moreover, figures in a collective library whose foundations it stands to undermine, and it is for precisely this reason that Jorge resorts to murder. The book is a threat to the abbey’s library, first of all, since it risks attracting the monks to that site of discovery and perdition that is culture. But from Jorge’s perspective, Aristotle’s second volume also jeopardizes another library without walls—the collective library of man. Our reading of the other books in that library, starting with the Bible, would forever be modified by Aristotle’s work. Within the interminable chain that links all books together, a single book has the capacity to displace every other one.

《玫瑰之名》的著名情节掩盖了艾柯小说中与我们的主题相关的两个重要元素。首先，巴斯克维尔并非通过无情的逻辑（正如调查员的名字和他对亚里士多德书籍内容的精确结论可能让人想到的那样）而是通过一系列错误的推理得出真相。

The celebrated plot of The Name of the Rose obscures two important and related elements in Eco’s novel that bear on our subject. First of all, it is not through implacable logic (as the name of the investigator and his precise conclusion about the contents of Aristotle’s book might lead one to think) but, in fact, through a series of false deductions that Baskerville arrives at the truth.

如果最后与乔治的对话让巴斯克维尔揭开了所谓的凶手的面纱，那么这也表明他的推理有多么错误。根据对第一批死亡事件的分析，巴斯克维尔得出结论，凶手确实遵循了《启示录》的预言，而这些罪行的性质也符合七号角的经文。11

If the final conversation with Jorge allows Baskerville to unmask the alleged murderer, it also shows him the extent to which he has gone astray in his reasoning. Based on his analysis of the first deaths, Baskerville has concluded that the murderer was literally following the prophecies of the Apocalypse, and that the nature of the crimes was in keeping with the text on the seven trumpets.11

事实上，事后才发现，乔治在监视巴斯克维尔时，发现他正在根据《启示录》对谋杀案进行解读，于是他决定通过植入一系列虚假线索来进一步引诱他犯错，以鼓励他坚持自己的论点，这让他对真相的探寻更加困难。更令人眼花缭乱的是，在欺骗巴斯克维尔时，凶手最终欺骗了自己，他相信这些死亡确实是按照天意安排发生的。12因此，巴斯克维尔发现，他已经找到了真相，但这仅仅是由于他随机积累的错误：

In reality, as is revealed only after the fact, his search for the truth has been further confounded by the fact that Jorge, spying on Baskerville and seeing him home in on his Apocalypse-based interpretation of the murders, decided to lure him further into error by planting a number of false clues designed to encourage him in his thesis. To make matters even more dizzying, in deceiving Baskerville the murderer ended up deceiving himself, becoming persuaded that the deaths were indeed occurring according to a providential plan.12 Thus Baskerville is led to observe that he has reached the truth, but only thanks to the random accumulation of his errors:

我设想了一个错误的模式来解释罪犯的行为，罪犯也信以为真。正是这个错误的模式让我找到了你。13

I conceived a false pattern to interpret the moves of the guilty man, and the guilty man fell in with it. And it was this same false pattern that put me on your trail.13

巴斯克维尔的许多错误推论引发了另一个问题，但本书并没有直接面对这个问题，而只是提出了这个问题：即它让我们怀疑他的最终解决方案是否正确。如果我们承认巴斯克维尔不是通过正确的推理而是通过一系列错误的推论成功地确定了罪犯和这本书，那么就不能保证他的结论是准确的。考虑到一位从未停止犯错的调查员，我们不接受他的最终结论也是可以原谅的。14

Baskerville’s many false deductions raise another problem, which the book does not confront directly but only suggests: namely, it invites us to wonder whether his ultimate solution is correct after all. If we admit that Baskerville has succeeded in identifying the culprit and the book not through correct reasoning but through a series of erroneous deductions, then there is no guarantee that his conclusions are accurate. Given an investigator who never ceases to get things wrong, we may be forgiven for not accepting his final conclusions at face value.14

因此，我们不能排除关于这本书和凶手的双重错误的可能性，也不能否认巴斯克维尔可能在一个案例中说对了，在另一个案例中说错了。乔治是凶手还有待证实；与此同时，他可能有充分的理由鼓励巴斯克维尔产生错觉，认为这本神秘的书确实是亚里士多德《诗学》的第二卷，特别是如果他打算保护一本更可怕的书的话。乔治一直保持着讽刺的态度，直到最后，他都没有真正证实巴斯克维尔的答案，这给结论蒙上了一层怀疑的阴影，在积累了这么多错误之后，这个结论似乎至少是无法证实的。

We cannot exclude the possibility of a twofold error about both the book and the murderer, then, nor can we reject the notion that Baskerville may have gotten things right in one case and wrong in the other. That Jorge is the murderer remains to be proven; meanwhile, he may have every reason to encourage Baskerville in the illusion that the mysterious book is indeed the second volume of Aristotle’s Poetics, particularly if he is intent on protecting an even more formidable book. The ironic attitude Jorge maintains until the end, without ever truly authenticating Baskerville’s solution, casts a shadow of doubt over a conclusion that, in the wake of so many accumulated errors, seems at the very least impossible to verify.

埃科的小说表明，我们所谈论的书只是与“真正的”书有着一丝关联——事实上，我们还能期待什么呢？——而且往往只不过是银幕书。15或者，如果你愿意的话，我们谈论的不是书籍本身，而是我们为此场合创造的替代物。

Eco’s novel illustrates that the books we talk about are only glancingly related to “real” books—indeed, what else would we expect?—and are often no more than screen books.15 Or, if you prefer, what we talk about is not the books themselves, but substitute objects we create for the occasion.

从纯粹的物质层面来看，亚里士多德的书在很大程度上是一个虚拟对象，因为豪尔赫和巴斯克维尔都无法接触到它。豪尔赫在故事开始前很多年就失去了视力，所以他对这本书的理解完全基于记忆，而他的疯狂进一步扭曲了记忆。至于巴斯克维尔，他只能快速浏览这本书，被迫主要依靠他对它的重构，而这种重构的不确定性已经得到证实。毫无疑问，这两个人谈论的是两本不同的书，每个人都根据自己的个人计划构建了一个想象中的对象。

On a purely material level, Aristotle’s book is largely a virtual object, since neither Jorge nor Baskerville has access to it. Jorge lost his vision many years before the story begins, and so his notion of the book is based solely on memory, which is further distorted by his madness. As for Baskerville, he can do no more than rapidly skim the book and is forced to rely primarily on his reconstruction of it, the uncertainty of which has already been demonstrated. Without question, then, the two men are speaking about two different books, each having constructed an imaginary object based on his own personal agenda.

无法接触到文本只会凸显其投射性质，因为这本书成为了两个角色幻想的容器。对豪尔赫来说，亚里士多德的书是他对教会威胁的担忧的源泉，而对巴斯克维尔来说，这本书为他对信仰的相对主义思考提供了支持。他们的幻想不太可能重叠，除非通过共同的幻想，因为这两个人都没有真正掌握文本。

The impossibility of accessing the text only serves to highlight its projective nature, as the book becomes the receptacle of both characters’ fantasies. To Jorge, Aristotle’s book is a locus for his anxieties about threats to the Church, while for Baskerville it provides support for his relativistic reflections on faith. Their fantasies are all the less likely to overlap, other than through shared illusion, in that neither of the two men has, properly speaking, the text in hand.

为了使自己相信我们谈论的任何书都是一本屏幕书，是所有书籍无尽链条中的替代元素，请进行一个简单的实验，将你对童年时珍藏的书的记忆与“真实”书进行比较。不变的差异表明，我们对书籍的记忆，尤其是那些重要到成为我们一部分的书籍，在多大程度上被我们当前环境的无意识利害关系无休止地重组。

To convince yourself that any book we may talk about is a screen book, a substitute element in the endless chain of all books, perform the simple experiment of comparing your memory of a book cherished in childhood with the “real” book. The invariable differences demonstrate the extent to which our memory of books, most particularly those that matter to the point where they become part of us, is endlessly reorganized by the unconscious stakes of our present circumstances.

屏幕书很大程度上由读者对书的了解或自以为了解的内容以及对书的评论组成。在很大程度上，我们关于书的讨论集中在其他人对这些书的讨论上，以此类推，直到无穷无尽。修道院的图书馆是这种关于讨论的讨论的一个光辉象征，其中书本身消失在语言的迷雾中，因为图书馆是无限评论的典型场所。

The screen book consists in large part of what the reader knows or believes he knows about the book, and thus to the comments exchanged about it. To a significant extent, our discourse about books focuses on the discourse of other people about those books, and so forth ad infinitum. The abbey’s library stands as a luminous symbol of such discourse about discourse, in which the book itself disappears in a fog of language, since libraries are the site par excellence of infinite commentary.

这种话语的核心是我们对自己说的话，因为我们自己对书籍的评价和他人的评论一样，将我们与书籍隔离开来，保护我们不受书籍的影响。一旦我们开始阅读，甚至可能在那之前，我们就开始自言自语，然后和别人谈论书籍。此后，我们将诉诸这些评论和观点，而现在变成假设的实体书籍将永远远离我们。

At the core of such discourse is the one we address to ourselves, for our own words about books separate and protect us from them as much as the commentary of others. As soon as we begin to read, and perhaps even before that, we begin talking to ourselves and then to others about books. We will resort thereafter to these comments and opinions, while actual books, now rendered hypothetical, recede forever into the distance.

对于埃科来说，书籍似乎比瓦莱里更像一个未定义的对象，我们只能用不精确的术语来讨论它，它永远受到我们的幻想和幻觉的冲击。亚里士多德的《诗学》第二卷，即使在容量无限的图书馆里也找不到，它与我们生活中讨论的大多数其他书籍没有什么不同。它们都是对原作的重构，这些原作深深地埋藏在我们的话语和他人的话语之下，即使我们愿意冒着生命危险，我们也几乎没有机会在触手可及的地方找到它们。



For Eco even more than Valéry, it seems, the book is an undefined object that we can discuss only in imprecise terms, an object forever buffeted by our fantasies and illusions. The second volume of Aristotle’s Poetics, impossible to find even in a library of infinite capacity, is no different from most other books we discuss in our lives. They are all reconstructions of originals that lie so deeply buried beneath our words and the words of others that, even were we prepared to risk our lives, we stand little chance of ever finding them within reach.

IV

你已经忘记的书

IV

Books You Have Forgotten

（其中，我们与蒙田一起提出了这样的问题：一本你读过却完全忘记的书，甚至你忘记自己读过的书，是否还是一本你读过的书）

(in which, along with Montaigne, we raise the question of whether a book you have read and completely forgotten, and which you have even forgotten you have read, is still a book you have read)

正如我们现在所看到的，一本“读过”的书（如果这个类别仍然有意义的话）和一本“略读”的书之间并没有太大区别。但瓦莱里有比这更好的理由，他只是翻阅了他所讨论的作品，巴斯克维尔也有更好的理由，他评论书籍时没有打开它们，这是因为最认真、最彻底的阅读在事后很快就会变成总结。要理解这一点，我们必须考虑许多理论家忽视的阅读的一个维度：时间。阅读不仅仅是熟悉文本或获取知识；从一开始，它也是一个不可避免的遗忘过程。

AS WE HAVE NOW SEEN, there is not much between a book that has been “read”—if that category still has a meaning— and one that has been skimmed. But Valéry has even better grounds than this for merely flipping through the works he discusses, and Baskerville, likewise, for commenting on books without opening them, which is that the most serious and thorough reading quickly metamorphoses after the fact into summary. To appreciate this, we must take into account a dimension of reading neglected by many theorists: that of time. Reading is not just acquainting ourselves with a text or acquiring knowledge; it is also, from its first moments, an inevitable process of forgetting.

甚至在我读书的时候，我也开始忘记我读过的内容，这个过程是不可避免的。它会延伸到好像我根本没有读过这本书的地步，因此实际上我发现自己重新加入了不读书者的行列，而我本来就应该留在这个行列。在这一点上，说我们读过一本书本质上就是一种转喻。说到书，我们读的从来都不超过长篇或短篇的一部分，而这部分从长远或短期来看，注定会消失。因此，当我们对自己和他人谈论书籍时，更准确的说法是，我们谈论的是我们对书籍的大致记忆，这些记忆会根据当前的情况重新排列。

Even as I read, I start to forget what I have read, and this process is unavoidable. It extends to the point where it’s as though I haven’t read the book at all, so that in effect I find myself rejoining the ranks of non-readers, where I should no doubt have remained in the first place. At this point, saying we have read a book becomes essentially a form of metonymy. When it comes to books, we never read more than a portion of greater or lesser length, and that portion is, in the longer or shorter term, condemned to disappear. When we talk about books, then, to ourselves and to others, it would be more accurate to say that we are talking about our approximate recollections of books, rearranged as a function of current circumstances.

没有读者能逃脱这种遗忘的过程，即使是最贪婪的读者。蒙田就是这种情况，他与古代文化和图书馆有着深厚的联系，但他却坦率地将自己展现为一位非常健忘的读者，这种坦率甚至超过了瓦莱里。

No reader is safe from this process of forgetting, not even the most voracious. Such was the case for Montaigne, who is fundamentally associated with ancient culture and libraries and who nevertheless presents himself, with a frankness that anticipates Valéry, as an eminently forgetful reader.

事实上，记忆缺陷是《随笔集》中一个持续的主题，即使不是最著名的主题。蒙田无休止地抱怨他的记忆问题以及它给他带来的不愉快。例如，他告诉我们，他无法在图书馆里寻找一条信息而不忘记他在寻找什么。在讲话时，他发现有必要保持严谨的话语顺序，以免失去思路。而且他记不住名字，所以他决定根据仆人的职业或原籍国来称呼他们。

The flaws of memory are, in fact, a persistent theme in the Essais,1 if not the best known. Montaigne complains endlessly about his memory trouble and the unpleasantness it causes him. He tells us, for example, that he is incapable of going to look for a piece of information in his library without forgetting on the way what he is looking for. When speaking, he finds it necessary to maintain a tightly ordered discourse so as not to lose his train of thought. And he is so unable to remember names that he resolves to refer to his servants according to their jobs or countries of origin.

问题变得如此严重，以至于一直处于身份危机边缘的蒙田，偶尔担心自己会忘记自己的名字。他甚至开始思考，如果这种不幸事件不可避免地发生，他将如何度过日常生活。

The problem grows so serious that Montaigne, always on the brink of an identity crisis, occasionally fears that he will forget his own name. He even goes so far as to ponder how he will navigate daily life on the inevitable day that such a misadventure occurs.

这种普遍的记忆缺陷显然影响了他所读过的书。在关于他读书的文章开头，蒙田毫不犹豫地承认他很难记住自己读过的书：“如果我是一个读过书的人，”他宣称，“那么我就是一个没有记忆力的人。” 2

This general faultiness of memory plainly affects the books he has read. Toward the beginning of his essay on his reading, Montaigne unhesitatingly acknowledges his difficulty in keeping track of what he has read: “And if I am a man of some reading,” he declares, “I am a man of no retentiveness.”2

蒙田经历了一场渐进而系统的抹杀，从作者到文本本身，这本书的每一个部分都被攻击，每一个部分都从他的记忆中消失得和它进入的速度一样快：

Montaigne experiences a progressive and systematic erasure that attacks every component of the book from the author to the text itself, each vanishing one after the other from his memory as quickly as it entered:

我翻阅书籍，但我并不研究它们。我记住的是那些我不再认为是别人的东西。只有那些让我的判断受益的材料，以及它所包含的思想和观念；作者、地点、文字和其他情况，我立刻就忘记了。3

I leaf through books, I do not study them. What I retain of them is something I no longer recognize as anyone else’s. It is only the material from which my judgment has profited, and the thoughts and ideas with which it has become imbued; the author, the place, the words, and other circumstances, I immediately forget.3

换句话说，这种抹杀是充实的另一面。蒙田将文本变成了自己的文本，然后急于忘记它，好像一本书只不过是某种普遍智慧的临时传递系统，而它的使命完成之后，它就消失了。但事实上，遗忘的含义并非完全是负面的，但这并不能解决它相关的所有问题，尤其是心理问题。它也不能消除因每天必须与他人交谈而加剧的无法在记忆中留下任何东西的痛苦。

This effacement, in other words, is the flip side of an enrichment. Having made the text his own, Montaigne rushes to forget it, as though a book were no more than a temporary delivery system for some general form of wisdom and, its mission accomplished, might as well disappear. But the fact that the implications of forgetting are not altogether negative does not solve all its associated problems, especially the psychological ones. Nor does it dispel the anguish, intensified by the daily obligation of speaking to others, of not being able to fix anything in one’s memory.

确实，我们所有人都会遇到这种不幸，所有文学作品最终都只能给我们提供脆弱而短暂的知识。然而，蒙田的情况似乎很特殊，并且表明他的记忆问题很严重，他无法回忆起自己是否读过某本书：

It is true that we all experience mishaps of this sort, and that all literature ends up providing us only a fragile and temporary kind of knowledge. What seems particular to the case of Montaigne, however, and indicates the breadth of his problems with memory, is his inability to recall whether he has read a specific book:

我的记忆力非常脆弱，我曾多次将几年前仔细阅读并做过笔记的书当作新书重新拿起，但这些书对我来说并不熟悉。为了弥补这一点，我已经养成了一个习惯，在每本书（我指的是那些我打算只读一次的书）的末尾加上我读完这本书的时间和对整本书的评价，这样，这至少可以代表我在阅读这本书时对作者的理解和总体印象。4

To compensate a little for the treachery and weakness of my memory, so extreme that it has happened to me more than once to pick up again, as recent and unknown to me, books which I had read carefully a few years before and scribbled over with my notes, I have adopted the habit for some time now of adding at the end of each book (I mean of those I intend to use only once) the time I finished reading it and the judgment I have derived of it as a whole, so that this may represent to me at least the sense and general idea I had conceived of the author in reading it.4

在这种情况下，记忆缺失更加严重，因为被遗忘的不仅仅是书本，还有阅读的经历。在这里，遗忘不仅抹去了物品的内容（至少物品的大致形状还能被记住），还抹去了阅读行为本身，仿佛抹去的彻底性最终影响了与物品相关的一切。在这种情况下，我们有理由怀疑，我们甚至不记得自己读过的书是否还值得被称为阅读。

The memory deficit is revealed as even more acute in this case, since it is no longer just the book but the experience of reading that is forgotten. Here, the forgetting erases not just the contents of the object—whose general shape, at least, can still be called to mind—but the act of reading itself, as though the radical nature of the erasure had ended up affecting everything related to the object. We would be justified in such circumstances in wondering whether reading that we cannot even remember performing still deserves to be called reading.

奇怪的是，蒙田对自己不喜欢的某些书有着相对准确的记忆；例如，他能够区分西塞罗的不同文本，甚至《埃涅阿斯纪》的不同书卷。5人们会觉得，这些文本尤其没有被遗忘——可能是因为它们比其他文本给人留下了更深刻的印象。在这里，情感因素在用屏幕书代替假设的真实书籍方面也发挥了决定性作用。

Curiously, Montaigne displays a relatively precise memory of certain books he dislikes; he is, for instance, capable of distinguishing different kinds of texts by Cicero or even the different books of the Aeneid.5 One gets the impression that these texts in particular—conceivably because they made a deeper impression than the others—have escaped oblivion. Here, too, the affective factor proves decisive in the substitution of a screen book for the hypothetical real book.

蒙田通过每卷书末的一套巧妙的注释系统找到了解决记忆问题的方法。一旦开始遗忘，他可以利用这些注释重新发现自己最初阅读时对作者及其作品的看法。我们可以假设，注释的另一个功能是确保他确实读过这些注释所记载的作品，就像小径上的火焰，旨在为未来的健忘期指明方向。

Montaigne finds a solution to his memory problem through an ingenious system of notations at the end of each volume. Once forgetfulness has set in, he can use these notes to rediscover his opinion of the author and his work at the time of his original reading. We can assume that another function of the notes is to assure him that he has indeed read the works in which they were inscribed, like blazes on a trail that are intended to show the way during future periods of amnesia.

这篇关于阅读的文章接下来的内容更加令人震惊。在解释了他的符号系统背后的原理之后，蒙田镇定地向读者展示了一些摘录。在这样做的过程中，他告诉读者很难说他是否读过书，因为他已经忘记了它们的内容，必须依靠自己的符号——例如，他写道：“这是我十年前在我的《Guicciardini》中写下的（无论我的书说什么语言，我都用自己的语言来对它们说话）。” 6

What follows in this essay about reading is even more astonishing. After explaining the principle behind his notational system, Montaigne unflappably presents the reader with a few excerpts. In doing so, he tells the reader about books that it is hard to say whether he has read, since he has forgotten their contents and must rely on his own notations—writing, for example, “Here is what I put some ten years ago in my Guicciardini (for whatever language my books speak, I speak to them in my own).”6

第一个“被讨论”的作者确实是文艺复兴时期的历史学家圭恰尔迪尼，蒙田认为他是一位“勤奋的史学家”，而且更值得信赖的是，他自己就是他所叙述事件的参与者，而且似乎不太愿意奉承当权者。他的第二个例子是菲利普·德·科米内斯，蒙田对他赞不绝口，赞赏他语言简洁、叙述纯粹、没有虚荣心。第三，他提到了杜·贝莱的回忆录7，他钦佩这位作家在公职中的工作，但他担心这位作家为国王服务太多了。8

The first author “discussed” is indeed the Renaissance historian Guicciardini, whom Montaigne deems to be a “diligent historiographer,” and all the more trustworthy in that he was himself an actor in the events he recounts and seems little inclined to flatter those in power. His second example is Philippe de Commines, for whom Montaigne has unstinting praise, admiring his simplicity of language, narrative purity, and absence of vanity. Third, he evokes the Memoirs7 of du Bellay, an author whose work in public office he admires, but who, he fears, is too much in the service of the king.8

蒙田在阅读笔记以评论这些文本时（他可能不记得读过这些文本，即使读过，也可能忘记了内容），发现自己处于一个矛盾的境地。他所读的评论并不完全是他的，但对他来说也不是陌生的。他向读者传达了他以前对这些书的反应，却没有费心去核实这种反应是否与他今天可能经历的反应相吻合。

In reading his notes in order to comment on these texts— which he may not remember reading, and even if he does, whose contents he may have forgotten—Montaigne finds himself in a contradictory position. The commentary he is reading is not exactly his, without its being foreign to him either. He conveys to his reader the reaction he had to these books on an earlier occasion, without taking the trouble to verify whether that reaction coincides with what he might experience today.

对于深谙引用艺术的蒙田来说，这是前所未有的情况：他引用的不是其他作家，而是自己。事实上，在这种极端情况下，引用和自我引用之间的区别消失了。蒙田忘记了自己对这些作家的评价，甚至忘记了自己说过什么，他已经变成了另一个人。由于记忆力的缺陷，他与自己早期的化身分不符，他对笔记的解读代表了无数次重新统一的尝试。

For Montaigne, an inveterate practitioner of the art of quotation, this is an unprecedented situation: instead of citing other writers, he cites himself. Indeed, at this extreme the distinction between quotation and self-quotation vanishes. Having forgotten what he said about these authors and even that he said anything at all, Montaigne has become other to himself. He is separated from the earlier incarnation of himself by the defects of his memory, and his readings of his notes represent so many attempts at reunification.

无论蒙田对这种笔记系统的依赖有多么令人惊讶，他毕竟只是从熟悉书籍的人那里得出一些合乎逻辑的结论，无论他的记忆状态如何。我们读过的书所保留的内容——无论我们是否做笔记，即使我们真诚地相信我们忠实地记住了它们——实际上只不过是漂浮在遗忘之海上的几个碎片，就像许多岛屿一样。

However surprising we may find Montaigne’s reliance on this system of notes, he is, after all, only drawing out the logical consequence of something known to anyone familiar with books, whatever the state of his memory. What we preserve of the books we read—whether we take notes or not, and even if we sincerely believe we remember them faithfully—is in truth no more than a few fragments afloat, like so many islands, on an ocean of oblivion.

蒙田的读者还有更多的惊喜等着他。作者继续揭示，尽管读者可能忘记别人的书，甚至记不清自己是否读过，但他更记不住自己的书：

The reader of Montaigne has still more surprises ahead of him. The author goes on to reveal that as forgetful as he may be of other people’s books, to the point where he cannot even recall whether he has read them, he is no more capable of remembering his own:

毫不奇怪，我的书会步其他书的后尘，我的记忆会忘记我所写的内容和我所读的内容，忘记我所给予的内容和我所收到的内容。9

It is no great wonder if my book follows the fate of other books, and if my memory lets go of what I write as of what I read, and of what I give as of what I receive.9

蒙田无法记住自己写过的东西，他发现自己面临着所有失去记忆的人的恐惧：在不知不觉中重复自己，并知道失去对自己写作的掌控的痛苦，却不知不觉地对自己过于忠诚。他的恐惧更有道理，因为《随笔集》谈的不是时事话题，而是永恒的问题。这些问题可能在任何场合被提出，因此，一个失去记忆的作家很容易在不知情的情况下再次处理这些问题，而且是用相同的术语：

Incapable of remembering what he has written, Montaigne finds himself confronted with the fear of all those losing their memory: repeating yourself without realizing it, and knowing the anguish of losing mastery over your own writing only to remain unwittingly all too faithful to yourself. His fear is all the more justified in that the Essais address not topical subjects, but timeless questions. These may be broached on any occasion, and a writer without memory is thus vulnerable to treating them again without knowing it, and in identical terms:

现在我在这里没有提出任何新学到的东西。这些都是常见的想法；也许我曾想过一百遍，恐怕我已经把它们记下来了。10

Now I am bringing in here nothing newly learned. These are common ideas; having perhaps thought of them a hundred times, I am afraid I have already set them down.10

蒙田认为荷马这样的作家身上的这些“重复”令人遗憾，而他觉得，在他自己的作品中，这种“重复”甚至更具“毁灭性”，因为“这些作品只吸引了肤浅而短暂的关注”，11他冒险逐字逐句地重写这些作品，从一章到下一章，甚至都没有意识到。

These “repetitions,” which Montaigne finds regrettable in an author like Homer, seem to him even more “ruinous” in texts like his own, “which attract only superficial and passing attention,”11 and which he risks rewriting word by word, from one chapter to the next, without even perceiving it.

但害怕重复自己的想法并不是忘记自己作品的唯一尴尬后果。另一个尴尬的后果是，当别人在他面前引用他的作品时，蒙田甚至不认识他的作品，这让他不得不谈论那些他没有读过但自己写过的作品。

But fear of repeating himself is not the only embarrassing consequence of forgetting his own books. Another is that Montaigne does not even recognize his own texts when they are quoted in his presence, leaving him to speak about texts he hasn’t read even though he has written them.

因此，对蒙田来说，阅读不仅与记忆缺陷有关，而且鉴于由此产生的矛盾，还与疯狂的痛苦有关。虽然阅读在发生时会丰富生活，但同时也是非人格化的根源，因为我们无法稳定最小的文本片段，这让我们无法与自己相一致。

For Montaigne, therefore, reading is related not only to defective memory, but also, given the contradictions that arise from it, to the anguish of madness. While reading is enriching in the moment it occurs, it is at the same time a source of depersonalization, since, in our inability to stabilize the smallest snippet of text, it leaves us incapable of coinciding with ourselves.

蒙田不断意识到自己的自我正在被遮蔽，他似乎比我们迄今为止遇到的其他任何作家都更能抹杀阅读与不阅读之间的任何区别。事实上，如果读完一本书后，它立即从我们的意识中消失，以至于我们无法记住自己是否读过它，那么阅读的概念本身就失去了意义，因为任何一本书，无论读过还是没读过，最终都会与其他任何一本书等同。

With his repeated sense that his self is being eclipsed, Montaigne, more than any of the other authors we have thus far encountered, seems to erase any distinction between reading and non-reading. Indeed, if after being read a book immediately begins to disappear from consciousness, to the point where it becomes impossible to remember whether we have read it, the very notion of reading loses its relevance, since any book, read or unread, will end up the equivalent of any other.

不管蒙田的例子多么极端，他与书籍的关系揭示了我们与书籍之间关系的真正本质。我们记忆中的书籍并不是与其他人记忆中的书籍完全相同的，而是部分阅读后留下的碎片，这些碎片经常融合在一起，并被我们的私人幻想进一步重塑。最终，我们只剩下伪造的书籍残片，类似于弗洛伊德所说的屏幕记忆，其主要功能是隐藏他人。

However extreme his case may be, Montaigne’s relationship with books reveals the true nature of the relationship we all have with them. We do not retain in memory complete books identical to the books remembered by everyone else, but rather fragments surviving from partial readings, frequently fused together and further recast by our private fantasies. In the end we are left with falsified remnants of books, analogous to the screen memories discussed by Freud, whose principal function is to conceal others.

按照蒙田的说法，我们或许应该用“不读”而不是“读”来描述我们不断遗忘的过程。这个过程既包括参考资料的消失和模糊，也包括书籍（通常只剩下书名或几页内容）变成在我们意识表面滑动的模糊阴影。

Following Montaigne, we should perhaps use the term unreading rather than reading to characterize the unceasing sweep of our forgetfulness. This process involves both the disappearance and the blurring of references, and transforms books, often reduced to their titles or to a few approximate pages, into dim shadows gliding along the surface of our consciousness.

在考虑阅读时，我们应时刻牢记，书籍不仅与知识有关，还与记忆甚至身份的丧失有关。阅读不仅是为了了解自己，而且也许最重要的是，是为了忘记，从而面对我们遗忘的能力。

In every consideration of reading, we should remain mindful that books are linked not only to knowledge, but also to loss of memory and even identity. To read is not only to inform ourselves, but also, and perhaps above all, to forget, and thus to confront our capacity for oblivion.

蒙田这篇散文中出现的阅读主体不是一个统一而自信的人物，而是一个不确定的人物，迷失在几乎无法辨认的文本碎片中。对于这个人物来说，他再也无法区分自己的文本和他人的文本，每次与书的相遇都变得令人恐惧，因为它威胁着让他面对自己的疯狂。

The reading subject that emerges in this essay of Montaigne’s is not a unified and self-assured figure but an uncertain one, lost among fragments of texts he can barely identify. For this figure, no longer able to distinguish his own texts from those of others, each encounter with a book becomes terrifying, for it threatens to bring him face-to-face with his own madness.

尽管蒙田的经历可能令人痛苦，但他的经历或许能给那些似乎无法获得文化素养的人带来安慰。我们必须记住，我们可能接触到的最认真的读者，也和蒙田一样，不自觉地不读书，他们甚至忘记了那些他们真诚地认为自己已经掌握的书籍。

As agonizing as it may be, Montaigne’s experience may nonetheless have the salutary effect of reassuring those to whom cultural literacy seems unattainable. It is vital to keep in mind that the most conscientious readers we might speak to are also, just like Montaigne, involuntary non-readers, and that their forgetfulness extends even to books that in all good faith they believe themselves to have mastered.

把阅读视为一种损失（无论是在浏览一本书之后，还是通过道听途说吸收一本书，或通过逐渐遗忘的过程）而不是收获，对于任何寻求有效策略以应对尴尬的文学冲突的人来说，这都是一种必不可少的心理资源。在定义了不同类型的非阅读行为之后，我们现在将注意力转向这些社交情况。



To conceive of reading as loss—whether it occurs after we skim a book, in absorbing a book by hearsay, or through the gradual process of forgetting—rather than as gain is a psychological resource essential to anyone seeking effective strategies for surviving awkward literary confrontations. Having defined the different kinds of non-reading, it is to these social situations that we now turn our attention.

2. The Complete Essays of Montaigne, translated by Donald Frame (Stanford: Stanford University Press, 1957), p. 296.

文学对抗

Literary Confrontations

五、

社会遭遇

V

Encounters in Society

（格雷厄姆·格林在其中描述了一个噩梦般的场景，主人公发现自己面对着满满一礼堂的崇拜者，他们不耐烦地等待着他讲述自己还没读过的书）

(in which Graham Greene describes a nightmarish situation where the hero finds himself facing an auditorium full of admirers impatiently waiting for him to speak about books that he hasn’t read)

在研究了不读书的主要类型之后，正如我们所看到的，不读书可能比单纯的不读书更微妙，现在让我们考虑几种常见的情况，在这些情况下，读者（或者更确切地说，不读书的人）发现自己被迫谈论他没有读过的书。我希望这些受我个人经历启发的思考能够帮助不读书的人自己处理这种情况。

HAVING EXAMINED THE PRINCIPAL KINDS of non-reading, which, as we have seen, may take more subtle forms than a simple absence of reading pure and simple, let us now consider several common situations in which the reader (or rather, the non-reader) finds himself forced to speak about books he hasn’t read. It is my hope that these reflections, inspired by my personal experience, will be of use to the nonreader in negotiating such situations himself.

最常见的文学冲突发生在我们的社交生活中，其中最令人恼火的是那些我们需要在一群人面前表达自己想法的冲突。在这种情况下，谈话可能会转向一本我们没有读过的书。如果所有有教养的人都认为这本书是众所周知的，或者我们错误地脱口而出说我们读过这本书，我们可能会发现自己不得不努力挽回面子。

The most common literary confrontations are those that occur in our social lives, and of these the most vexing are those in which we are expected to express ourselves in front of a group. On such occasions, the conversation may turn to a book we have not read. If the book in question is assumed to be known by all cultivated individuals, or if we make the error of blurting out that we have read it, we may find ourselves forced to try to save face.

毫无疑问，这是一种令人不快的情况，但只要稍微巧妙一点，我们就可以毫不费力地摆脱它——例如，通过改变话题。但很容易想象这种情况会变成一场噩梦，在噩梦中，被迫谈论一本他没有读过的书的人会受到一群渴望了解他想法的听众的全神贯注。这种情况让人想起弗洛伊德所说的“考试梦”，在梦中，惊恐的做梦者想象自己被叫去参加一场他没有准备好的考试，这让他的意识中又浮现出一系列埋藏的童年恐惧。1

This is an unpleasant situation, no doubt, but with a little finesse we may extricate ourselves from it at no great cost— by changing the subject, for example. But it’s easy to imagine such a situation turning into a nightmare, in which the person being forced to speak about a book he hasn’t read is subjected to the rapt attention of an entire audience eager to know his thoughts. Such circumstances bring to mind what Freud calls the “examination dream,” in which the terrified dreamer imagines himself summoned to an exam for which he is not prepared, and which calls back to consciousness a whole series of buried childhood fears.1

这正是《第三人》中罗洛·马丁斯的遭遇，这部小说是格雷厄姆·格林的小说，卡罗尔·里德的著名电影就是受此启发而拍摄的。小说开头，故事主人公马丁斯来到战后的维也纳，这里被分成四个区域，分别由法国、英国、美国和苏联控制。

This is indeed what happens to Rollo Martins in The Third Man, the Graham Greene novel that inspired Carol Reed’s celebrated film. At the beginning of the book, Martins, the story’s protagonist, arrives in postwar Vienna, which has been divided into four sectors respectively controlled by France, England, the United States, and the Soviet Union.

马丁斯前往维也纳寻找童年好友哈里·莱姆，莱姆请马丁斯来见他。但当他到达莱姆家时，却发现他的朋友刚刚在一场事故中丧生，在离开家时被车撞倒。马丁斯前往举行葬礼的墓地，在那里遇到了莱姆的情妇安娜和一名名叫卡洛威的宪兵。

Martins has traveled to Vienna to find his childhood friend Harry Lime, who has asked Martins to come meet him. But when he arrives at Lime’s home, he discovers that his friend has just died in an accident, struck down by a car as he left his house. Martins heads to the cemetery where the funeral is being held, and there meets Anna, Lime’s mistress, along with a military police officer named Calloway.

在接下来的几天里，马丁斯在询问多位证人时，注意到了许多矛盾之处，他确信他的朋友不是死于意外，而是死于谋杀。卡洛威也对莱姆的死因心存疑虑，但原因不同。他知道莱姆不仅是马丁斯记忆中体贴的朋友，而且还是一个不择手段的奸商，他利用战后时期贩卖被污染的青霉素，服用后会致命。

In questioning various witnesses in the days that follow, Martins notices a number of contradictions, and he becomes convinced that his friend was the victim not of an accident, but of a murder. Calloway also has doubts about the circumstances of Lime’s death, but for other reasons. He knows that Lime was not only the considerate friend Martins remembers, but also an unscrupulous profiteer who took advantage of the postwar period to sell tainted penicillin, whose effects were fatal for those who consumed it.

与此同时，马丁斯爱上了安娜。一天，当他离开安娜的公寓楼时，马丁斯注意到街上有一名男子在站岗，原来是莱姆。事实上，他还活着，由于害怕被警方逮捕，他在几名同伙的帮助下策划了自己的失踪。

Meanwhile, Martins has fallen in love with Anna. One day, as he leaves her apartment building, Martins notices a man standing watch in the street, who turns out to be Lime. He is, in fact, still alive and has staged his own disappearance with the help of a few accomplices out of fear of being arrested by the police.

通过其中一名同伙，马丁斯要求与莱姆见面。重逢在维也纳普拉特的摩天轮上举行。莱姆表现出马丁斯从小就认识的那个富有同情心的人，但偶尔也会让人觉得他是一个毫无顾忌、对受害者的命运漠不关心的人。

Through one of these accomplices, Martins demands a meeting with Lime. The reunion takes place on the great Ferris wheel of the Prater in Vienna. Lime shows himself to be the sympathetic fellow that Martins has known since childhood, but also offers occasional glimpses of a man without scruples, indifferent to the fate of his victims.

马丁斯被朋友的所作所为吓坏了，决定与警方合作，通过安排另一次会面将莱姆引入陷阱。但莱姆逃进了地下下水道系统，在那里被警方打伤。为了结束他的痛苦，马丁斯杀死了他，然后带着安娜离开了维也纳。

Terrified by what his friend has become, Martins decides to collaborate with the police and draw Lime into a trap, by arranging for another meeting. But Lime escapes into the underground sewer system, where he is wounded by the police. To put an end to his suffering, Martins finishes him off, then leaves Vienna with Anna at his side.

侦探故事的中心叙事与围绕马丁斯职业活动的另一条更幽默的情节相得益彰。他是一名作家，尽管他没有这样描述自己。他谦虚的原因是，他写的不是伟大的文学作品，而是西部片，这些作品以笔名巴克·德克斯特 (Buck Dexter) 出现，并带有诸如《圣达菲的孤独骑士》等令人回味的标题。2

The central narrative of the detective story is complemented by another more humorous plotline surrounding Martins’s professional activities. He is a writer, though he doesn’t describe himself as such. He owes his modesty to the fact that he writes not great works of literature, but westerns, which appear under the pseudonym Buck Dexter and bear such evocative titles as The Lonely Horseman of Santa Fe.2

笔名巴克·德克斯特是贯穿全书的误解的根源。事实上，大使馆文化处把马丁斯和另一个德克斯特搞混了，后者的名字是本杰明。这位德克斯特是一位高雅小说家，他的作品包括《弯曲的船头》3，与亨利·詹姆斯的作品属于同一文学流派。

The pen name Buck Dexter is the basis of a misunderstanding that extends throughout the book. The cultural office of the embassy has, in fact, confused Martins with another Dexter, whose first name is Benjamin. This Dexter is a highbrow novelist whose works, bearing such titles as The Curved Prow,3 occupy the same literary genre as those of Henry James.

马丁斯没有澄清事实，而是非常小心地避免消除这种混乱，因为他来到维也纳时身无分文，而错误的身份是他免费住宿酒店的门票，他需要这张票才能继续调查。但他竭尽全力避开文化办公室代表克拉宾，因为他害怕必须履行本杰明·德克斯特的职责。

Rather than clear things up, Martins is extremely careful not to dispel the confusion, for he has arrived in Vienna without any money, and the mistaken identity is his ticket to free lodging in a hotel, which he needs in order to pursue his investigation. But he makes every effort to avoid the representative of the cultural office, Crabbin, for fear of having to fulfill the duties that are Benjamin Dexter’s.

一天晚上，克拉宾强迫马丁斯为他的崇拜者们发表文学演讲，事情因此变得糟糕起来。由于人们认为马丁斯就是德克斯特，他不得不对德克斯特的作品发表评论，理论上，作为作者，他是德克斯特作品方面的专家——尽管事实上他既没有写过这些作品，也没有读过这些作品。

Things go awry one evening when Crabbin forces Martins to come deliver a literary lecture to an audience of admirers. Since he is assumed to be Dexter, he finds himself in the position of having to comment on Dexter’s works, on which (as the author himself ) he is theoretically a specialist—even though he has, in fact, neither written nor read them.

马丁斯的情况尤其复杂，因为另一个德克斯特生活在一个对他来说完全陌生的文学领域，他是一位通俗小说作家。这个世界是如此陌生，以至于马丁斯不仅完全无法回答观众的问题，而且在很大程度上甚至无法理解他们的问题：“马丁完全错过了第一个问题，”格林写道，“但幸运的是，克拉宾填补了空白，并给出了令人满意的答案。” 4

Martins’s situation is especially complex in that the other Dexter dwells in a region of literature that is totally foreign to him, an author of popular novels. So alien is this world that Martins is not only completely incapable of answering the audience’s questions, but for the most part incapable of even understanding them: “Martin missed the first question altogether,” Greene writes, “but luckily Crabbin filled the gap and answered it satisfactorily.”4

更糟糕的是，马丁斯面对的并不是普通的读者群体，而是一群崇拜者——“他”作品的文学爱好者，他们终于能得到《德克斯特》的帮助，并渴望表达敬意，他们忍不住炫耀，问了一些非常专业的问题：



To make matters even worse, Martins is not dealing with just any group of readers, but with a circle of admirers— literary enthusiasts of “his” works, who, delighted finally to have Dexter at their disposal and eager to pay homage, cannot resist showing off by asking highly specialized questions:



一位身穿手工编织套头衫、面容和蔼的女士若有所思地说道：“德克斯特先生，您不同意吗？没有人能像弗吉尼亚·伍尔夫那样用诗意的方式描写情感？我的意思是，用散文的方式。”

A kind-faced woman in a hand-knitted jumper said wistfully, “Don’t you agree, Mr. Dexter, that no one, no one has written about feelings so poetically as Virginia Woolf? In prose, I mean.”

克拉宾低声说道：“你可以谈谈意识流。”

Crabbin whispered, “You might say something about the stream of consciousness.”

“什么流？” 5



“Stream of what?”5



甚至在问到哪些作家影响了他的创作时，马丁斯也很快陷入了困境。虽然他确实崇拜一些大师，但他将自己置于与同名作家完全不同的世系中，这个世系的作家都是廉价小说作家：



Even on the question of writers that have influenced his work, Martins quickly finds himself in trouble. While there are certainly great masters whom he admires, he places himself within an entirely different lineage than the man who shares his name, a lineage featuring writers of dime-store fiction:



“德克斯特先生，您能告诉我们哪位作家对您影响最大吗？”

“Mr. Dexter, could you tell us what author has chiefly influenced you?”

马丁斯不假思索地回答道：“格雷。”他当然是指《紫色鼠尾草骑士》的作者，6他很高兴地发现他的回答让所有人都满意——除了一位年长的奥地利人问道：“格雷。什么格雷？我不知道这个名字。”

Martins, without thinking, said, “Grey.” He meant of course the author of Riders of the Purple Sage,6 and he was pleased to find his reply gave general satisfaction— to all save an elderly Austrian who asked, “Grey. What Grey? I do not know the name.”

马丁斯觉得自己现在安全了，说道：“赞恩·格雷——我不认识其他人了。”他对英国殖民地传来的低沉而卑微的笑声感到很困惑。7



Martins felt he was safe now and said, “Zane Grey— I don’t know any other,” and was mystified at the low subservient laughter from the English colony.7



无论马丁斯如何回应，显然对讨论没有直接影响，讨论仍在继续。对话发生在一个似乎不真实的场景中，更像是梦境中的空间——拥有自己的法则，与我们日常对话的法则相去甚远。

No matter how Martins responds, it evidently has no direct impact on the discussion, which continues to follow its normal course. The dialogue transpires in a setting that seems not real, but rather like the space in dreams—possessed of its own laws, which are considerably removed from those that govern our ordinary conversations.

尽管如此，克拉宾还是感觉到马丁斯有麻烦了，并最终介入。但他的干预却不由自主地使交流变得更加复杂，加深了观众和作者之间的误解：



All the same, Crabbin senses that Martins is in trouble and finally steps in. But his intervention has the involuntary effect of complicating the exchange still further, by compounding the misunderstanding between the audience and the author:



“这是德克斯特先生的一个小玩笑。他指的是诗人格雷——一位温和、温和、细腻的天才——人们可以看出他和格雷的相似之处。”

“That is a little joke of Mr. Dexter’s. He meant the poet Gray—a gentle, mild, subtle genius—one can see the affinity.”

“他叫赞恩·格雷吗？”

“And he is called Zane Grey?”

“那是德克斯特先生的玩笑。赞恩·格雷写的就是我们所谓的西部片——关于土匪和牛仔的廉价通俗小说。”

“That was Mr. Dexter’s joke. Zane Grey wrote what we call Westerns—cheap popular novelettes about bandits and cowboys.”

“他不是一个伟大的作家吗？”

“He is not a great writer?”

“不，不。远非如此，”克拉宾先生说。“严格意义上来说，我根本不会称他为作家。” 8



“No, no. Far from it,” Mr. Crabbin said. “In the strict sense I would not call him a writer at all.”8



现在，克拉宾这样说，让马丁斯感到难以忍受，因为他正在涉足构成马丁斯个人世界和他生存理由的文学领域。尽管马丁斯一般不认为自己是一名作家，但当他看到自己被公开剥夺了这一头衔时，他成为了一名作家：



Now, in saying this, Crabbin creates an intolerable situation for Martins, for he is taking on that sector of literature that constitutes Martins’s personal universe and is his reason for living. And while in general Martins does not consider himself a writer, he becomes one upon seeing himself publicly denied that title:



马丁斯告诉我，这句话让他第一次感到反感。他以前从未把自己视为作家；但克拉宾的自信让他恼火——甚至克拉宾眼镜反射的光线似乎也让他恼火。克拉宾说：“他只是一个受欢迎的艺人。”

Martins told me that he felt the first stirrings of revolt at that statement. He had never regarded himself before as a writer; but Crabbin’s self-confidence irritated him—even the way the light flashed back from Crabbin’s spectacles seemed an added cause of vexation. Crabbin said, “He was just a popular entertainer.”

“为什么不呢？”马丁斯愤怒地说道。

“Why the hell not?” Martins said fiercely.

“哦，好吧，我只是想——”

“Oh well, I merely meant—”

“莎士比亚是什么？” 9



“What was Shakespeare?”9



情况很快就变得更加复杂，因为克拉宾试图为一位没有读过他所讨论作品的作家解围（因为他没有写过这本书），这使他陷入了类似的境地。正如马丁斯迅速指出的那样，他也只能谈论他不了解的书：



The situation quickly becomes even more tangled, because Crabbin, trying to come to the rescue of a writer who hasn’t read the work he’s discussing (because he hasn’t written it), puts himself in a parallel situation. He, too, is reduced to speaking about books he doesn’t know, as Martins is quick to point out:



“你读过赞恩·格雷 (Zane Grey) 的作品吗？”

“Have you ever read Zane Grey?”

“不，我不能说——”

“No, I can’t say—”

“那你就不知道自己在说什么了。” 10



“Then you don’t know what you are talking about.”10



毫无疑问，这是事实。不过，克拉宾的判断是基于《格雷》在集体图书馆中的地位，而集体图书馆让我们能够发展我们对书籍的看法。根据《格雷》小说的类型、书名以及马丁斯对这些小说的描述，克拉宾发表意见的合理性并不比我们迄今为止遇到的所有其他知情的非读者更差。

This is unarguably true. Still, Crabbin is basing his judgment on Grey’s place in the collective library that allows us to develop our idea of books. Based on the genre Grey’s novels fall into, their titles, and what Martins communicates about them, Crabbin is no less justified in voicing an opinion than all the other informed non-readers we have encountered thus far.

尽管观众偶尔会发出一些惊讶的低语，但马丁斯还是相当优雅地完成了这项任务，原因有二。

Despite the occasional murmurs of surprise from his audience, Martins emerges quite gracefully from this exercise, for two reasons.

首先是无论问什么问题，他都表现出坚定的自信：



The first is the unfailing self-assurance he demonstrates, no matter what question is asked:



“那么詹姆斯·乔伊斯，您会把詹姆斯·乔伊斯放在哪里呢，德克斯特先生？”

“And James Joyce, where would you put James Joyce, Mr. Dexter?”

“你说什么‘放’？我不想放任何人，”马丁斯说。这一天过得非常充实：他和库勒上校喝得太多；他坠入爱河；一个人被谋杀了——现在他有一种非常不公平的感觉，觉得自己被人针对了。赞恩·格雷是他的英雄之一：如果他要忍受任何胡言乱语，他就该死。

“What do you mean, ‘put’? I don’t want to put anyone anywhere,” Martins said. It had been a very full day: he had drunk too much with Colonel Cooler; he had fallen in love; a man had been murdered—and now he had the quite unjust feeling that he was being got at. Zane Grey was one of his heroes: he was damned if he was going to stand any nonsense.

“我的意思是，你会把他列为真正伟大的人吗？”

“I mean would you put him among the really great?”

“如果你想知道，我从来没听说过他。他写了什么？” 11



“If you want to know, I’ve never heard of him. What did he write?”11



如果马丁斯的自信部分归因于他的性格，那么这也与他被这次会议的组织者和听众置于权威地位有关。他说的任何话都会对他有利，因为考虑到他所拥有的象征性地位（只要他的身份不被揭露），他不可能说出任何愚蠢的话。因此，他越是表现出自己不了解这个主题，他在另一个层面上就越令人信服：

If Martins’s confidence is due in part to his character, it is also a function of his having been placed in a position of authority by the organizer of this meeting and his audience. Anything he might say redounds in his favor, since given the symbolic place he holds (and so long as his identity is not revealed), it is impossible that he would say anything foolish. Thus the more he demonstrates that he doesn’t know his subject, the more convincing he becomes on another level:

他没有意识到，但他给人们留下了深刻的印象。只有伟大的作家才能写出如此傲慢、如此独创的文字。几个人在信封背面写了赞恩·格雷的名字，格雷夫沙哑地对克拉宾低声说：“赞恩这个名字怎么拼写？”

He didn’t realize it, but he was making an enormous impression. Only a great writer could have taken so arrogant, so original a line. Several people wrote Zane Grey’s name on the backs of envelopes and the Gräfin whispered hoarsely to Crabbin, “How do you spell Zane?”

“说实话，我不太确定。”

“To tell you the truth, I’m not quite sure.”

马丁斯同时被抛出几个名字——像斯坦因一样尖锐的小名字，像伍尔夫一样圆润的小名字。一位留着一头黑色前额头发的奥地利年轻人喊道：“达芙妮·杜穆里埃”，克拉宾先生皱了皱眉，斜眼看着马丁斯。他低声说：“对他们温柔一点。” 12



A number of names were simultaneously flung at Martins—little sharp pointed names like Stein, round pebbles like Woolf. A young Austrian with an intellectual black forelock called out, “Daphne du Maurier,” and Mr. Crabbin winced and looked sideways at Martins. He said in an undertone, “Be gentle with them.”12



权威是我们讨论书籍时必不可少的因素，因为引用文本通常是确立自己权威或质疑他人权威的一种方式。马丁斯可以将本杰明·德克斯特与西部片传统联系起来，而不会产生矛盾：要么他的陈述会被接受为富有启发性和原创性，要么如果它们太过分，它们会被理解为幽默。13 无论是哪种情况，对他的陈述的准确性的信念先于其表述，因此陈述的内容相对不那么重要。

Authority is an essential element at play in our discussions of books, if only because citing a text is most often a way of establishing one’s own authority or contesting that of others. Martins can connect Benjamin Dexter to the tradition of the western without risk of contradiction: either his statements will be accepted as illuminating and original, or, should they push the envelope too far, they will be understood as humorous.13 In either case, the belief that his statement is accurate precedes its formulation, and thus the content of the statement is of relatively little importance.

发掘和研究其中的力量，或者，如果你愿意的话，分析我们在谈论一部作品时所处的确切位置，对于我们反思未读过的书至关重要。只有通过这样的分析，当我们发现自己没有读过我们谈论的书时，我们才能采取正确的策略，就像马丁斯在这里所经历的那样。我们将有机会在后面回到这个策略问题上。

To uncover and study the power in play, or, if you prefer, to analyze the exact position we find ourselves in when speaking about a work, is essential to our reflection on books we haven’t read. It is only through such analysis that we will be able to adopt the correct strategy when we find ourselves in the position of not having read the books we’re talking about, as Martins experiences here. We will have occasion to return to this question of strategy further on.

那么，在这次公开演讲中，一位没有读过他要讲的书的作家面对的是一位没有读过他所写作品的听众。我们面前有一个完美的例子，即传统上所谓的聋人对话。14

In this public lecture, then, a writer who has not read the books on which he is expected to speak confronts an audience that has not read those he has written. We have before us a perfect example of what is conventionally called a dialogue of the deaf.14

虽然这种情况在《第三人》的讲座中被推向了极端，但在我们的书籍对话中，这种情况比你想象的更常见。首先，不同的对话者通常不会读过他们正在谈论的书，或者只是粗略地看过，在这种情况下，他们实际上谈论的是不同的书。

While this scenario is taken to the extreme in the case of the lecture in The Third Man, it occurs more commonly than you might think in our conversations about books. First, often the various interlocutors will not have read the book they are talking about, or will only have skimmed it, in which case they are each actually talking about a different book.

其次，在更不寻常的情况下，每个人都拿过书并真正了解它，讨论的重点不是书本身，而是关于一个碎片化和重构的对象（例如，正如我们在翁贝托·埃科的作品中看到的那样），这是一本私人的屏幕书，与其他读者的屏幕书无关，因此不太可能与它们重叠。

Second, in the more unusual case in which each person has held the book in his or her hands and truly knows it, the discussion is less about the book itself than about a fragmentary and reconstituted object (as we have seen in Umberto Eco, for example), a private screen book unrelated to the screen books of the other readers and unlikely, as a result, to overlap with them.

但这里所涉及的问题超越了任何一本书的范畴。聋人对话不仅体现了马丁斯所谈论的两位作者之间的分歧，还体现了在场各方试图基于两套书籍，或者说，两个截然不同且相互对立的图书馆进行对话这一事实。这不仅仅是两本书在起作用，而且是两份不可调和的名字列表（德克斯特和德克斯特，格雷和格雷），这是两种文化相互对抗的深刻差异，甚至是不相容的结果。

But what is at stake here transcends the case of any individual book. The dialogue of the deaf is a function not only of the divergence between the two authors Martins is speaking about, but also of the fact that the parties present are attempting to conduct a dialogue on the basis of two sets of books, or, if you prefer, two distinct and adversarial libraries. It is not simply two books that are in play, but two irreconcilable lists of names (Dexter and Dexter, Grey and Gray), as a result of the profound difference, indeed the incompatibility, of the two cultures confronting each other.

我们或许可以使用“内在图书馆”这个术语来描述那套书籍——集体图书馆的一个子集——每个人的个性都围绕着它构建，并塑造每个人与书籍和他人的个人关系。15这些私人图书馆里有特定的书名，但就像蒙田的图书馆一样，它们主要由一些被遗忘和想象的书籍的片段组成，我们通过这些书籍来理解世界。

We might use the term inner library to characterize that set of books—a subset of the collective library—around which every personality is constructed, and which then shapes each person’s individual relationship to books and to other people.15 Specific titles figure in these private libraries, but, like Montaigne’s, they are primarily composed of fragments of forgotten and imaginary books through which we apprehend the world.

在这种情况下，聋人对话的起因是马丁斯和他的听众的内部图书馆没有重叠，或者重叠程度有限。即使提到了某些书名，冲突也不仅限于任何特定的书，而是更广泛地涉及书籍和文学的概念。因此，实现两个图书馆之间的沟通并不容易，任何这样做的尝试都不可避免地会造成紧张。

In this case, the dialogue of the deaf arises from the fact that the inner libraries of Martins and of his audience don’t overlap, or do so only to a limited extent. The conflict is not limited to any particular book, even if certain titles are mentioned, but bears more broadly on the very conception of what a book, and literature, may be. For this reason, achieving communication between the two libraries will not be easy, and any attempt to do so will inevitably create tension.

因此，事实上我们从不谈论一本书本身；一整套书总是通过一个标题进入讨论，这个标题是完整文化概念的临时象征。在每一次这样的讨论中，我们的内心图书馆——多年来在我们内心建立起来并收藏着我们所有的秘密书籍——都会与他人的内心图书馆发生接触，从而可能引发各种摩擦和冲突。

Thus it is that in truth we never talk about a book unto itself; a whole set of books always enters the discussion through the portal of a single title, which serves as a temporary symbol for a complete conception of culture. In every such discussion, our inner libraries—built within us over the years and housing all our secret books—come into contact with the inner libraries of others, potentially provoking all manner of friction and conflict.

因为我们不仅仅是内心图书馆的庇护所；我们是这些书籍的总和。这些书籍一点一点地塑造了我们，如果我们不把它们从我们身边带走，我们就会遭受痛苦。就像马丁斯无法忍受听到对他的英雄所写的小说的批评一样，那些挑战我们内心图书馆的书籍、攻击我们身份一部分的评论可能会伤害到我们内心的核心。



For we are more than simple shelters for our inner libraries; we are the sum of these accumulated books. Little by little, these books have made us who we are, and they cannot be separated from us without causing us suffering. Just as Martins cannot bear to hear criticism of the novels written by his heroes, comments that challenge the books in our inner libraries, attacking what has become a part of our identity, may wound us to the core of our being.



1. “每个通过了高中入学考试的人在毕业时都会抱怨自己总是被焦虑的梦境所困扰，梦见自己考试不及格，或者不得不重新参加考试等等。对于那些已经获得大学学位的人来说，这个典型的梦境被另一个梦境所取代，这个梦境代表他们在大学期末考试中失败；他们甚至在睡梦中也反驳说自己多年来一直在行医、担任大学讲师或办公室主任，但这是徒劳的。我们童年时因做坏事而受到惩罚的难以磨灭的记忆再次活跃在我们心中，并与我们学习的两个关键点——最严格的考试的dies irae和dies illa紧密相连。”西格蒙德·弗洛伊德， 《梦的解析》，詹姆斯·斯特雷奇译（纽约：埃文，1965 年），第 308 页。

1. “Everyone who has passed the Matriculation examination at the end of his school studies complains of the obstinacy with which he is pursued by anxiety-dreams of having failed, or of being obliged to take the examination again, etc. In the case of those who have obtained a University degree this typical dream is replaced by another one which represents them as having failed in their University finals; and it is in vain that they object, even while they are still asleep, that for years they have been practicing medicine or working as University lecturers or heads of offices. The ineradicable memories of the punishments that we suffered for our evil deeds in childhood become active within us once more and attach themselves to the two crucial points in our studies—the dies irae, dies illa of our stiffest examinations.” Sigmund Freud, The Interpretation of Dreams, translated by James Strachey (New York:Avon, 1965), p. 308.

13. Before arriving in Vienna, Martins makes a stop in Frankfurt, where he is also mistaken for the other Dexter and where his frank answers are also taken to be humorous:

当一名记者走近他的桌子时，他从二十英尺外就认出了一名男子。

A man he could recognize from twenty feet away as a journalist approached his table.

“您是德克斯特先生吗？”他问道。

“You Mr. Dexter?” he asked.

“是的，”马丁斯放松了警惕说道。

“Yes,” Martins said, taken off his guard.

“你看上去比照片上年轻，”那人说……“那对美国小说的看法呢？”

“You look younger than your photographs,” the man said [ . . . ] “What about views on the American novel?”

“我不读它们。”

“I don’t read them.”

“这是众所周知的尖刻幽默，”这位记者说道。（同上，第 13 页。）

“The well-known acid humor,” the journalist said. (Ibid., p. 13.)
