15. The second of the three libraries I am introducing in this book, the inner library is a subjective part of the collective library and includes the books that have left a deep impression on each subject.

VI

与教授的邂逅

VI

Encounters with Professors

（我们与西非的蒂夫人族一致确认，完全没有必要打开一本书来发表开明的观点，即使你在此过程中惹恼了专家）

(in which we confirm, along with the Tiv tribe of western Africa, that it is wholly unnecessary to have opened a book in order to deliver an enlightened opinion on it, even if you displease the specialists in the process)

作为一名教师，我比一般人更经常地被迫向一大群听众讲述我从未读过的书，无论是严格意义上的（从未打开过）还是粗略意义上的（只是粗略地看过或忘记了）。我不确定我处理这种情况的方式是否比罗洛·马丁斯更好。但我经常试图用这样的想法来安慰自己：那些正在听我讲话的人无疑与我有同样的处境，而且可能并不比我更有信心。

AS A TEACHER, it is my lot more often than average to find myself obligated to speak to a large audience about books I haven’t read, either in the strict sense (having never opened them) or the attenuated sense (having only skimmed them or forgotten them). I am not sure I have dealt with the situation any better than Rollo Martins. But I have often attempted to reassure myself with the thought that those who are listening to me are no doubt on similar ground and are probably no more confident about it than I am.

多年来，我观察到这种情况丝毫不会让我的学生感到不安，他们经常会根据我无意或无意地向他们传达的文本元素，对他们没有读过的书做出不仅相关而且相当准确的评论。为了避免让我工作中的任何人感到尴尬，我将选择一个地理位置遥远但与我们的主题接近的例子：西非的蒂夫部落。

I have observed over the years that this situation in no way unsettles my students, who often comment about books they haven’t read in ways that are not only relevant, but indeed quite accurate, by relying on elements of the text that I have, involuntarily or not, conveyed to them. To avoid embarrassing anyone in my place of employment, I shall choose an example that is geographically remote, to be sure, but close to our subject: that of the Tiv tribe of West Africa.

如果蒂夫人与一般学生不一样的话，那么当一位名叫劳拉·博汉南 (Laura Bohannan) 的人类学家着手向蒂夫人介绍英国戏剧经典《哈姆雷特》1中那部他们从未听说过的经典作品时，蒂夫人中的一群人确实发现自己处于这样的境地。

If the Tiv are not comparable to students in general, a group of them did find themselves in such a position when an anthropologist named Laura Bohannan undertook to acquaint them with that classic entry in the English theatrical canon Hamlet,1 which they had never heard of.

选择莎士比亚的戏剧并非完全出于个人利益。一位英国同事怀疑美国人不懂莎士比亚，而美国人劳拉·博汉南则反驳说，人性在任何地方都是一样的；这位同事向她挑战，要她证明这一点。于是她带着一本《哈姆雷特》去了非洲，希望证明人类在文化差异中本质上是相同的。

The choice of Shakespeare’s play was not entirely disinterested. In response to a British colleague who suspected that Americans did not understand Shakespeare, Laura Bohannan, who is American, had countered that human nature is the same everywhere; he challenged her to prove it. Thus she left for Africa with a copy of Hamlet in her luggage, in the hope of demonstrating that human beings are fundamentally the same across cultural differences.

劳拉·博汉南受到部落的欢迎，她曾经和部落住过，于是在一位博学长老的领地内扎营，这位长老管理着大约 140 人，这些人或多或少都和他有血缘关系。这位人类学家原本希望能够与主人讨论他们仪式的意义，但他们大部分时间都花在喝啤酒上。她独自待在小屋里，专心阅读莎士比亚的戏剧，最终得出了一个在她看来具有普遍性的解释。

Welcomed by the tribe, with whom she had stayed once before, Laura Bohannan set up camp within the territory of a knowledgeable elder, who presided over some 140 people all more or less related to him. The anthropologist had hoped to be able to discuss the meaning of their ceremonies with her hosts, but most of their time was taken up with drinking beer. Isolated in her hut, she devoted herself to reading Shakespeare’s play and eventually came up with an interpretation that seemed to her to be universal.

但蒂芙注意到劳拉·博汉南花了大量时间阅读同一篇文章，并好奇地建议她向他们讲述这个似乎让她如此着迷的故事。他们要求她在阅读过程中提供必要的解释，并承诺会宽容她的语言错误。因此，她获得了一个绝佳的机会来验证她的假设并证明莎士比亚戏剧的普遍性。

But the Tiv noticed that Laura Bohannan was spending a great deal of time reading the same text and, intrigued, suggested that she recount to them this story that seemed to fascinate her so much. They asked her to supply them with the necessary explanations as she went along and promised to be indulgent about her linguistic errors. She was thus given an ideal opportunity to verify her hypothesis and prove the universality of Shakespeare’s play.

不久之后，问题就出现了。在描述戏剧的开头时，博汉南试图解释，一天晚上，三个站在酋长院外守卫的男人突然看到死去的酋长向他们走来。这是第一个引起分歧的根源，因为对于蒂夫人来说，这三个男人所看到的形状不可能是死去的领袖：



It is not long before problems arise. In describing the beginning of the play, Bohannan tries to explain how, one night, three men standing guard outside a chief ’s compound suddenly see the dead chief approaching them. This is the first source of disagreement, because for the Tiv, there is no way the shape perceived by the men can be the dead leader:



“为什么他不再是他们的首领了？”

“Why was he no longer their chief?”

“他死了，”我解释道。“所以他们看到他时才感到不安和害怕。”

“He was dead,” I explained. “That is why they were troubled and afraid when they saw him.”

“不可能，”一位长老开口道，他把烟斗递给邻座，邻座打断道，“当然不是酋长的死。这是女巫发出的预兆。继续说。” 2



“Impossible,” began one of the elders, handing his pipe on to his neighbor, who interrupted, “Of course it wasn’t the dead chief. It was an omen sent by a witch. Go on.”2



博汉南被对话者的自信所震惊，但她还是继续讲述她的故事，并讲述了霍雷肖如何向老哈姆雷特询问如何才能让他安息，以及当死者没有回应时，霍雷肖如何宣布由已故酋长哈姆雷特的儿子来干预。博汉南的听众们听到这里又感到一阵惊讶，因为对于蒂夫人来说，这种事情不是年轻人的事，而是长辈的事，而死者还有一个活着的兄弟克劳迪斯：



Shaken by the self-assurance of her interlocutors, Bohannan nonetheless continues her tale and recounts how Horatio addresses Hamlet the elder to ask him what must be done to give him peace, and how, when the deceased fails to respond, he declares that it is up to the son of the dead chief, Hamlet, to intervene. At this there is a new stir of surprise in Bohannan’s audience, since for the Tiv this kind of matter is not the business of the young, but of the elders, and the deceased has a living brother, Claudius:



老人们嘀咕道：这种预兆是酋长和长老的事，不是年轻人的事；背着酋长做这种事不会有什么好处；显然霍雷肖不是一个深谙世事的人。3



The old men muttered: such omens were matters for chiefs and elders, not for youngsters; no good could come of going behind a chief ’s back; clearly Horatio was not a man who knew things.3



博汉南进一步不安，因为她发现自己无法判断老哈姆雷特和克劳迪斯是否有同一个母亲，而这一区别在蒂夫族人眼中至关重要：



Bohannan is then further disconcerted by finding herself unable to say whether Hamlet the elder and Claudius had the same mother, a distinction that is crucial in the eyes of the Tiv:



“哈姆雷特的父亲和叔叔有同一个母亲吗？”

“Did Hamlet’s father and uncle have one mother?”

他的问题几乎没能深入我的脑海；我太沮丧了，太失衡了，因为《哈姆雷特》中最重要的元素之一被直接排除在外。我犹豫地说，我认为他们有同一个母亲，但我不确定——故事里没有说。老人严厉地告诉我，这些家谱细节很重要，我回家后一定要问长辈们。他冲出门，叫他的一个年轻妻子把他的山羊皮包拿来。4



His question barely penetrated my mind; I was too upset and thrown too far off balance by having one of the most important elements of Hamlet knocked straight out of the picture. Rather uncertainly I said that I thought they had the same mother, but I wasn’t sure—the story didn’t say. The old man told me severely that these genealogical details made all the difference and that when I got home I must ask the elders about it. He shouted out the door to one of his younger wives to bring his goatskin bag.4



博汉南随后将话题转向哈姆雷特的母亲格特鲁德，但情况并没有好转。在西方对这部戏剧的解读中，人们习惯于强调格特鲁德在丈夫去世后再婚的速度有点不雅，但蒂夫人却对她等待了这么长时间感到惊讶：



Bohannan then turns the discussion to Hamlet’s mother, Gertrude, but this goes no better. Whereas in Western readings of the play, it is customary to insist on the slightly indecent rapidity with which Gertrude remarries after the death of her husband, the Tiv are surprised that she waited so long:



“哈姆雷特的儿子非常伤心，因为他的母亲这么快就再婚了。她没有必要这么做，而且我们的习俗是，寡妇要服丧两年才能嫁给下一个丈夫。”

“The son Hamlet was very sad because his mother had married again so quickly. There was no need for her to do so, and it is our custom for a widow not to go to her next husband until she has mourned for two years.”

“两年太长了，”妻子反驳道，她提着老人破旧的山羊皮包出现。“你没有丈夫，谁来帮你锄地？”

“Two years is too long,” objected the wife, who had appeared with the old man’s battered goatskin bag. “Who will hoe your farms for you while you have no husband?”

“哈姆雷特，”我不假思索地反驳道，“他已经长大了，可以自己耕种他母亲的田地。她没有必要再婚。” 看起来没有人相信。我放弃了。5

“Hamlet,” I retorted without thinking, “was old enough to hoe his mother’s farms himself. There was no need for her to remarry.” No one looked convinced. I gave up.5

如果博汉南发现很难向蒂夫人解释哈姆雷特的家庭状况，那么让他们理解鬼魂在莎士比亚戏剧中的地位以及产生该剧的社会就更加困难了：



If Bohannan finds it difficult to explain Hamlet’s family situation to the Tiv, this is even more the case in getting them to understand the place of ghosts in Shakespeare’s play and the society that produced it:



我决定跳过这段独白。即使克劳迪斯娶他哥哥的遗孀是完全正确的，但毒药的情节仍然存在，我知道他们会反对兄弟相残。我满怀希望地继续说道：“那天晚上，哈姆雷特和见过他死去父亲的三个人一起守夜。死去的首领再次出现，尽管其他人都很害怕，但哈姆雷特还是跟着他死去的父亲走到一边。当他们独处时，哈姆雷特死去的父亲说话了。”

I decided to skip the soliloquy. Even if Claudius was here thought quite right to marry his brother’s widow, there remained the poison motif, and I knew they would disapprove of fratricide. More hopefully I resumed, “That night Hamlet kept watch with the three who had seen his dead father. The dead chief again appeared, and although the others were afraid, Hamlet followed his dead father off to one side. When they were alone, Hamlet’s dead father spoke.”

“预兆是不会说话的！”老人强调道。

“Omens can’t talk!” The old man was emphatic.

“哈姆雷特死去的父亲不是预兆。看到他可能是一个预兆，但事实并非如此。”我的听众看起来和我听起来一样困惑。“这是哈姆雷特死去的父亲。这是我们称之为‘鬼魂’的东西。” 6



“Hamlet’s dead father wasn’t an omen. Seeing him might have been an omen, but he was not.” My audience looked as confused as I sounded. “It was Hamlet’s dead father. It was a thing we call a ‘ghost.’ ”6



虽然鬼魂对我们来说很熟悉，但蒂夫人却不相信鬼魂的存在，而且在他们的文化中也没有鬼魂的位置：



As familiar as ghosts are to us, the Tiv do not believe in them and they have no place in their culture:



我不得不使用英语单词，因为与许多邻近的部落不同，这些人不相信人格的任何个体部分在死后会继续存在。

I had to use the English word, for unlike many of the neighboring tribes, these people didn’t believe in the survival after death of any individuating part of the personality.

“‘鬼’是什么？预兆吗？”

“What is a ‘ghost’? An omen?”

“不，‘鬼’是指已经死了但仍能走动、能说话的人，人们能听到他、看到他，却不能触摸他。”

“No, a ‘ghost’ is someone who is dead but who walks around and can talk, and people can hear him and see him but not touch him.”

他们反对道：“僵尸是可以碰的。”

They objected. “One can touch zombis.”

“不，不！那不是女巫们用来献祭和食用的尸体。没有其他人让哈姆雷特死去的父亲行走。是他自己做的。” 7



“No, no! It was not a dead body the witches had animated to sacrifice and eat. No one else made Hamlet’s dead father walk. He did it himself.”7



这种解释根本没有解决问题，因为蒂夫人比盎格鲁撒克逊人更理性，不接受行尸走肉的概念：



This explanation resolves the problem not at all, since the Tiv are more rational than Anglo-Saxons and do not accept the idea of the walking dead:



“死人不能走路。”听众们异口同声地抗议道。

“Dead men can’t walk,” protested my audience as one man.

我倒是愿意妥协。“鬼魂是死人的影子。”

I was quite willing to compromise. “A ‘ghost’ is the dead man’s shadow.”

但他们再次反驳道：“死人不会留下影子。”

But again they objected. “Dead men cast no shadows.”

我厉声说道：“在我的国家，确实有这样的人。”

“They do in my country,” I snapped.

老人平息了立刻出现的怀疑的喋喋不休，并以虚伪但礼貌的同意态度告诉我，这是对年轻、无知和迷信的幻想的一种回应，“毫无疑问，在你们国家，死人也可以行走，而不是僵尸。”他从包里掏出一块枯萎的可乐果，咬掉一端以表明它没有毒，然后把剩下的递给我作为和解的礼物。8

The old man quelled the babble of disbelief that arose immediately and told me with that insincere, but courteous, agreement one extends to the fancies of the young, ignorant, and superstitious, “No doubt in your country the dead can also walk without being zombis.” From the depths of his bag he produced a withered fragment of kola nut, bit off one end to show it wasn’t poisoned, and handed me the rest as a peace offering.8

尽管博汉南做出了种种让步，但整部戏剧仍然没有成功缩小与蒂夫人之间的文化距离，也没有在莎士比亚戏剧的基础上构建出一个她和蒂夫人可以分享的讨论对象。

And despite all the concessions Bohannan makes, the whole play parades by without her succeeding at all in bridging the cultural distance to the Tiv and constructing, based on Shakespeare’s play, a discursive object that she and they can share.

即使蒂夫人从未读过《哈姆雷特》的任何一句台词，他们也能够获得一些关于这部戏剧的具体想法，因此，就像我的学生没有读过我正在讲授的文本一样，他们发现自己完全有能力讨论它并提出他们的意见。

Even if they’ve never read a line of Hamlet, the Tiv are thus able to gain a number of specific ideas about the play, and so, like my students who haven’t read the text I’m lecturing on, they find themselves perfectly capable of discussing it and offering their opinions.

事实上，如果戏剧为他们表达思想提供了一个很好的机会，那么这些思想既不是同时的也不是随后的，因此，到最后，根本不需要它。相反，他们的想法实际上是先于戏剧的，因为他们构成了一个完整而系统的世界观，而书籍在其中被接受并占有一席之地。

Indeed, if the play offers a good occasion for the expression of their ideas, these ideas are neither simultaneous nor subsequent to it and thus do not, at the end of the day, need it at all. Their ideas are instead actually prior, in the sense that they constitute a whole and systematic vision of the world, in which the book is received and given a place.

事实上，收到的甚至不是书本身，而是书的碎片，它们在每一次对话或书面评论中流传，并在书不在的时候代替了书。蒂芙最终谈论的是一个想象中的哈姆雷特。尽管劳拉·博汉南对莎士比亚的戏剧了解得更多，但她的版本却陷入了自己有组织的表述中，因此并不比她们的版本更真实。

In fact it is not even the book that is received, but those fragments of the book that circulate in every conversation or written commentary and come to substitute for it in its absence. What the Tiv end up speaking about is an imaginary Hamlet. And despite her being better informed about Shakespeare’s play, Laura Bohannan’s version is caught up in its own organized set of representations, and thus is no more real than theirs.

我建议用“内在书”这个术语来指代一组神话表征，无论是集体的还是个人的，它们介于读者和任何新作品之间，在读者不知情的情况下塑造了他的阅读。这本想象中的书在很大程度上是无意识的，它充当着一个过滤器，通过选择保留哪些元素以及如何解释这些元素来决定新文本的接受程度。9

I propose the term inner book to designate the set of mythic representations, be they collective or individual, that come between the reader and any new piece of writing, shaping his reading without his realizing it. Largely unconscious, this imaginary book acts as a filter and determines the reception of new texts by selecting which of its elements will be retained and how they will be interpreted.9

从蒂夫族的例子中可以清楚地看出，内书包含一个或多个基础故事，这些故事对持有者具有重要价值，特别是因为它们向持有者讲述了起源和结局。博汉南对莎士比亚的解读与蒂夫族集体内书中包含的关于起源和生存的理论相冲突，而这些理论将蒂夫族凝聚在一起。

As can be seen clearly in the case of the Tiv, the inner book contains one or more foundational stories that have an essential value for its bearer, particularly since they speak to him about origins and endings. Bohannan’s reading of Shakespeare clashes with the theories on origins and survival that are contained in the collective inner book of the Tiv and that serve to bind the group together.

因此，他们听到的并不是《哈姆雷特》的故事，而是故事中符合他们对家庭和死者地位的观念并可能给他们带来安慰的部分。在书中不符合他们期望的地方，令人震惊的段落要么被忽略，要么被转化，使他们内心的书与《哈姆雷特》有最大程度的重叠——或者更确切地说，不是《哈姆雷特》，而是通过另一本内心书的棱镜传递给他们的莎士比亚戏剧的形象。

It is not, then, the story of Hamlet that they hear, but whatever in that story conforms to their notions of the family and the status of the dead and might serve to comfort them. In the places where the book does not conform to their expectations, the alarming passages are either ignored, or they undergo a transformation that allows the largest possible overlap between their inner book and Hamlet—or rather, not Hamlet, but the image transmitted to them of Shakespeare’s play through the prism of another inner book.

由于他们没有讨论博汉南想要讨论的作品，蒂芙人不需要直接接触它。人类学家设法传达给他们的对《哈姆雷特》的引用足以让他们参与两本内部书籍之间的辩论——在这场辩论中，莎士比亚的戏剧为双方提供了一个借口。

Since they are not discussing the work that Bohannan wants to talk to them about, the Tiv have no need for direct access to it. The references to Hamlet that the anthropologist manages to convey to them are sufficient to allow them to participate in a debate between two inner books—a debate in which Shakespeare’s play serves both sides as, more than anything else, a pretext.

而且，由于他们主要谈论的是他们内心的书，他们对莎士比亚的评论，就像我的学生在类似情况下的评论一样，很可能在他们获得对这部作品的任何了解之前就开始了——无论如何，这部作品本身注定会融化并逐渐消失在内心的书中。

And since they are speaking primarily about their inner book, their comments on Shakespeare, like those of my students in similar circumstances, can very well begin before they acquire any knowledge of the work—which is itself, in any event, destined to melt and gradually disappear into the inner book.

就蒂夫族而言，内心的书本更具集体性而非个人性。它由一般的文化表征构成，这些表征不仅基于家庭关系和来世的共同观念，还基于阅读、如何恰当地阅读一本书以及如何在现实与想象之间划清界限等共同观念。

In the case of the Tiv, the inner book is more collective than individual. It is made up of general cultural representations that draw upon common ideas not only of family relations and the afterlife, but also of reading, how one appropriately approaches a book, and how, for example, to draw the line between reality and imagination.

除了年长的领袖，我们对蒂夫族的个体成员一无所知，而且，群体的凝聚力往往会统一他们的反应，这种说法似乎很有道理。但是，尽管每种文化似乎都存在一本集体的内心书，但集体的每个成员也都存在一本个人的内心书，它在文化对象的接受（即构建）中同样（如果不是更积极的话）活跃。

We know nothing about the individual members of the Tiv, aside from their elderly leader, and it is plausible that the cohesion of the group tends to unify their reactions. But although a collective inner book would seem to exist for every culture, there also exists, for each member of the collective, an individual inner book, which is equally (if not more) active in the reception—which is to say, the construction—of cultural objects.

每个人内心的书都是由个人的幻想和私人神话编织而成的，它影响着我们的读书欲望，也就是我们寻找和阅读书籍的方式。它是每个读者一生追求的幻影般的事物，他一生中遇到的最好的书只是其中不完美的片段，迫使他继续阅读。

Woven from the fantasies and private mythologies particular to each person, the individual inner book is at work in our desire to read—that is, in the way we seek out and read books. It is that phantasmagorical object that every reader lives to pursue, of which the best books he encounters in his life will be but imperfect fragments, compelling him to continue reading.

我们还可以进一步推测，每个作家都试图发现并塑造自己内心的书，并永远对自己遇到的实际书籍感到不满，包括他自己的书，无论它们多么精致。事实上，如果没有完美书籍的理想形象（即与我们自己相符的书籍），我们如何开始写作或继续写作？我们无休止地寻找并不断接近，但永远无法实现完美书籍的理想形象。

We might further speculate that every writer is driven by the attempt to discover and give form to his inner book and is perpetually dissatisfied with the actual books he encounters, including his own, however polished they may be. How indeed might we begin to write, or continue doing so, without that ideal image of a perfect book—one congruent to ourselves, that is—which we endlessly seek and constantly approach, but never reach?

就像集体内部书籍一样，个人内部书籍也创建了一个接收其他文本的系统，并参与接收和重组。从这个意义上说，它们形成了一种网格，我们通过它来阅读世界，尤其是书籍，组织我们感知这些文本的方式，同时产生透明的幻觉。

Like collective inner books, individual inner books create a system for receiving other texts and participate both in their reception and their reorganization. In this sense, they form a kind of grid through which we read the world, and books in particular, organizing the way we perceive these texts while producing the illusion of transparency.

正是这些内在的书籍使得我们关于书籍的交流变得如此困难，使得我们无法就讨论对象达成一致意见。它们是我在《哈姆雷特》研究中所说的内在范式的一部分——一种感知现实的系统，它是如此独特，以至于没有两个范式能够真正交流。10

It is these inner books that make our exchanges about books so difficult, rendering it impossible to establish unanimity about the object of discussion. They are part of what I have called, in my study of Hamlet, an inner paradigm—a system for perceiving reality that is so idiosyncratic that no two paradigms can truly communicate.10

内在书籍的存在，以及不读或遗忘，使得我们讨论书籍的方式如此不连续和异质。我们认为自己读过的书实际上是文本碎片的异常积累，经过我们的想象重新加工，与他人的书毫无关联，即使这些书与我们手中的书在实质上完全相同。

The existence of the inner book, along with unreading or forgetting, is what makes the way we discuss books so discontinuous and heterogeneous. What we take to be the books we have read is in fact an anomalous accumulation of fragments of texts, reworked by our imagination and unrelated to the books of others, even if these books are materially identical to ones we have held in our hands.

蒂夫族提供的至少是他们没有读过的书的部分阅读，但这并不意味着他们的阅读是讽刺性的——因为它强调了阅读的每个行为的特点——或者没有兴趣。恰恰相反，蒂夫族与莎士比亚作品的双重外在性（他们没有读过莎士比亚的作品，而且他们来自不同的文化）使他们处于讨论莎士比亚作品的特权地位。他们拒绝相信鬼故事，接近莎士比亚批评中少数派——但活跃的——的立场，这种立场对哈姆雷特父亲的再次出现表示怀疑，并暗示这位英雄可能患有幻觉。11这个假设是异端的，但至少值得研究，在这种情况下，蒂夫族与戏剧的陌生性促成了这种情况。不了解文本——以两种不同的方式——反而会让他们更直接地接触文本，当然，不是接触文本所谓的普遍真理，而是接触文本众多潜在财富之一。

That what the Tiv offer is, to say the least, a partial reading of a book they have not read should not lead us to believe either that their reading is a caricature—for it underscores the characteristics of every act of reading—or that it is without interest. Quite to the contrary, the double exteriority of the Tiv in relation to Shakespeare’s work (they haven’t read it and they are from a different culture) places them in a privileged position to discuss it. In refusing to believe in the ghost story, they approach the position of a minority trend—but an active one—in Shakespearean criticism, which casts doubt on the reappearance of Hamlet’s father and suggests that the hero may have been suffering hallucinations.11 The hypothesis is heterodox, but is at the least deserving of examination, a circumstance facilitated in this case by the foreignness of the Tiv to the play. Not knowing the text—in two different ways—paradoxically gives them more direct access, not, to be sure, to its supposed universal truth, but to one of its many potential riches.

因此，回到我在本章开头提到的情况，我的学生即使没有读过我正在讨论的这本书，也能很快掌握其中的某些内容，并根据他们的文化观念和个人经历自由地对其进行评论，这并不奇怪。同样不足为奇的是，他们的评论——无论与最初的文本相差多远（但事实上，接近又意味着什么呢？）——都为这次相遇带来了一种独创性，如果他们读这本书，他们无疑会缺乏这种独创性。



Thus, to return to the situation I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter, it is not astonishing that my students, without having read the book I am discussing, quickly grasp certain of its elements and feel free to comment on it, based on their cultural notions and personal history. And it is also unsurprising that their comments—however far removed from the initial text (but what, in fact, might it mean to be close?)—bring to the encounter an originality that they would undoubtedly have lacked had they undertaken to read the book.

9 .内心书是本文研究的三本“书”中的第二本，它影响着我们对书籍进行的所有转化，将其变成屏幕书。内心书一词在普鲁斯特的作品中出现的意义与我赋予它的意义相近：“至于那本充满未知符号的内心书（它们可能是浮雕的符号，我的注意力在探索我的潜意识时，摸索着、偶然发现并追随它们的轮廓，就像潜水员探索海底一样），如果我试图阅读它们，没有人能给我提供任何规则，因为阅读它们是一种创造行为，没有人能替我们做工作，甚至没有人能与我们合作[...]这本书比其他任何书都更难解读，也是唯一一本由现实强加给我们的书，唯一一本由现实本身在我们身上印上‘印象’的书。”《重现的时光》，《追忆似水年华》，第一卷。 3，由 CK Scott Moncrieff、Terence Kilmartin 和 Andreas Mayor 译（纽约：兰登书屋，1981 年），第 913-14 页。

9. The second of the three “books” studied in this essay, the inner book influences all the transformations to which we subject books, turning them into screen books. The term inner book appears in Proust with a meaning close to the one I am giving it: “As for the inner book of unknown symbols (symbols carved in relief they might have been, which my attention, as it explored my unconscious, groped for and stumbled against and followed the contours of, like a diver exploring the ocean-bed), if I tried to read them, no one could help me with any rules, for to read them was an act of creation in which no one can do our work for us or even collaborate with us [ . . . ] This book, more laborious to decipher than any other, is also the only one which has been dictated to us by reality, the only one of which the ‘impression’ has been printed in us by reality itself.” Time Regained, Remembrance of Things Past, vol. 3, translated by C. K. Scott Moncrieff, Terence Kilmartin, and Andreas Mayor (New York: Random House, 1981), pp. 913–14.

VII

与作家的邂逅

VII

Encounters with the Writer

（皮埃尔·西尼亚克证明，在作家面前注意自己的言行很重要，尤其是当他本人没有读过他所著的书时）

(in which Pierre Siniac demonstrates that it may be important to watch what you say in the presence of a writer, especially when he himself hasn’t read the book whose author he is)

当你不一定了解你谈论的那本书时，遇到一个比老师更糟糕的人——这个人最关心你对某本书的看法，也最有可能知道你读过这本书是否属实。这个人就是这本书的作者，人们认为他自己读过这本书。

WHEN YOU DO NOT necessarily know the book you’re talking about, there is a person even worse to encounter than a teacher—the person at once the most interested in your opinion of a particular book, and the most likely to know whether you are telling the truth about having read it. This person is the author of the book, who is assumed a priori to have read the book himself.

有人可能会认为，只有运气极差的人才会遇到这种情况。事实上，许多人一辈子不读书，却从未遇到过一位作家，更不用说他们假装没有读过某本书的作者这种特殊情况了。

One might think that you would have to have a stroke of incredible bad luck to find yourself in such a situation. Indeed, many people spend a whole lifetime of non-reading without encountering a single writer, never mind the exceptional case of the author of a book they haven’t read while pretending the contrary.

但一切都取决于你的职业背景。文学评论家经常与作家接触——当然，这两个群体重叠的情况更是如此。鉴于这两个群体通常包括相同的人，评论家生活在一个如此孤立的世界中，以至于在评论一本书时，他们几乎别无选择，只能将其大加赞扬。

But everything depends on your professional context. Literary critics regularly come into contact with writers—all the more so, of course, in that the two groups overlap. Given that both groups often include the same people, critics move within a world so insular that in commenting on a book, they have hardly any other choice than to praise it to the skies.

不幸的是，大学教授也是如此。事实上，我的同事中很少有人不出版作品，也不觉得有义务把书寄给我。因此，每年我都处于一种微妙的境地，需要向那些熟悉自己作品的作者发表意见，而且他们还是经验丰富的评论家，能够熟练地评估我在多大程度上真正读过这些书，以及我在多大程度上是在虚张声势。

Such is also the case, to my misfortune, with university professors. Very few of my colleagues, in fact, do not publish and do not feel obliged to send me their books. Every year I thus find myself in the delicate situation of giving my opinion to authors who know their own texts and who are, moreover, experienced critics, skilled in evaluating to what extent I have actually read the books, and to what extent I am bluffing.

皮埃尔·西尼亚克 (Pierre Siniac) 的著名惊悚小说《费尔迪诺·塞利纳( Ferdinaud Céline) 1》中两位主人公所著书籍的公众评论，最好用“模棱两可”这个词来形容。在小说的开篇，畅销书《棕色的爪哇(La Java brune ) 2》的两位作者多钦 (Dochin) 和加斯蒂内尔 (Gastinel ) 作为嘉宾出现在一档文学电视节目中，在与主持人的交流中，他们表现得相当奇怪。他们似乎都不愿意回答关于这本书的问题，这本书本应给他们带来快乐，因为它为他们赚了一大笔钱，并邀请他们上电视。

The public remarks about books made by the two heroes of Ferdinaud Céline,1 Pierre Siniac’s celebrated thriller, might best be described with the word ambiguous. In the opening pages of the novel, Dochin and Gastinel, the two authors of the best seller La Java brune,2 appear as guests on a literary television program and behave rather strangely, to say the least, in their exchanges with the host. It is as though they both prefer not to answer the questions they are being asked about a book that ought to be a source of nothing but joy for them, since it has earned them a fortune and gotten them invited on television.

两位作者中较为年轻且体格瘦弱的让-雷米·多钦 (Jean-Rémi Dochin) 在直播中显得明显不自在：



The younger and physically slighter of the two authors, Jean-Rémi Dochin, seems manifestly ill at ease during the broadcast:



而多钦则越来越昏昏欲睡，完全失去了意识。他似乎跟不上。在镜头前，他似乎犹豫不决、不自在，几乎从未完成他能说的几句话。3



Dochin, for his part, seemed more and more to be falling asleep, completely out of it. He seemed to be having trouble following. Before the cameras, he seemed hesitant, uncomfortable, almost never completing the few sentences he managed to say.3



事实证明，多钦有充分的理由出现在他自己的书上，用叙述者的话来说，是“茫然不知所措” 。他被剥夺了那本据说是他与加斯蒂内尔合著的书，加斯蒂内尔体格魁梧，而他的同伴却身材苗条，加斯蒂内尔强行将自己的名字与多钦的名字一起印在了封面上。

It turns out Dochin has an excellent reason to appear, in the narrator’s words, “more than at sea”4 on the subject of his own book. He has been dispossessed of the book that he has supposedly cowritten by Gastinel, who is as physically imposing as his companion is slender, and who has forced his own name onto the cover with Dochin’s.

作家多钦最初联系加斯蒂内尔，希望他能成为出版商。加斯蒂内尔读了手稿后，立即确信自己将获得巨大成功。他决心以合著者的身份将自己的名字写在书上，尽管他一个字也没写。为了迫使多钦同意，加斯蒂内尔决定敲诈他。为了实现这个目标，他在舞会上勾引了一个女孩，然后把她和多钦带到他的乡间别墅，把多钦灌醉。在强奸了这名年轻女子并用汽车碾压她之后，他拍摄了多钦俯身看着她尸体的画面，并在尸体上偷偷植入了这位作家的身份证明。

Originally approached by the writer Dochin as a possible publisher, Gastinel read the manuscript and immediately became convinced he had a huge success on his hands; he became determined to put his own name on the book as coauthor, despite not having written a word. To force Dochin to consent, Gastinel decided to blackmail him. With this goal in mind, he seduced a girl at a dance, then took her to his country house along with Dochin, whom he got drunk. After raping the young woman and running her over with his car, he filmed Dochin bending over her corpse, on which he had discreetly planted the writer’s ID.

根据加斯蒂内尔严密保管的一盘录音带，多钦一直面临被指控谋杀的威胁，他没有犯下谋杀罪，但他却默许谋杀发生，没有干预。他发现自己被迫遵从敲诈者的意愿，作为对他保持沉默的交换，敲诈者夺走了他作为这本书合著者的权利，并把一半的版税收入囊中。

Based on a tape closely guarded by Gastinel, Dochin is thus under constant threat of being accused of a murder he didn’t commit, but which he allowed to happen without intervening. He finds himself forced to abide by the wishes of his blackmailer, who has, in exchange for his silence, appropriated the right to be credited as coauthor of the book and to pocket half the royalties.

虽然对加斯蒂内尔来说，声称拥有其他作家的手稿或谋杀似乎并不构成多大道德问题，但他仍然不愿意向众多观众谈论这本书。因此，他要求节目主持人保证不提及这本书的内容，而加斯蒂内尔在问题变得具体到足以构成威胁时就提醒了他这一承诺：



Though neither laying claim to another writer’s manuscript nor committing a murder seems to pose much of a moral problem to Gastinel, he is nonetheless uncomfortable at the thought of speaking about the book to a large audience. He has therefore exacted a pledge from the program’s host not to mention the contents of the book, a promise of which Gastinel reminds him as soon as the questions get specific enough to present a threat:



“别忘了我们在节目开始前达成的小协议。Dochin 和我都不想泄露我们小说的情节。所以，如果你不介意的话，我们还是谈谈作者吧。归根结底，我认为这才是观众感兴趣的。” 5



“Don’t forget the little deal we made before the program. Dochin and I do not in any way want to give away the plot of our novel. So, if you don’t mind, let’s talk about the authors instead. At bottom, I think that’s what your viewers are interested in anyway.”5



加斯蒂内尔的行为更令人惊讶，因为他对二人组后续著作（尚未完成的《棕色的爪哇》续集）的话题滔滔不绝，甚至公开讲述了其中的几个情节。至少在多钦面前，加斯蒂内尔显然不可能谈论多钦的作品。

Gastinel’s behavior is even more surprising in that he is quite eloquent on the subject of the duo’s follow-up book, the as yet unwritten sequel to La Java brune, to the point of publicly recounting several of its episodes. What is clearly out of the question, at least in the presence of Dochin, is for Gastinel to speak about Dochin’s work.

事实证明，加斯蒂内尔的谨慎是完全合理的。他不愿意谈论这本书，并不是因为他没有读过这本书，就像我们遇到的许多其他人物一样；而是因为多钦虽然是这本书的作者，却没有读过这本书。实际上，西尼亚克的小说构建了一个不太可能的情况，其中一个所谓的合著者在谈论一本他读过但没写过的书，而另一个人在谈论一本他写过但没读过的书。

As it turns out, Gastinel’s discretion is completely justified. That he prefers not to speak about the book is not due to not having read it, like many other characters we have encountered; it is because Dochin, who is nevertheless the book’s author, has not read it. In effect, Siniac’s novel constructs an unlikely situation in which one supposed coauthor is speaking about a book he has read without having written it, while the other is speaking about a book he has written but hasn’t read.

要真正理解这两个角色在第一幕中所处的境况，读者必须知道，多钦并不是一个陷阱的受害者——加斯蒂内尔勒索版税——而是两个陷阱的受害者，第二个陷阱只在小说的最后几页中揭示，并在事后加以阐释。第一个陷阱解释了多钦奇怪的态度，而只有在发现第二个陷阱时，我们才能理解加斯蒂内尔的态度。

To truly understand the situation in which the two characters find themselves during this first scene, the reader must know that Dochin is not the victim of just one trap— Gastinel’s blackmail to appropriate royalties—but of two, the second of which is revealed only in the novel’s final pages and which illuminates it retrospectively. Whereas the first trap explains Dochin’s strange attitude, only in discovering the second one do we come to understand Gastinel’s.

在撰写《Java brune》手稿时，当时没有固定住址的多钦被一家破旧旅馆的女主人塞琳·费迪诺 (Céline Ferdinaud) 收留。塞琳刚开始阅读文本，就被热情所淹没，并敦促多钦完成并出版它。她甚至主动提出提供实际帮助，重新打印多钦每天交给她的那些打字很差的页面。

While he was working on the manuscript of Java brune, Dochin, who at the time had no permanent address, was taken in by Céline Ferdinaud, the madam of a seedy hotel. Having barely begun to read the text, Céline was overcome with enthusiasm and urged Dochin to complete and publish it. She even offered to help on a practical level, by retyping the poorly typed pages that Dochin gave her each day.

问题在于，塞利纳利用这份秘书工作的机会，写了一部完全不同的小说，并逐渐用它取代了多钦的小说，只保留了标题、故事发生的时期和两个儿童主角的名字。日复一日，她用自己精心编写的文字取代了多钦写得不好、无法出版的文字。

The problem is that Céline seized the opportunity of this secretarial work to write a completely different novel, which she gradually substituted for Dochin’s, retaining only the title, the period during which the story took pace, and the first names of the two child protagonists. Day by day, she replaced Dochin’s poorly written and unpublishable pages with a much more carefully composed text of her own.

这个计谋的目的是什么？塞琳·费迪诺这个名字实际上是占领时期臭名昭著的合作者塞琳·费昂特的化名。为了勒索一些已经和平恢复生活的著名合作者，塞琳决定出版她虚构的回忆录。但在解放时，她同意不再引起人们的注意，以换取免责的承诺。由于无法按原样出版这本书，以免被人认出，她发现了房客的三流手稿，并突然想到以他的名义出版自己的书，而作者——如果我们可以这样称呼他的话——却没有意识到这一点。

What is the point of this stratagem? The name Céline Ferdinaud is in fact an alias for a notorious collaborator in the Occupation, Céline Feuhant. With an eye to blackmailing a number of prominent fellow collaborators who had peacefully resumed their lives, Céline had decided to publish her fictionalized memoirs. But at the Liberation she had agreed, in exchange for a promise of impunity, to desist from calling attention to herself. Unable to publish the book as it was lest she be recognized, she discovered her lodger’s third-rate manuscript and hit upon the idea of publishing her own book under his name, without the author—if we can call him that—realizing it.

因此，两篇同名文本在西尼亚克的小说中不断流传，相互替代。多钦和读者一样，不明白他自己的文本——他完全正确地认为它是可恶的——怎么会激起整个批评界的热情，事实上，批评界已经得到了塞利纳撰写的另一份手稿。因此，在整个诡计期间，参与阴谋的加斯蒂内尔在多钦面前谈论这本书时倾向于尽可能含糊其辞，这样多钦就不会发现引起所有兴奋的那本书是他从未读过的。

Thus two texts bearing the same title continually circulate throughout Siniac’s novel, each by turns substituting for the other. Dochin, like the reader, fails to understand how his own text—which he quite rightly judges to be execrable— could have aroused the enthusiasm of the entire critical community, which has, in fact, been given the other manuscript, written by Céline. For the duration of the ruse, then, Gastinel, who is in on the plot, is inclined to remain as vague as possible when speaking of the book in Dochin’s presence, so that Dochin will not find out that the book causing all the excitement is one he has never read.

因此，多钦不得不谈论一本他不认识的书，尽管他相信自己是这本书的作者。与罗洛·马丁斯不同，罗洛·马丁斯知道自己谈论的不是与听众相同的作者，而多钦不知道自己正在参与一场聋哑人的对话，因为加斯蒂内尔竭尽全力（包括没有给他一本书等）阻止多钦发现《棕色的爪哇》不是《棕色的爪哇》。

Dochin thus finds himself in the position of having to speak about a book that is unknown to him, although he believes himself to be its author. Unlike Rollo Martins, who knew that he was not speaking about the same author as the members of his audience, Dochin has no idea he is participating in a dialogue of the deaf, since Gastinel is doing his best (failing to give him a copy of his book, among other measures) to prevent Dochin from discovering that La Java brune is not La Java brune.

对于加斯蒂内尔来说，广播中的评论尽可能含糊不清是至关重要的——他与观众读的是同一本书，但他必须不惜一切代价阻止他的搭档说得太露骨，以免主持人的反应让多钦知道手稿被替换了。他的解决方案之一是坚持谈论文本以外的内容，例如作者的生活或他们的下一本书。

It is essential for Gastinel—who has read the same book as his audience, but who must at any cost prevent his partner from being too explicit, lest the host’s reaction tip Dochin off to the substitution of the manuscript—that the comments made during the broadcast be as ambiguous as possible. One of his solutions is to insist on speaking of something other than the text, such as the lives of the authors or their next book.

加斯蒂内尔的另一个选择是确保讨论只涉及两本书所共有的文本的几个表面方面。占领时期是这两部作品的背景，也是塞利纳在《棕色爪哇》版本中保留的两个儿童英雄马克斯和米米尔的背景：



Another option for Gastinel is to make sure that the discussion touches only on the few superficial aspects of the text that are shared by the two books. This is the case for the Occupation period that serves as a backdrop for both works, as well as for the two child heroes, Max and Mimile, whom Céline has made sure to retain in her version of La Java brune:



[主人] 冲了回来：显然，他非常想谈论这部小说。加斯蒂内尔拒绝了他，但在叹了一口气后，他还是同意谈论这部作品……于是，大家同意谈论马克斯和米米尔的人物，但这并不会损害他们的利益，他们仍然执着于不泄露情节。于是这位肥胖的作者以权威的口吻，仿佛他自己就是讨论的主持人，将讨论引向了巴黎的占领、突袭、限制、库存不足的商店前的排队、宵禁、墙上张贴的人质名单、匿名举报以及那四年漫长岁月中每天的苦难。这样做也没有什么不妥，因为这种压抑、阴郁的氛围是这本书的永恒背景。6



[The host] came charging back: he was dying, it was clear, to talk about the novel. Gastinel rebuffed him, then consented, all the same, after emitting a declamatory sigh, to say two or three words on the work [ . . . ] It was thus agreed to say two or three little things—which were not at all compromising, there was still this obsession with not giving away the plot—about the Max and Mimile characters, whereupon the portly author directed the discussion authoritatively, as though he himself were the host of the discussion, to the Occupation in Paris in general, the raids, the restrictions, the lines in front of the poorly stocked shops, the curfew, the lists of hostages posted on the walls, the anonymous denunciations, and the entire litany of daily miseries of those four interminable years. There was nothing inappropriate in doing so, besides, since this oppressive, lugubrious atmosphere was the constant backdrop for the book.6



对于加斯蒂内尔来说，这些关于两个孩子或两部作品所共有背景的概括性描述是唯一安全的领域。在少数情况下，当对话变得不那么模糊时，多钦和节目主持人之间开始产生误解，加斯蒂内尔不得不介入，提供足够模糊的评论，让双方都感到安心：



For Gastinel, these generalities about the two children or the setting shared by the two works are the only safe territory. On the few occasions when the conversation does become less vague, incomprehension starts to blossom between Dochin and the program host, and Gastinel is obliged to intervene, offering comments that are ambiguous enough to set both parties at ease:



“你将会为自己树敌。”

“You’re going to make yourself enemies.”

“那就更好了——我们喜欢一场精彩的战斗。无论如何，自从我们成功以来，我们已经得到了应有的回报。我们甚至拒绝了一些。”

“So much the better—we love a good fight. In any event, since our success we’ve already had our share. We’ve even turned away a few.”

“对当时某些著名人物的提及……有时会产生很深远的影响……”

“The references to . . . certain people in prominence at the time . . . go pretty far, at moments . . .”

“我可不这么认为，”多钦说道。“你肯定看错了。”

“That’s not at all my opinion,” said Dochin. “You must have misread.”

“我们从来不会真的攻击别人，”加斯蒂内尔说。“最多也就是偷偷地戳几下而已。” 7



“We never really attack people,” said Gastinel. “No more than, say, a few discreet jabs.”7



加斯蒂内尔面临的问题是，他必须找到既适合多钦读过的书（他写的书）又适合主持人不熟悉的书的短语，以及主持人手中的书（多钦不知道这本书的存在）。多钦的手稿没有表现出让新近受人尊敬的前合作者的事情复杂化的兴趣，而塞利纳的手稿则是对她以前的同伙的全面攻击。从弗洛伊德的角度来看，“谨慎的攻击”这个表达是节目中同时讨论的两本书之间的妥协形式。因此，在数百万观众面前，加斯蒂内尔发现自己正在编写一本联合书籍的片段，这本书可能为双方提供可接受的和解，每个读者都可以在其中找到自己的文本。

The problem facing Gastinel is that he has to find phrases simultaneously befitting the book Dochin has read—the one he wrote—with which the program host is unfamiliar, and the book that the host has in his hands, whose existence is unknown to Dochin. Whereas Dochin’s manuscript shows no interest in complicating matters for newly respectable ex-collaborators, Céline’s is a full-blown attack on her former accomplices. The expression “discreet jabs” is a compromise formation, in the Freudian sense, between the two books being discussed simultaneously on the program. So it is that live, in front of millions of viewers, Gastinel finds himself compiling fragments of a joint book that might offer an acceptable reconciliation to both parties, within which each reader will be able to identify his own text.

但这位电视主持人并不是唯一一个在与多钦进行连贯对话时遇到困难的人。塞利纳和其他评论家也遇到了同样的问题，他们不断与他谈论这本他难以在书中认出自己的书。

But the television host is not the only one experiencing difficulties in having a coherent conversation with Dochin. The same holds for Céline and for other critics, who talk to him constantly about a book in which he finds it hard to recognize himself.

不幸的是，塞琳每天都要打字，因此她很熟悉多钦的书，她无法告诉他她对这本书的真实看法，只能和他谈论一本他难以将其叠加到自己作品中的虚构书籍。塞琳在抄写手稿时表现出的狂热评论令他目瞪口呆，这些评论在他看来似乎有点不着边际，因为她实际上是在自言自语：



If Céline, to her misfortune, is familiar with Dochin’s book, having been obliged to type it out daily, she can’t tell him what she really thinks of it and is forced to talk to him about an imaginary book that he has difficulty superimposing onto his own. He is stupefied by Céline’s wildly enthusiastic observations during the period when she is transcribing the manuscript, remarks that understandably seem a bit off the mark to him in that she is really addressing herself:



“坦白说，这对我来说是个幸运的时刻。现在很难找到一个好的作家。所有伟大的作家都离开了……再也没有回来！‘我把我的书留给你们——好好享受吧！’塞利纳……阿拉贡……吉奥诺……贝克特……亨利·米勒……更不用说马塞尔了……当我想到有些句子被划掉，甚至无法再辨认，因为你用笔把一切都浸透了！当我奇迹般地读到你删掉的东西时，我惊呆了。你删掉了真正的宝石！我开始好奇，当你把所有这些都删掉的时候，你到底在想什么。”

“Frankly, this is a lucky time for me. It’s so hard to find a good writer, especially these days. All the great ones have taken leave . . . and never returned! ‘I leave you my books—enjoy!’ Céline . . . Aragon . . . Giono . . . Beckett . . . Henry Miller . . . Not to mention Marcel [ . . . ] And when I think that there are crossed out sentences that can no longer even be deciphered because you’ve drenched everything with strokes of your pen! When by some miracle I manage to read what you’ve slashed out, I’m dumbfounded. You’ve eliminated true gems! I start wondering what you could possibly have been thinking when you got rid of all that.”

我嘴角露出的微笑一定表达了一种愤怒的怀疑。

The smile beginning to form on my lips must have expressed an outraged skepticism.

“一个小问题：你确定你读过我的手稿吗？” 8



“One small question: are you sure you read my manuscript?”8



这段文字中讽刺性地描述了所有作家都熟悉的经历，他们意识到关于他们作品的评价与他们认为自己写的内容不符。每一个与细心的读者进行过长时间交谈的作家，或者读过一篇关于自己的长篇文章的作家，都有过一种不可思议的经历，那就是发现自己想要完成的事情和读者对这件事的理解之间没有任何联系。这种脱节并不令人惊讶；因为他们内心的书在定义上是不同的，读者在书上叠加的书不太可能让作家感到熟悉。

What is being described in this passage to the point of caricature is an experience familiar to all writers, in which they realize that what is said about their books does not correspond to what they believe they have written. Every writer who has conversed at any length with an attentive reader, or read an article of any length about himself, has had the uncanny experience of discovering the absence of any connection between what he meant to accomplish and what has been grasped of it. There is nothing astonishing in this disjuncture; since their inner books differ by definition, the one the reader has superimposed on the book is unlikely to seem familiar to the writer.

对于不了解你书的意图的读者来说，这种体验已经够不愉快的了，但当读者是善意的，欣赏这本书，并在开始详细谈论它时变得热情洋溢时，这种体验可能反而更痛苦。在热情中，他诉诸于他最熟悉的词语，这并没有让他更接近作者的书，而是让他更接近自己的理想书，这对他与语​​言和他人的关系至关重要，它是独一无二的，无法用任何其他词语来表达。在这种情况下，作者的幻灭感可能更加明显，因为它源于发现我们与他人之间存在着深不可测的距离。

This experience is unpleasant enough with a reader who has not understood your book’s project, but it is perhaps paradoxically more painful when the reader is well-intentioned and appreciates the book and grows passionate when he begins talking about it in detail. In his enthusiasm, he resorts to the words most familiar to him, and instead of this bringing him closer to the writer’s book, it brings him closer to his own ideal book, which is so crucial to his relation to language and to others that it is unique, and not transcribable into any other words. In this case, the author’s disillusionment may be even more pronounced, since it arises from the discovery of the unfathomable distance that separates us from others.

有人可能会说，当我们喜欢某本书时，谈论作者的著作伤害作者的可能性就更大。除了一般的满意表达往往会产生一种共同点感之外，我们试图更精确地阐述我们为什么喜欢这本书，这很可能会使他士气低落。在这种尝试中，我们迫使他突然面对对方身上不可化约的一切，因此他自己和他试图表达自己的词语中也是不可化约的。

It might then be said that the chances of wounding an author by speaking about his book are all the greater when we love it. Beyond the general expressions of satisfaction that tend to create a sense of common ground, there is every likelihood that trying to be more precise in our exposition of why we appreciated the book will be demoralizing for him. In the attempt, we force him into an abrupt confrontation with everything that is irreducible in the other, and thus irre- ducible in him and in the words through which he has attempted to express himself.

在西尼亚克的书中，这种痛苦的不理解体验因作家认为自己写的书与其他人认为自己读过的书之间存在的真正分离而加剧，因为在这种情况下，有两本实质上不同的书。但除了表面的吸引力之外，正是作家内心的书与读者内心的书之间无法沟通的危机在这里以一种近乎寓言的方式展现出来。

In Siniac’s book, this painful experience of incomprehension is heightened by the real dissociation between the book the writer believes he has written and the one the others believe they have read, since in this instance there are two materially distinct books. But beyond the surface intrigue, it is indeed this crisis of impossible communication between the writer’s inner book and those of his readers that is played out here, in an almost allegorical manner.

因此，西尼亚克的小说中对双重性问题的痴迷并不令人意外。多钦是双重性过程的参与者，因为他无法从别人对他的书的评价中认出自己，就像其他人的评论常常让作家觉得他们正在处理的是另一种文本（事实上确实如此）。双重性是由我们内心的书的存在产生的，它不能传递给任何人，也不能叠加在别人身上。对于内心的书来说，一切让我们绝对独特的东西的表现都是我们内心无法传达的东西本身的表达。9

It’s unsurprising, therefore, that the question of the double is such an obsession in Siniac’s novel. Dochin is a participant in a process of doubling in that he does not recognize himself in what others say about his book, just as other people’s comments often make writers feel that they are dealing with a text that is other (which is effectively the case). The doubling is produced by the presence in us of the inner book, which can be transmitted to no one and superimposed on no other. For the inner book, the manifestation of everything that makes us absolutely unique is the expression within us of the incommunicable itself.9

那么，当我们面对作家本人时，我们该怎么办呢？当我们遇到一本我们从未读过的书的作者时，乍一看似乎是最棘手的情况，因为作者被认为熟悉他所写的内容，但最后我们发现这是最简单的情况。

What, then, are we to do when facing the writer himself? The case of the encounter with the author of a book we haven’t read at first seems to be the thorniest case, since the author is assumed to be familiar with what he wrote, but it is revealed in the end to be the simplest of all.

首先，与你的预期相反，作家是否最有资格谈论他的书或准确记住它，这一点并不明显。蒙田的例子无法确定他被引用的情况，这证明在我们写完一篇文章并脱离它之后，我们可能和其他人一样远离它。

First, it is far from evident, despite what you would expect, that the writer is in the best position either to speak about his book or to remember it precisely. The example of Montaigne, unable to identify the cases in which he is being quoted, serves as evidence that after we write a text and are separated from it, we may be as far from it as others are.

其次，也是最重要的一点，如果两个人的内心世界确实无法重合，那么在面对作家时，长篇大论的解释是毫无意义的。当我们讨论他写的东西时，他的焦虑可能会加剧，同时他也会觉得我们在和他谈论另一本书，或者我们找错了人。他甚至有可能经历真正的非人格化体验，因为他面临着一个人与另一个人之间巨大的差异。

But second and most especially, if it is true that the inner books of two individuals cannot coincide, it is useless to plunge into long explanations when faced with a writer. His anxiety is likely to grow as we discuss what he has written, along with his sense that we are talking to him about another book or that we have the wrong person. And he is even in danger of undergoing a genuine experience of depersonalization, confronted as he is with the enormity of what separates one individual from another.

可以看出，对于那些不得不与作者谈论他的作品而又未读过的人，只有一条明智的建议：赞美而不详述。作者并不期望对他的作品进行总结或理性分析，甚至不希望你尝试这样做。他只希望你在保持最大程度的模糊性的同时告诉他你喜欢他写的东西。



As may be seen, there is only one sensible piece of advice to give to those who find themselves having to talk to an author about one of his books without having read it: praise it without going into detail. An author does not expect a summary or a rational analysis of his book and would even prefer you not to attempt such a thing. He expects only that, while maintaining the greatest possible degree of ambiguity, you will tell him that you like what he wrote.
