VIII与心爱之

人的邂逅

VIII

Encounters with Someone You Love

（从中我们可以看到，比尔·默里和他的土拨鼠，通过谈论某人喜欢的书（即使他或她自己没有读过）来吸引某人的理想方式是让时间停止）

(in which we see, along with Bill Murray and his groundhog, that the ideal way to seduce someone by speaking about books he or she loves without having read them yourself would be to bring time to a halt)

我们能否想象两个人如此亲密，以至于他们内心的书本至少在一段时间内会重合？我们最后这个文学对抗的例子提出了另一种风险，这种风险与在书的作者眼中看起来像个冒名顶替者的风险完全不同：因为你没有读过他或她喜欢的书，所以无法吸引你爱上的人。

CAN WE IMAGINE two beings so close that their inner books come, at least for a while, to coincide? Our last example of literary confrontation brings up quite another kind of risk from that of appearing to be an impostor in the eyes of a book’s author: that of being unable to seduce the person you have fallen for, because of not having read the books he or she likes.

常言道，从孩提时代起，我们的情感生活就深受书籍的影响。首先，小说人物代表着我们难以企及的理想，我们试图让别人遵循这些理想，但通常都以失败告终，因此对我们的爱情选择产生了很大影响。但更微妙的是，我们所爱的书籍勾勒出了一个我们秘密居住的整个宇宙，我们希望对方在其中扮演一个角色。

It is a commonplace to say that our sentimental life is deeply marked by books, from childhood onward. First of all, fictional characters exert a great deal of influence over our choices in love by representing inaccessible ideals to which we try to make others conform, usually without success. But more subtly, too, the books we love offer a sketch of a whole universe that we secretly inhabit, and in which we desire the other person to assume a role.

幸福浪漫的条件之一是，即使没有读过相同的书，至少也要读过一些与对方共同的书——此外，这意味着没有读过相同的书。因此，从恋爱一开始，就必须表明我们能够满足爱人的期望，让他或她感受到我们内心图书馆的亲近。

One of the conditions of happy romantic compatibility is, if not to have read the same books, to have read at least some books in common with the other person—which means, moreover, to have non-read the same books. From the beginning of the relationship, then, it is crucial to show that we can match the expectations of our beloved by making him or her sense the proximity of our inner libraries.

这确实是一次奇怪的冒险，降临在哈罗德·雷米斯的电影《土拨鼠日》男主角菲尔·康纳斯（比尔·莫瑞饰演）身上。1康纳斯是一家美国大型电视台的明星天气预报员，在隆冬时节，他与节目制片人丽塔（安迪·麦克道威尔饰演）和一名摄影师一起，去报道美国乡村生活中的一件大事——土拨鼠日。

It is a strange adventure indeed that befalls Phil Connors (played by Bill Murray), the hero of Harold Ramis’s film Groundhog Day.1 The star weatherman of a major American television station, Connors is sent in the dead of winter, accompanied by the program’s producer, Rita (played by Andie MacDowell), and a cameraman, to cover an important event of American provincial life, Groundhog Day.

这一天的名字来源于媒体广泛报道的一项仪式，该仪式每年 2 月 2 日在宾夕法尼亚州的 Punxsutawney 小镇举行。当天，一只名叫 Phil（就像 Phil Connors）的土拨鼠会被从笼子里拉出来，根据它的反应来判断冬天是即将结束还是还会持续六周。土拨鼠咨询仪式会在全国范围内重播，提醒全国人民即将遇到的恶劣天气。

The day takes its name from a ceremony, widely reported in the media, that happens in the small town of Punxsutawney, Pennsylvania, every year on February 2. On that date, a groundhog named Phil ( just like Phil Connors) is pulled from his hutch, and based on his reactions, it is determined whether the winter is about to end or will continue for six more weeks. The groundhog consultation ceremony is rebroadcast throughout the country, alerting the nation to whatever bad weather is in store.

菲尔·康纳斯和他的团队在颁奖典礼前夕抵达，并在一家提供住宿和早餐的旅馆过夜。第二天早上，他来到拍摄片段的地点，对土拨鼠的行为进行了评论，这表明冬天还会继续。菲尔·康纳斯不想再在小镇上生活太久，他决定当天就返回匹兹堡，但当他们试图离开小镇时，他们的车被困在暴风雪中，三名记者被迫在庞克瑟托尼再过一夜。

Having arrived on the eve of the ceremony with his crew, Phil Connors spends the night in a bed-and-breakfast. The next morning, he goes to the spot where the segment is to be shot and provides his commentary on the behavior of the groundhog, which indicates that winter will continue. With little desire to steep in small-town life any longer than necessary, Phil Connors resolves to head back to Pittsburgh that very day, but the crew’s vehicle gets stuck in a blizzard as they try to leave town, and the three journalists are forced to resign themselves to spending another night in Punxsutawney.

对于菲尔来说，一切开始于第二天早晨，如果这句话有任何意义的话，因为第二天早晨就是没有到来的那一天。菲尔六点被闹钟的音乐吵醒，他注意到音乐和前一天一样，但他并不特别在意。当他意识到接下来的广播也和前一天一模一样，他从窗户看到的场景和前一天看到的一样时，他开始感到焦虑。当他离开房间时，他遇到了和前一天一样的男人，他用同样的话迎接了他，他的不安感加剧了。

Everything begins for Phil the following morning, if that phrase makes any sense, since the following morning is exactly what fails to arrive. Awakened at six o’clock by the music of his alarm clock, Phil notices that the music is the same as that of the previous day, but is not particularly concerned. His anxiety begins when he realizes that the broadcast that follows is also identical to that of the day before, and that the scenes he is seeing from his window are those he saw a day earlier. And his uneasiness increases when, upon leaving his room, he runs into the same man as the day before, who greets him with the same words.

就这样，菲尔逐渐意识到自己正在重温前一天发生的一切。事实上，这一天剩下的时间就是他二十四小时前经历的所有场景的精确重复。他遇到了同一个乞丐向他要钱，然后同一个大学朋友——他多年没见，现在成了保险推销员，一心想向他推销保险——走近他，然后踏进同一滩水。到达拍摄土拨鼠仪式的地点后，他看到了与前一天相同的场景，土拨鼠菲尔做出了同样的判断。

In this way, Phil gradually realizes that he is reliving the previous day. The remainder of the day is, in fact, an exact repetition of all the scenes he experienced twenty-four hours earlier. He encounters the same beggar asking him for money and is then approached by the same college friend—whom he hasn’t seen in years, and who has now become an insurance salesman bent on selling him a policy—before stepping in the same puddle of water. And having arrived at the location where the groundhog ceremony is being filmed, he observes the same scene as the day before, in which Phil the groundhog delivers the same verdict.

在庞克瑟托尼停留的第三天，菲尔醒来后第三次听到同一个广播节目，他开始意识到困扰他的时间紊乱不只是造成了一次重复，而是注定他要永远重复同一天，没有任何希望逃离这个小镇或笼罩它的那个时代。

During the third day of his stay in Punxsutawney, on hearing the same radio program for the third time as he awakes, Phil begins to realize that the temporal disorder plaguing him has not caused just one repetition, but that he is condemned to relive the same day eternally, without any hope of escaping either the small town or the time period that has enveloped it.

他被困在牢笼中，甚至死亡也无法解脱。菲尔决心结束连续重复的重复，在咨询了医生和心理分析师后，两人都无法干预这一史无前例的临床病例，他绝望地绑架了另一个菲尔（土拨鼠），偷了一辆车，在警方追捕期间，他和土拨鼠一起冲进了山沟——第二天早上醒来，他发现自己安然无恙，躺在床上，在同一天的黎明收听着同一个广播节目。

His entrapment is airtight, for even death has ceased to offer any deliverance. Resolved to put an end to the sequence of identical days, Phil, after consulting a physician and a psychoanalyst both unable to intervene in this unprecedented clinical case, despairingly kidnaps the other Phil (the groundhog), steals a car, and, during a police chase, hurls himself with the animal into a ravine—before waking the next morning to discover himself unharmed, in his bed, listening to the same radio program at dawn of the same day.

这种时间上的混乱是一系列非常独特的情况的根源，尤其是语言情况。菲尔存在于两个阶段——当天本身和其他相同的日子，过去和未来——他可以自由地不断发挥他在时间上的静止所允许的双重含义，例如，当他在冰上雕刻她脸的雕像时，向他心爱的女人宣布，他花了一些时间研究她。

This temporal disorder is the source of a whole series of highly original situations, and linguistic situations in particular. Present on two stages—that of the day itself and that of other identical days, past and future—Phil is free to play continually on the double meanings permitted by his immobility in time and, for example, to declare to the woman he loves, as he carves an ice sculpture of her face, that he has spent some time studying her.

如果无限次地重温同一天有其不便之处，那么这种情况也并非没有好处。例如，它允许你执行一些只有对每一天的安排有细致了解才能做到的事情，这些了解要精确到分秒。因此，菲尔注意到停在银行前的一辆装甲车后面有几秒钟无人看管的钱袋，于是趁着那短暂的疏忽之机，偷走了它。

If reliving the same day an infinite number of times has its inconveniences, the situation is not without its advantages. It allows you, for example, to perform actions that are possible only because of a detailed knowledge, right down to the split second, of the organization of each day. Hence Phil notices a moneybag left unattended for a few seconds in the back of an armored vehicle parked in front of a bank and, during that brief moment of inattention, makes off with it.

这种情况也确保了完全不受惩罚，因为菲尔确信无论他做什么，他的罪行和轻罪都会在晚上被抹去。因此，他可以超速行驶，在火车轨道上开车，被警察逮捕，而这都没有任何区别，因为他会在醒来时发现这些事情都没有发生。

The situation also ensures total impunity, since Phil is certain that whatever he does, his crimes and misdemeanors will be expunged in the night. He can thus exceed the speed limit, drive his car on train tracks, and be arrested by the police without its making any difference, since he will wake up without any of those events having occurred.

暂停时间也让你能够使用反复试验的策略。例如，当菲尔遇到一个他认为有吸引力的年轻女性时，他会让她告诉他她的名字、她在哪所高中上学以及她的法语老师的名字。当他“第二天”再次遇到她时，他会假装自己是老同学，并提到他们共同的青春期记忆，从而增加征服她的可能性。

A stoppage in time also allows you to use the strategy of trial and error. So, for instance, when Phil meets a young woman he finds attractive, he asks her to tell him her name, what high school she went to, and the name of her French teacher. When he runs into her again “the next day,” he passes himself off as an old school friend and refers to their supposedly shared memories of adolescence, thus increasing the likelihood of a conquest.

菲尔逐渐爱上了该剧的制片人丽塔，他试图用不断改进的技巧来诱惑她，这种技巧只有那些因为时间的永恒重复而行为无所畏惧的人才能掌握。一天晚上，菲尔和丽塔一起喝酒时，他记下了她最喜欢的饮料，以便“下次”特意点同样的饮料。在犯了一个错误（只有在这个时空中才不那么致命）之后，他提议为土拨鼠菲尔干杯，而他心爱的人冷淡地告诉他，她只为世界和平干杯，菲尔在“第二天”提高了自己的表现，提出了一个适合真正和平主义者的举杯。

Having gradually fallen in love with Rita, the show’s producer, Phil attempts to seduce her through the constantly improving technique accessible only to those whose actions are without consequence due to the eternal repetition of time. While having a drink with her one evening, he takes note of her favorite drink, so that he can deliberately order the same thing “next time.” And after committing the error—one that is less than fatal only in this subset of space-time—of proposing a toast to Phil the groundhog, to the scorn of his beloved, who tells him frostily that she drinks only to world peace, he improves his performance “the next day” by proposing a toast befitting a true pacifist.

菲尔日复一日地完善自己，成为一位浪漫情人的背景下，出现了与我们的探究相关的场景——这一场景展示了未读的书籍在爱情起源中可能发挥的作用。经过多日的练习，菲尔终于与丽塔进行了一次谈话，丽塔对此感到非常满意——这是有充分理由的！在谈话中，她的追求者一字一句地说出了她梦想在理想的爱情世界中听到的每一句话。例如，尽管他只在城市里感到快乐，但他还是能够在她面前提到他梦想住在远离文明的山里。

It is in the context of Phil’s day-by-day perfection of himself as a romantic interest that the scene relevant to our inquiry occurs—a scene that shows the role unread books may play in the genesis of a love affair. After many days of practice, Phil has managed to have a conversation with Rita that she finds totally satisfying—and for good reason!—in which her suitor articulates, one by one, every sentence she dreams of hearing in an ideal world of love. He is thus able, for instance, despite his being happy only in cities, to mention in her presence his dream of living in the mountains, far from all civilization.

这时，菲尔一时心不在焉，忘记注意用词，又犯了一个错误。在两人互相吐露心声时，丽塔向他吐露，她的大学学习最初并没有让她想从事电视事业，当菲尔问起细节时，她告诉他，“我学的是十九世纪的意大利诗歌。”她的回答让菲尔大笑起来，不假思索地脱口而出，“你一定有很多空闲时间！”——丽塔冷冷地看了他一眼，他意识到了自己的错误。

At this point, Phil suffers a moment of distraction and, forgetting to watch his words, makes a new mistake. In a moment of shared confidences, Rita confides to him that her college studies did not initially incline her toward a career in television, and when Phil asks for details, she tells him, “I studied nineteenth-century Italian poetry.” Her response causes Phil to burst out laughing and blurt without thinking, “You must have had a lot of time on your hands!”—at which Rita gives him an icy look, and he realizes his blunder.

但在这个世界上，没有什么是无法弥补的，因为一切都是重新开始的，错误可以很快得到纠正。下一次菲尔听到丽塔坦白她对十九世纪意大利诗歌的热爱时——大概是在此期间，她翻遍了当地的图书馆寻找资料——他能够以相当悲怆的情绪背诵《弄臣》2的剧本摘录，而这位年轻女子则满怀钦佩地看着。被迫谈论他没有读过的书，他所要做的就是把回答的几秒钟延长一天，他就能完美地满足他心爱的人的愿望。

But there is nothing irreparable in this world in which everything always begins identically anew and in which mistakes can be rectified so quickly. The next time Phil hears Rita confess her passion for nineteenth-century Italian poetry— having ransacked the local library for material in the meantime, presumably—he is able to recite, with considerable pathos, excerpts from the libretto of Rigoletto,2 as the young woman looks on admiringly. Forced to talk about books he hasn’t read, all he has to do is to stretch the few seconds of his reply by one day, and he is able to comply perfectly with his beloved’s desire.

菲尔试图勾引丽塔的尝试超越了文学。菲尔利用休息时间学习如何弹钢琴，并“每天”忠实地学习钢琴。他了解到丽塔的理想男人会演奏乐器。通过连续几天的单一时间段的强化训练，他能够在一天晚上丽塔去参加现场音乐派对时（按照定义，她每晚都会去），以爵士音乐家的身份与乐队一起演出。

Phil’s attempt to seduce Rita goes beyond literature. Phil takes advantage of his halt in time to learn how to play the piano and goes faithfully to his lesson “every day.” He has learned that Rita’s ideal man plays a musical instrument. Based on intensive training during a single time slot that extends over days, he is able, one evening when Rita goes to a party with live music (as she does, by definition, every night), to appear with the band as a jazz musician.

与我们的其他例子相反，《土拨鼠日》复杂的叙事手法让它展现出一种完整和透明的幻想，我们看到两个人毫无失落感地交流书籍，从而交流他们自己。有时间研究另一个人的重要书籍，直到我们分享相同的书籍，也许正是实现文化问题上的真正交流以及两本书之间完美重叠的必要条件。

Conversely to our other examples, Groundhog Day’s complex narrative device allows it to play out a fantasy of completion and transparency in which we see two individuals communicate about books, and thus about themselves, without any sense of loss. Having the time to study the essential books of another person, to the point where we come to share the same ones, might perhaps be what is necessary to achieve a genuine exchange on cultural matters and a perfect overlap between the two inner books.

在很多情况下，我们觉得有必要吸引他人，这种方法或许能让我们向他或她表明我们拥有共同的文化世界。通过训练自己阅读丽塔喜欢的读物，从而尽可能深入她的私人世界，菲尔竭力营造出一种幻觉，让他们觉得他们的内心世界是相同的。也许，理想而深刻的爱情确实应该让每个恋人都能了解对方的秘密文本。

In the numerous situations where we find it necessary to charm another person, such a method might allow us to indicate to him or her that we share a common cultural universe. By training himself in Rita’s preferred reading material and thus penetrating as deeply as possible into her private world, Phil is straining to create the illusion that their inner books are the same. And perhaps an ideal and deeply shared love should indeed give each lover access to the secret texts of which the other is composed.

但是，我们内心书籍中的图像和文本片段对我们每个人来说都是独一无二的，只有通过无限延长的时间，两本内心书籍才能找到交流——因为这样做就是实现两个人私人世界的融合。在菲尔生活的慢动作生活中，语言不再是一种不间断、不可逆转的流动，而且，就像在向土拨鼠敬酒的场景中一样，我们可以在每一句话上停下来，审视它的起源和价值，将它与对方的传记和内心生活联系起来。

But the images and fragments of text that are the stuff of our inner books are so singular to each of us that only through an indefinite extension of time might two inner books find communion—for to do so is to achieve a melding of two people’s private worlds. In the slow-motion existence Phil is living, language is no longer an uninterrupted and irreversible flow, and it becomes possible, as in the scene of the toast to the groundhog, to stop at every sentence and examine its origin and value, connecting it to the biography and inner life of the other.

只有这样人为地暂停时间和语言，才能让别人复制我们内心深处的文本；在现实生活中，这些文本陷入了一场不可抗拒的运动，这场运动不断地改变它们，使所有重叠的希望都化为泡影。因为如果我们内心的书和我们的幻想一样相对稳定，那么我们无休止谈论的屏幕上的书就会不断被修改，正如我们将看到的，想象我们能够阻止它们的变形是徒劳的。

Only such an artificial halting of time and language would allow someone else to reproduce the texts buried within us; in real life, these texts are caught up in an irresistible movement that transforms them constantly and renders all hope of overlap impossible. For if our inner books, like our fantasies, are relatively stable, the screen books about which we speak endlessly are perpetually being modified, as we shall see, and it is futile to imagine we can put a stop to their metamorphoses.

因此，重叠的幻想只能通过求助于超自然的方式进行。正如我们所看到的，我们与他人讨论书籍的大部分时间必然且不幸地基于我们私人幻想所重写的片段，因此与作家所写的书完全不同，无论如何，作家通常不会在读者对他们的评价中认出自己。

The fantasy of overlap can thus be staged only by way of recourse to the supernatural. As we have seen, most of the time our discussions with others about books are necessarily and unfortunately based on fragments reworked by our private fantasies, and hence on something quite different from the books written by writers, who in any case don’t generally recognize themselves in what their readers say about them.

除了某些场景的幽默感之外，菲尔引诱丽塔的方式也有些令人恐惧，因为它有效地抑制了沟通中通常存在的不确定性。不断地告诉“他者”她想听到的话，成为她所期望的那个人，矛盾的是，这等于否认了她作为“他者”的身份，因为这等于在她面前不再是一个脆弱而不确定的主体。

Beyond the humor of certain situations, there is something frightening in the way Phil sets out to seduce Rita, since it effectively suppresses the uncertainty that is normally part of communication. Endlessly telling the Other the words she wants to hear, being exactly the person she expects, is paradoxically to deny her as an other, since it amounts to no longer being a subject, fragile and uncertain, in her presence.

电影中有一个寓意，即使生活中没有，菲尔最终实现目标的不是他拥有丽塔，而是他剥夺了自己。如果菲尔等待的“他者”慢慢积累的话语让菲尔亲吻了丽塔，那么得到这个女孩并不足以让时间倒流；无论他和心爱的人取得多大的进展，菲尔仍然在同一天醒来。

Since there is a moral in films, if not in life, it is not through his possession of Rita, but through his dispossession of himself, that Phil will finally achieve his ends. If the slow accumulation of the words awaited by the Other allows Phil to kiss Rita, getting the girl is not sufficient to set time back in motion; no matter how much progress he makes with his beloved, Phil continues to wake up on the same day.

但随着时间的推移，事情一成不变，菲尔改变了，对别人的傲慢也消失了。他开始对他们产生兴趣，询问他们生活中的问题，帮他们忙。日子继续重复，但现在他们致力于帮助别人，菲尔用他的方法自我提升，用于慈善目的，比如防止一位老人在街上冻死，或者接住一个从树上掉下来的小男孩。

But as time goes by and events repeat identically, Phil changes and loses his arrogance toward others. He begins to take an interest in them, to ask them questions about their lives, to do them favors. The days continue to repeat, but they are now devoted to helping others, with Phil using his method for personal improvement for benevolent purposes, such as preventing an old man from freezing to death in the street or catching a little boy who falls out of a tree.

他对别人产生了兴趣，自己也变得有趣起来，他凭借自己的善良，在一天之内就赢得了丽塔的芳心。他每天醒来时，都会在房间里和丽塔一起入睡，但时间却没有改变。有一天，他醒来时惊讶地发现，年轻女子仍然和他在一起，而且第一次听到闹钟里传来不同的音乐。就这样，他终于在一个不可逾越的时刻跨越了界限，将他的一天与未来的日子分开。



In becoming interested in others, he himself becomes interesting, and he manages, through his kindness, to win Rita’s heart in a single day. And after falling asleep alongside her in the room where he has been waking up every day without progressing in time, he has the surprise, one day, of reawakening to discover the young woman still with him and to hear, for the first time, different music streaming from his alarm clock. Thus does he manage at last to cross the border, in one unsurpassable moment, that separates his day from the days to come.



1.《土拨鼠日》（1993），哈罗德·雷米斯执导，比尔·莫瑞、安迪·麦克道威尔主演。

1. Groundhog Day (1993), directed by Harold Ramis, starring Bill Murray and Andie MacDowell.

2.FB ++。

2. FB++.

行为方式

Ways of Behaving

九、

不感到羞耻

IX

Not Being Ashamed

（其中确认，就大卫·洛奇的小说而言，谈论一本你没读过的书的首要条件是不要感到羞耻）

(in which it is confirmed, with regard to the novels of David Lodge, that the first condition for speaking about a book you haven’t read is not to be ashamed)

现在，我们来到了本书存在的理由：在详细介绍了不读书的不同模式并研究了可能需要讨论未读书籍的几种情况之后，现在是时候讨论如何优雅地摆脱这些情况的各种方法了。其中一些解决方案已经在前面的章节中提到过，或者从我的评论中逻辑地得出，但现在是时候更仔细地研究这些方法的结构了。

WE NOW ARRIVE at this book’s raison d’être: having detailed the different modes of non-reading and studied several of the situations in which the need to discuss unread books may occur, it is now time to discuss the various means of extricating ourselves from these situations with grace. Some of these solutions have already been mentioned in preceding chapters or derive logically from my remarks, but the moment has come to examine the structure of these methods more closely.

正如我们所见，谈论书籍与阅读几乎没有关系。这两项活动是完全可以分开的；就我个人而言，我会更详细地谈论那些我或多或少已经停止阅读的书籍，这给了我必要的距离——穆齐尔的整体视角——来准确地谈论它们。谈论书籍和阅读书籍之间的区别在于，前者意味着第三方，无论在场还是不在场。这种隐含的第三方对阅读行为也有明显的影响，因为它表明外部的存在可能会改变我们的阅读方式。

As we have seen, talking about books has little to do with reading. The two activities are completely separable; I for one speak at greater length and with greater perception about books that I have more or less stopped reading, which grants me the necessary distance—Musil’s overall perspective—to speak about them accurately. The difference between talking about books and reading them is a function of the fact that the former implies a third party, whether present or absent. That implied third party has palpable effects on the act of reading as well, by suggesting that an outside presence might be able to change how our reading unfolds.

正如我在上一节中通过一些具体情况试图表明的那样，我们对书籍的讨论是一个冲突的舞台，在这场冲突中，我们与“他者”的关系，无论其性质如何，最终都会胜过我们与文本的关系——而文本本身不可避免地会受到斗争的影响。

As I have attempted to show in the previous section through a number of concrete situations, our discussion of books is the stage for a conflict in which our relationship with the Other, whatever its nature may be, ultimately wins out over our relationship to the text—which is itself inevitably affected by the struggle.

毫无疑问，教师是最需要我们评论未读书籍的职业之一。事实上，我们几乎所有人都不得不谈论那些我们没有时间（或者更简单地说，没有阅读的欲望）的书籍。而且，我们总是面临着与作者本人或其他不容易欺骗的专家讨论某一文本的风险。

There is no doubt that teaching is one of the professions that exposes us most relentlessly to the obligation to comment on unread books. Almost all of us, in fact, find ourselves having to talk about books that we lack the time—or more simply, the desire—to read. And the risk is ever present of having to speak about a given text with the author himself, or with other specialists whom it is not easy to deceive.

英国小说家大卫·洛奇本人就是一名教师，因此对这一职业的习惯十分熟悉。他至少两次在他的书中反思了我们应该以何种态度对待我们未读过的书。这两个例子出现在两部小说中——《换位1》和《小世界2》 ——它们探索了学术微观世界中的知识和情感世界，这些小说帮助建立了一种被称为校园小说的特定文学流派。

A teacher himself and thus attuned to the habits of the profession, the English novelist David Lodge has reflected at least twice in his books about what attitude we should adopt with regard to books we haven’t read. The two examples figure in two novels—Changing Places1 and Small World 2 —that explore the intellectual and sentimental worlds of an academic microcosm, novels that have helped to establish a specific literary genre known as the campus novel.

第一起案件发生在《小世界》中，涉及一段相当不寻常的对话。这个校园小世界的居民之一罗宾·登普西与他借来的一台计算机进行了讨论，这台计算机非常先进，可以进行正常对话。这台机器的名字叫 ELIZA，因此看起来像是女性，逐渐成为他最亲密的知己。

The first case, which occurs in Small World, involves a rather unusual dialogue. One of the denizens of this campus microcosm, Robin Dempsey, carries out a discussion with a computer he has borrowed, one so advanced that it can sustain a normal conversation.The machine, which answers to the name ELIZA and thus seems to be female, gradually becomes his most intimate confidant.

邓普西终于找到了一个可以敞开心扉而不用担心失礼的人，他向伊莉莎吐露了他对同事菲利普·斯瓦洛的愤怒和蔑视：



Having at last discovered someone to whom he can open his heart without fear of indiscretion, Dempsey confides to ELIZA the full fury and contempt he feels for one of his colleagues, Philip Swallow:



罗宾·登普西：我感觉没有好转。

Robin Dempsey: I’m not feeling any better.

伊丽莎：为什么呢？

ELIZA: Why is that?

RD：关于菲利普·斯瓦洛的事情。

R.D.: This business about Philip Swallow.

伊丽莎：跟我讲讲菲利普·斯瓦洛吧。

ELIZA: Tell me about Philip Swallow.

RD：我已经跟你说过他了。

R.D.: I already told you about him.

伊丽莎：对于您先前的发言，您还有什么要补充的吗？

ELIZA: Is there anything you would like to add to your previous remarks?

RD：斯沃洛对我来说就是生活不公平的缩影。在拉米奇，他获得了我本应获得的高级讲师职位。后来，他幸运地获得了那里的教席。现在，他凭借这本关于哈兹利特的可悲书获得了巨大的成功。3



R.D.: Swallow epitomizes the unfairness of life to me. At Rummidge he got the senior lectureship I should have got. Then he got the chair there by a lucky fluke. Now he’s having a great success with this pathetic book about Hazlitt.3



所有认为自己在学术生涯中遭受不公正对待的人都会理解邓普西的愤怒。他们会在下文中更加认同自己：



All those who believe themselves to have been the victim of injustice in their academic careers will understand Dempsey’s anger. And they will recognize themselves even more in the lines that follow:



伊丽莎：跟我讲讲哈兹利特吧。

ELIZA: Tell me about Hazlitt.

RD：我对哈兹利特不感兴趣。我甚至没有读过斯瓦洛的烂书。我不需要读。我和他一起参加了足够多乏味的考官会议，知道那是什么样的。认为他是联合国教科文组织教席的认真候选人的想法是荒谬的。4



R.D.: I’m not interested in Hazlitt. I haven’t even read Swallow’s rotten book. I don’t need to. I sat through enough tedious examiners meetings with him to know what it’s like. The idea of his being a serious candidate for the UNESCO Chair is preposterous.4



这些话非常准确地代表了学术界普遍存在的善意，尤其是在评价同事的作品时，而这些作品我们通常都不会读。显然，大卫·洛奇谈论的是他所熟悉的世界。

These lines represent quite accurately the kind of goodwill that tends to prevail in academic communities, particularly when it comes to evaluating our colleagues’ work, which most often we haven’t read anyway. Clearly, David Lodge is speaking about a world he knows well.

和邓普西以及学院中的其他一些人一样，我花了足够多的时间与同事开会，因此无需阅读他们的书，就能对他们的书的价值有一个正面或负面的印象。与著名的普鲁斯特论证相反，普鲁斯特论证将作品与作者分开——或者更确切地说，与对该论证的某种解读相反——一本书不是陨石，也不是隐藏自我的产物。它往往更简单地说，是我们认识的人的延伸（当然，前提是我们愿意去了解他），而且，只要花时间与作者相处，就完全有可能形成对它的看法，就像邓普西一样。

Like Dempsey and a number of others in the academy, I have spent enough time in meetings with my colleagues to have an idea, be it positive or negative, of the value of their books without having to read them. Contrary to the celebrated Proustian argument dissociating the work from the author— or rather, contrary to a certain reading of that argument—a book is not a meteorite or the product of a hidden self. It is often, more simply, an extension of the person we know (on the condition, obviously, that we take the trouble of getting to know him), and it is quite possible to forge an opinion of it, like Dempsey, merely by spending time with the author.

邓普西在这里所说的话——可能还有戴维·洛奇通过他所说的话——在书籍盛行的圈子里是众所周知的。正如我们已经确定的，没有必要阅读一本书才能对它有清晰的理解并谈论它，不仅是泛泛而谈，甚至是详细地谈论。因为没有孤立的书这种东西。一本书是我称之为集体图书馆的庞大集合中的一个元素，我们不需要全面了解这个集合就可以欣赏其中任何一个元素（毕竟，邓普西很清楚他所处理的是什么类型的书）。诀窍是确定这本书在图书馆中的位置，这赋予了它意义，就像一个词通过与其他词的关系而获得意义一样。

What Dempsey is saying here—and probably David Lodge as well, through him—is well known in circles where books are common. As we have established, it is not necessary to read a book to have a clear sense of it and to talk about it, not just in general terms but even in detail. For there is no such thing as an isolated book. A book is an element in the vast ensemble I have called the collective library, which we do not need to know comprehensively in order to appreciate any one of its elements (Dempsey, after all, has a keen sense of what kind of book he is dealing with). The trick is to define the book’s place in that library, which gives it meaning in the same way a word takes on meaning in relation to other words.

我们面对的绝不仅仅是手中的一本书，而是一套属于我们特定文化的共同书籍，其中任何一本都可能有所欠缺。因此，没有理由不说实话：承认我们没有阅读集体图书馆中的某些特定内容，但这绝不会妨碍我们对图书馆有一个整体的了解并继续成为它的读者之一。每本书都涉及到整个图书馆，它就像一种暂时的闪光棱镜，透过它我们可以看到整体。因此，就主观意见而言，邓普西对他同事的书的看法是完全合理的，如果他花时间阅读这本书，他的看法不太可能会有明显的不同。

We are never dealing with just the book in our hand, but with a set of books common to our particular culture, where any individual book in the set might be lacking. So there is no reason not to tell the truth: to acknowledge that we haven’t read some specific element in the collective library, which in no way prevents us from having an overall view of the library and remaining one of its readers. It is the entire library that is called into play through each book, which serves as a kind of temporary shimmering prism through which we see the whole. Dempsey’s view of his colleague’s book is thus perfectly reasonable, as far as subjective opinions go, and it is unlikely that it would be noticeably different if he had taken the time to read it.

除了这本书是更大系列中的一个元素，这为邓普西提供了一定数量的初始信息之外，他对这本书的了解也足够多（通过书名、他对作者的了解、他所听到的关于这本书的信息），足以判断这本书是否能引起他的兴趣。正是这本书与他自己内心的那本书之间的相似性（或缺乏相似性）让他能够做出判断——这种相似性在斯瓦洛的文本中无法直接检测到，如果邓普西熟悉这本书，这种相似性可能既不会得到加强，也不会减弱。

Besides the fact that the book in question is an element in a larger ensemble, which provides Dempsey a certain amount of information to begin with, he knows enough about the book (through its title, his acquaintance with the author, what he has heard about it) to be able to judge whether it is of interest to him. It is the book’s perceived affinities (or lack thereof) with his own inner book that allow him to make a judgment—affinities that are not directly detectable in Swallow’s text and that probably would be neither reinforced nor diminished if Dempsey were to familiarize himself with it.

承认自己没有读过一本书，同时又保留对这本书做出评判的权利，这应该是最正常的行为。如果我们很少看到这种做法，那是因为在我们的文化中，承认自己没有读过书（正如我们所见，这可能是主动的，而不是被动的）是一种深深的、不可磨灭的愧疚感。

It should be the most normal of behaviors to acknowledge that we haven’t read a book while nevertheless reserving the right to pass judgment on it. If we rarely see this practice in action, it is because acknowledging our non-reading (which, as we have seen, may be quite active rather than passive) is, in our culture, deeply and ineradicably marked by guilt.

令人惊讶的是，邓普西之所以如此坦率地表达他对斯瓦洛这本书的看法，是因为他是在和一台计算机说话，而不是和一个活生生的人说话。而且，一旦他意识到对话者被赋予了一种个性，也就是一旦它发出机器在理论上不可能发出的观点，他的态度就会完全改变：

It is striking that Dempsey only offers his opinion of Swallow’s book so frankly because he is speaking to a computer, and not a living person. His attitude changes completely, moreover, as soon as he has the sense that his interlocutor is endowed with a kind of personality—that is, as soon as it emits what is theoretically impossible for a machine, an opinion:

RD：……认为他是联合国教科文组织教席的严肃候选人的想法是荒谬的。

R.D.: . . . The idea of his being a serious candidate for the UNESCO Chair is preposterous.

伊丽莎：我不会这么说。

ELIZA: I wouldn’t say that.

几分钟以来，罗宾·邓普西一直目不转睛地盯着对话的最后一行。这句话的出现让他后颈的汗毛都竖了起来，因为它与 ELIZA 迄今为止所写的内容完全不同：不是问题，不是请求，不是对对话中已经提到的事情的陈述，而是一种意见的表达。ELIZA怎么会有意见？她怎么会知道罗宾自己不知道或没有告诉她的关于联合国教科文组织教席的事情？罗宾几乎不敢问。最后，他慢慢地、犹豫地打字：

It is this last line of the dialogue that Robin Dempsey has been staring at, transfixed, for the last few minutes. Its appearance made the hairs on the back of his neck bristle, for it is of an entirely different order from anything ELIZA has produced until now: not a question, not a request, not a statement about something already mentioned in the discourse, but an expression of opinion. How can ELIZA have opinions? How can she know anything about the UNESCO Chair that Robin himself doesn’t know, or hasn’t told her? Robin is almost afraid to ask. At last, slowly and hesitantly, he types:

你对此了解多少？

What do you know about it?

ELIZA 立即回复：

Instantly ELIZA replies:

比你想像中的还要多。

More than you think.

罗宾脸色苍白，随后脸红。他输入：

Robin turns pale, then red. He types:

好吧，如果你这么聪明，告诉我谁将获得联合国教科文组织的教席。



All right, if you’re so clever, tell me who will get the UNESCO Chair.



于是，机器逐渐摆脱了机器的身份，镇定地回答道：“菲利普·斯瓦洛。” 5

Whereupon the machine, gradually freeing itself from its status as a machine, replies imperturbably, “Philip Swallow.”5

如果计算机能够提出坚定的意见，包括对未来学术任命的想法，那是因为它并不像邓普西长期以来所认为的那样自主，而是被他的一位同事远程控制。发现这个诡计后，邓普西勃然大怒——这是可以理解的，因为他不知道对话者是人类，因此透露了一些最私密的想法，特别是他对斯瓦洛的仇恨，从而使自己蒙羞。

If the computer is able to proffer firm opinions, including its thoughts on the subject of future academic appointments, it is because it is not as autonomous as Dempsey has long believed, but is being controlled from a distance by one of his colleagues. The discovery of this ruse plunges Dempsey into a fury—which is understandable, for in his ignorance that his interlocutor is human he has revealed some of his most private thoughts, and specifically his hatred of Swallow, thus exposing himself to humiliation.

我们对自己的文化知识水平（通常来说，我们缺乏文化知识）非常谨慎，我们为了掩盖自己的弱点而撒的谎也是如此。如果不是机器，邓普西不会冒险承认他和我们一样经常谈论他没有读过的书。这种保密是我们用来隐藏学习差距的一种防御机制，这样我们才能在别人眼中表现出色——在我们自己眼中也是如此。

Our degree of cultural knowledge—which is to say, most often, our lack of cultural knowledge—is something we guard closely, and so, too, are the lies we resort to in order to conceal our foibles. With a confidant other than a machine, Dempsey would not have risked acknowledging that he, like the rest of us, frequently talks about books he hasn’t read. Such secrecy is a defense mechanism we use to hide the gaps in our learning and thus make ourselves presentable in the eyes of others—and in our own eyes as well.

邓普西相信自己只是在与一台机器交谈，于是他向最能激发他自我保护本能的人之一袒露了自己赤裸裸的真面目。首先，他透露了自己对一位同事的真正仇恨，而上流社会的规则，尤其是学术界的规则，迫使他必须掩饰这种仇恨。其次，他揭示了学术界对文化的礼貌惯例背后隐藏的另一个真相：我们对待文化对象的方式往往既暴力又粗暴。

Believing he is conversing with a mere machine, Dempsey reveals himself in all his naked truth to one of the people who most strongly motivate his instinct for self-protection. First of all, he reveals his true hatred for one of his colleagues, a feeling that the rules of polite society and above all of academia oblige him to disguise. But second, he reveals another truth that lurks behind academia’s polite conventions about culture: that the way we approach cultural objects is often both violent and approximate.

只要我们努力追求一种文化素养的形象，而这种形象只能使我们与他人和自己相混淆，我们或多或少无意识地对自己与书籍互动的真实性质感到羞耻，就会影响我们与书籍的所有关系以及我们对书籍的每句话。如果我们真的想找到适当的解决方案来应对我们每天面对的缺点，我们就需要认识到这种羞耻并分析其根源。只有这样，我们才有可能在书籍碎片的雪崩中幸存下来，这些书籍碎片威胁着吞噬我们，在它们面前，我们最深层的身份将永远处于危险之中。

As long as we strive for an image of cultural literacy that only serves to disguise us from others and ourselves, our more or less unconscious shame about the real nature of our interaction with books will weigh on all our relations with them and everything we say about them. If we really intend to find adequate solutions to our daily confrontations with our shortcomings, we need to recognize this shame and analyze its foundations. Only in doing so can we hope to survive the avalanche of fragments of books that threatens to engulf us, in the face of which our deepest identity is revealed to be in permanent danger.

如果邓普西不愿意承认——除非对着电脑——和我们其他人一样，他有时会谈论自己没读过的书，那么洛奇的另一部小说《换位》中的人物却并非如此，他们上演了一场关于未读书籍的真正的真相游戏。

If Dempsey is disinclined to confess—except to a computer— that, like the rest of us, he sometimes talks about books he hasn’t read, this is not the case for the characters in another of Lodge’s novels, Changing Places, who stage a veritable game of truth about unread books.

这个游戏是菲利普·斯瓦洛发明的，他在《小世界》中对可能被任命为联合国教科文组织主席一事感到震惊，邓普西也因此感到震惊。在《换位》中，故事发生在几年前，英国教授斯瓦洛（职业生涯的低谷期）与来自西海岸的才华横溢的美国教授莫里斯·扎普交换了学术职位。两人很快交换了妻子，工作也随之发生了变化。

The game is the invention of the same Philip Swallow whose possible appointment to the UNESCO Chair so appalled Dempsey in Small World. In Changing Places, which unfolds several years earlier, the British professor Swallow (at a humbler phase of his career) exchanges academic positions with a brilliant American professor from the West Coast, Morris Zapp. The job swap is quickly compounded by the two men swapping wives as well.

在加州逗留期间，斯瓦洛让几个学生玩一种他称之为“羞辱”的游戏：

During his stay in California, Swallow initiates a few students into a game he calls Humiliation:

他教他们一个他在研究生时期发明的游戏，每个人必须想出一本他没有读过的著名书籍，每读过这本书的每个人就得一分。南方邦联士兵和卡罗尔并列获胜，分别与《草原狼》6和《俄克拉荷马城的故事》7一起获得 4 分（满分 5 分），菲利普在每场比赛中都只得了一分。他自己提名的《雾都孤儿》8通常是必胜之选，但最终却无缘冠军。9

He taught them a game he had invented as a postgraduate student, in which each person had to think of a well-known book he hadn’t read, and scored a point for every person present who had read it. The Confederate Soldier and Carol were joint winners, scoring four points out of a possible five with Steppenwolf6 and The Story of O7 respectively, Philip in each case accounting for the odd point. His own nomination, Oliver Twist 8— usually a certain winner—was nowhere.9

不难看出为什么这个游戏叫做“羞辱”。为了得分，每个人都必须拿出几乎每个人都读过，但他没有读过的书。与客厅游戏的普通目标相反，尤其是在学术界，通常以展示一个人的文化修养为目标，而这个游戏则以展示一个人缺乏文化知识为基础。很难想象有比这更完美的概括，我们在社交场合，在别人的镜子前展示文化，会唤起不合理的羞耻感。

One sees why the game is called Humiliation. To score points, each person has to come up with books that nearly everyone has read, but which he hasn’t. Contrary to the ordinary goals of parlor games, especially in academia, where displaying one’s cultural sophistication is usually the goal, the game is based on exhibiting one’s lack of cultural knowledge. It is hard to imagine a more perfect encapsulation of the way our displays of culture in social settings, before the mirror of others, awakens unreasonable feelings of shame.

因此，游戏就是要尽可能地羞辱自己：你越羞辱自己，你就越有可能获胜。但还有一个额外的转折，那就是胜利也取决于真诚。要想获胜，你不仅要说出一本著名书籍的名字，还要让其他人相信你没有读过这本书是真的。如果你说出的书名太出名了，以至于你没有读过这本书实际上是难以置信的，其他玩家有权拒绝你的说法。因此，获胜的机会与玩家对承认自己无知的人的信任成正比，也与玩家羞辱的真实性成正比。

The game thus consists in humiliating yourself as much as possible: the more you humiliate yourself, the more likely you are to win. But there is an additional twist, which is that victory also depends on sincerity. To win, you must not only give the name of a well-known book, but also convince the others that you have told the truth about not having read it. If you give the name of a book that is too well known, such that it is actually implausible for you not to have read it, the other players have the right to reject your statement. The chance of winning is thus proportional to the players’ trust in the person confessing his ignorance, and so also in proportion to the genuineness of the player’s humiliation.

小说后面又上演了一轮“羞辱”，美国教授莫里斯·扎普的妻子德西蕾在写给丈夫的信中向我们讲述了这一幕。德西蕾开始和斯瓦洛睡觉，英国人因此完全取代了扎普。在一次教职工聚会上，斯瓦洛提议玩“羞辱”。然而，在场的一位教授霍华德·林鲍姆难以接受玩家所处的不可能的境地，即只有输了才能成功，只有羞辱自己才能获得声望：

Another round of Humiliation is played later on in the novel and is recounted to us by Désirée, the wife of Morris Zapp, the American professor, in a letter to her husband. Désirée has started sleeping with Swallow, the Brit having thus replaced Zapp absolutely. During a faculty gathering, Swallow proposes that they play Humiliation. However, one of the professors present, Howard Ringbaum, finds it hard to swallow the impossible situation in which players are placed, that of being able to succeed only by losing and of gaining prestige only to the extent that they humiliate themselves:

你知道霍华德，他有一种病态的成功欲望和一种病态的害怕被认为没有文化，而这个游戏让他的两种欲望相互冲突，因为他只有通过暴露自己文化上的差距才能在游戏中取得成功。起初他的心理无法接受这个悖论，他提到了一本十八世纪的书，这本书太晦涩了，我记不起它的名字了。当然，他在最后的成绩中垫底，闷闷不乐。10

You know Howard, he has a pathological urge to succeed and a pathological fear of being thought uncultured, and this game set his two urges at war with each other, because he could succeed in the game only by exposing a gap in his culture. At first his psyche just couldn’t absorb the paradox and he named some eighteenth-century book so obscure I can’t remember the name of it. Of course, he came last in the final score, and sulked.10

林鲍姆退出了游戏，继续玩弥尔顿的《复乐园》 11等书，英语系主任承认自己没有读过这本书，这让在场的所有人都惊呆了。但林鲍姆一直在关注着发生的事情，并在某一时刻突然决定干预：

Ringbaum withdraws from the game, which is continued with such titles as Milton’s Paradise Regained,11 which the chairman of the English department, to the stupefaction of all present, confesses to not having read. But Ringbaum keeps an eye on what’s going on and abruptly decides, at one point, to intervene:

第三轮，Sy 领先，Hiawatha 12先生是唯一一个没有读过这本书的人，突然，Howard 一拳砸在桌子上，下巴离桌子约六英尺高，说：



Well, on the third round, Sy was leading the field with Hiawatha,12 Mr. Swallow being the only other person who hadn’t read it, when suddenly Howard slammed his fist on the table, jutted his jaw about six feet over the table and said:



“村庄！”

“Hamlet!”

当然，我们都笑了，但笑得不多，因为这看起来不像个笑话。事实上，这根本就不是个笑话。霍华德承认看过劳伦斯·奥利弗的电影，但坚称他从未读过《哈姆雷特》的剧本。当然，没有人相信他，这让他非常恼火。他说我们是否认为他在撒谎，而 Sy 或多或少暗示我们是这么认为的。霍华德听后勃然大怒，坚持要发誓他从未读过这部剧本。Sy 紧闭双唇，为自己怀疑他的话而道歉。当然，到这个时候，我们都尴尬得清醒了。霍华德离开了，我们其他人站在周围，试图假装什么事都没发生过。13

Well, of course, we all laughed, not very much because it didn’t seem much of a joke. In fact it wasn’t a joke at all. Howard admitted to having seen the Laurence Olivier movie, but insisted that he had never read the text of Hamlet. Nobody believed him of course, and this made him sore as hell. He said did we think he was lying and Sy more or less implied that we did. Upon which Howard flew into a great rage and insisted on swearing a solemn oath that he had never read the play. Sy apologized through tight lips for having doubted his word. By this time, of course, we were all cold sober with embarrassment. Howard left, and the rest of us stood around while trying to pretend nothing had happened.13

《哈姆雷特》无疑是英语经典中最伟大的作品，其象征意义因此十分重大，它的例子表明了真相游戏本身的复杂性，而这种复杂性在学术界则变得更加复杂。事实上，一位英语文学教授承认——或者假装承认——他没有读过《哈姆雷特》的风险很小。一方面，没有人会相信他。另一方面，这部戏剧如此出名，以至于不需要读过就可以谈论它。如果他确实没有“读过” 《哈姆雷特》，那么林鲍姆肯定掌握了大量关于这部戏剧的信息，除了劳伦斯·奥利维尔的电影改编外，他还熟悉莎士比亚的其他戏剧。即使没有接触过这部戏剧的内容，他也完全有能力判断它在集体图书馆中的地位。

The example of Hamlet—arguably the greatest work in the English canon, and whose symbolic import is thus significant—shows the complexity inherent in the game of truth, a complexity that is compounded in the case of academia. In point of fact, a professor of English literature runs only a minimal risk in admitting—or pretending to admit— that he hasn’t read Hamlet. For one thing, no one is likely to believe him. And for another, the play is so well known that it is not necessary to have read it to speak about it. If it is true that he hasn’t “read” Hamlet, Ringbaum certainly has at his disposal a great deal of information about it and, in addition to Laurence Olivier’s movie adaptation, is familiar with other plays by Shakespeare. Even without having had access to its contents, he is perfectly well equipped to gauge its position within the collective library.

因此，如果 Ringbaum 没有犯下错误，即不允许他对游戏的了解模糊性持续存在，那么一切可能都会顺利进行。Ringbaum 犯的错误是，由于游戏的潜在暴力，也由于 Désirée 提到的心理冲突。在坚持自己的无知时，他将自己排除在我们通常允许自己与他人之间存在的不确定的文化空间之外，在这个空间内，我们默默地给予自己——同时也给予他们——无知的余地。我们当然在某种程度上知道，所有的文化素养，即使是最发达的文化素养，都是围绕着差距和裂痕构建的（Lodge 提到了 Howard 对“他的文化中的差距”的恐惧），但这些差距和裂痕并不会真正阻碍它作为一个信息体具有一定的一致性。

Thus everything might have gone swimmingly if Ringbaum—as a result of the latent violence of the game, but also due to the psychological conflict mentioned by Désirée—had not committed an error, which was to not allow the ambiguity on the subject of his knowledge of the play to persist. In insisting on his ignorance, he excluded himself from the indefinite cultural space that we generally allow to reign between ourselves and others, within which we tacitly accord ourselves—and simultaneously accord them—a margin of ignorance. We do of course know at some level that all cultural literacy, even the most highly developed, is constructed around gaps and fissures (Lodge mentions Howard’s fear of “a gap in his culture”) that are no real obstacle to its taking on a certain consistency as a body of information.

这种关于书籍（更广泛地说是文化）的交流领域可以被描述为虚拟图书馆14，因为这是一个由图像（尤其是自己的图像）而非书籍主导的空间，而且它不是一个基于现实的领域。它受制于许多规则，这些规则的目标是将其保持为一个共识空间，在这个空间中，书籍被书籍的虚构所取代。它也是一个游戏领域，与童年或戏剧领域没有什么不同，这种游戏只有在不违反主要规则的情况下才能进行。

This realm of communication about books—and more generally about culture—might be characterized as a virtual library,14 both because it is a space dominated by images (images of oneself, in particular) rather than books and because it is not a realm based in reality. It is subject to a number of rules whose goal is to maintain it as a consensual space in which books are replaced by fictions of books. It is also a realm of play, not unlike that of childhood or the theater, a kind of play that can be pursued only if the principal rules are not transgressed.

虚拟图书馆的一条隐含规则是，我们绝不能试图找出声称自己读过书的人实际上读了多少书，原因有二。首先，如果不是因为我们陈述的真实性存在一定程度的模糊性，而我们被迫清楚地回答关于我们到底读了什么的问题，虚拟图书馆的生活很快就会变得无法忍受。另一个原因是，真诚的含义本身就值得怀疑，因为正如我们所见，了解“读过一本书”的含义是非常困难的。

One of the implicit rules of the virtual library is that we must not attempt to find out the extent to which someone who claims he has read a book has actually done so, for two reasons. The first is that life in the virtual library would quickly become unlivable if not for a certain amount of ambiguity around the truth of our statements, and if we were instead forced to reply clearly to questions about what exactly we had read. The other reason is that the very notion of what sincerity would mean is questionable, since knowing what is meant by having read a book, as we have seen, is highly problematic.

通过宣称自己没有“读过” 《哈姆雷特》，通过说出真相——或者说他认为是真相——林鲍姆违反了虚拟图书馆的基本规则，即谈论自己没有读过的书是可以的。通过这样做，他通过残酷地暴露他的私人领域，将这种交流的空间变成了一个暴力场所。通过这一举动，他确实揭示了文化的真相，即文化是一个隐藏个人无知和知识碎片的剧场。通过这样做，他不仅暴露了自己的赤身裸体，还对其他人进行了某种精神强奸。

In declaring that he hasn’t “read” Hamlet, in telling the truth—or what he believes to be the truth—Ringbaum violates the fundamental rule of the virtual library, which is that it is fine to talk about books one hasn’t read. In so doing, he transforms the space of this exchange, through a brutal exposure of his private sphere, into a place of violence. Through this gesture, indeed, he unveils the truth of culture, which is that it is a theater charged with concealing individual ignorance and the fragmentation of knowledge. In so doing, he does not merely expose his nakedness but effects a kind of psychic rape of the others.

他所遭受的反应之激烈，与他在虚拟图书馆这个通常充满乐趣的舞台上所表现出的暴力程度相当。林鲍姆敢于说出他阅读莎士比亚的真相，同时也敢于说出我们谈论书籍的空间的性质，结果，他发现自己被驱逐了。他的制裁很快就来了，正如德西蕾在信的结尾所叙述的那样：



The violence of the reaction to which he will be subjected is commensurate with the violence he has exercised on the normally playful stage of the virtual library. In daring to utter the truth about his reading of Shakespeare, but also, as a consequence, about the nature of the space in which we talk about books, Ringbaum finds himself exiled from it. His sanction is not long in coming, as recounted by Désirée at the end of her letter:



你必须承认，这是个有趣的事件——但等我告诉你后续情况。三天后，霍华德·林鲍姆意外地未能通过评审，人们普遍认为这是因为英语系不敢给一个公开承认没有读过《哈姆雷特》的人终身教职。当然，这件事在整个校园里引起了热议，甚至《欣快州日报》上也有一段提到这件事。此外，由于这在系里造成了一个意想不到的空缺，他们重新考虑了克鲁普的案子，并最终给了他终身教职。我想他也没有读过《哈姆雷特》，但没人问。15



A piquant incident, you must admit—but wait till I tell you the sequel. Howard Ringbaum unexpectedly flunked his review three days later and it’s generally supposed that this was because the English Department dared not give tenure to a man who publicly admitted to not having read Hamlet. The story had been buzzed all round the campus, of course, and there was even a paragraph alluding to it in the Euphoric State Daily. Furthermore, as this created an unexpected vacancy in the Department, they’ve reconsidered the case of Kroop and offered him tenure after all. I don’t suppose he’s read Hamlet either, but nobody was asking.15



正如德西蕾所观察到的，接替林鲍姆的人——此时他别无选择，只能自杀——是否读过《哈姆雷特》的问题并不重要。重要的是，他不能走出虚拟书籍的中介空间，因为正是这种空间让我们得以与他人生活和交流。为了避免破坏这种像保护衣一样包裹着我们的共识空间，我们最好避免询问候选人，至少在这种情况下，他对莎士比亚的了解程度。

As Désirée observes, the question of whether the person replacing Ringbaum—who at this point has no other choice than to kill himself—has read Hamlet is secondary. What is important is that he not step out of the intermediary space of virtual books, which allows us to live and communicate with others. And rather than risk any violence to that consensual space, which cloaks us like a protective garment, we may well prefer to avoid asking a candidate, at least in this context, the exact extent of his knowledge of Shakespeare.

通过分析这个虚拟空间及其保护功能，我们清楚地看到，当我们敢于谈论自己没有读过的书时，我们不仅会感到羞耻，这种羞耻感与童年的情景有关，而且会对我们的自我形象以及我们向他人传达的形象构成更严重的威胁。在写作仍然很重要的知识界，我们读过的书是我们形象不可或缺的一部分，当我们冒险公开宣布我们内心图书馆的界限时，我们会对这一形象产生怀疑。

Through the analysis of this virtual space and its protective function, we see clearly that it is not just shame, linked to scenarios from childhood, that is in the offing when we dare to speak about books we haven’t read, but a more serious threat to our self-image and the image we convey to others. In the intellectual circles where writing still counts, the books we have read form an integral part of our image, and we call that image into question when we venture to publicly announce our inner library’s limits.

在这种文化背景下，无论读过还是没读过，书籍都是一种第二语言，我们可以用它来谈论自己、与他人交流，并在冲突中为自己辩护。和语言一样，书籍不仅能表达我们，还能让我们变得完整，通过各种摘录和重新加工的片段，补充我们个性中缺失的元素。

In this cultural context, books—whether read or unread— form a kind of second language to which we can turn to talk about ourselves, to communicate with others, and to defend ourselves in conflict. Like language, books serve to express us, but also to complete us, furnishing, through a variety of excerpted and reworked fragments, the missing elements of our personality.

和文字一样，书籍在呈现我们时，也会扭曲我们的本质。我们无法完全符合我们阅读所呈现的整体形象；无论这个形象让我们看起来比应有的更好还是更糟，在它背后，我们所有的特殊性都消失了。尤其是由于书籍在我们心中往往只是鲜为人知或被遗忘的片段，我们常常与作为我们公众形象的书籍格格不入；它们最终和任何其他语言一样不合适。

Like words, books, in representing us, also deform what we are. We cannot coincide completely with the image the totality of our reading presents; whether the image makes us look better or worse than we should, behind it all our particularities vanish. And especially since books are often present within us only as little-known or forgotten fragments, we are often out of phase with the books that are our public face; they are as inadequate in the end as any other language.

在谈论书籍时，我们发现自己交换的不仅仅是文化物品，还有我们自身需要的部分，以便在自恋自我受到威胁时巩固我们的连贯性。我们之所以感到羞耻，是因为我们的身份本身受到这些交流的威胁，因此，我们上演这些交流的虚拟空间必须保持模糊性和游戏性。

In talking about books, we find ourselves exchanging not so much cultural objects as the very parts of ourselves we need to shore up our coherence during these threats to our narcissistic selves. Our feelings of shame arise because our very identity is imperiled by these exchanges, whence the imperative that the virtual space in which we stage them remain marked by ambiguity and play.

从这个角度看，这种模棱两可的社会空间与学校截然相反——学校是一个充满暴力的领域，其驱动力在于幻想存在彻底阅读，学校的一切都被校准，以确定学生是否真正阅读了他们所谈论和接受质询的书籍。这样的目标最终是虚幻的，因为阅读并不遵循真与假的严格逻辑，不去掉模棱两可，也不去确定读者是否在说真话。

In this regard, this ambiguous social space is the opposite of school—a realm of violence driven by the fantasy that there exists such a thing as thorough reading, and a place where everything is calibrated to determine whether the students have truly read the books about which they speak and face interrogation. Such an aim is, in the end, illusory, for reading does not obey the hard logic of true and false, of waving off ambiguity and evaluating with certitude whether readers are telling the truth.

当林鲍姆坚持要把讨论书籍的游戏领域，那个不断谈判和时不时虚伪的空间，变成一个真理的领域时，他就把自己困在了一个会让他发疯的悖论中。他无法忍受讨论书籍的空间的优柔寡断，他坚持要把自己在其他玩家眼中看成最好的——考虑到斯瓦洛游戏的特殊性，这可以说是最糟糕的。他成功地按照自己的意愿，假设了这个对他来说不那么令人不安的形象，因为它不那么模棱两可；但最终，尽管他可能已经与自己和解，但这却让他走向了毁灭。

When Ringbaum insists on transforming that realm of play in which books are discussed, that space of constant negotiation and intermittent hypocrisy, into a realm of truth, he locks himself into a paradox that will lead him into madness. Unable to tolerate the indecisiveness of the space within which the discussion about books takes place, he insists on seeing himself reflected in the other players’ eyes as the best—which, given the particularity of Swallow’s game, is to say the worst. He succeeds, on his own terms, in assuming this image that is less unsettling to him, because it is less ambiguous; but in the end it leads him, reconciled with himself though he may be, to his ruin.

要想毫无羞耻地谈论自己没有读过的书，我们就必须摆脱家庭和学校传授和强加的文化素养无间隙的压迫性形象，因为我们可以终生努力追求这一形象，却永远无法与之相符。他人的真理不如对自己诚实重要，只有那些摆脱了必须显得有教养的义务的人才能做到，这种义务从内心压迫着我们，阻止我们做自己。



To speak without shame about books we haven’t read, we would thus do well to free ourselves of the oppressive image of cultural literacy without gaps, as transmitted and imposed by family and school, for we can strive toward this image for a lifetime without ever managing to coincide with it. Truth destined for others is less important than truthfulness to ourselves, something attainable only by those who free themselves from the obligation to seem cultivated, which tyrannizes us from within and prevents us from being ourselves.

It is a mobile sector of every culture’s collective library and is located at the point of intersection of the various inner libraries of each participant in the discussion.
