实施你的想法

X

Imposing Your Ideas

（巴尔扎克证明，将你的观点强加于书本的关键之一是要记住书本不是一个固定的物体，即使用绳子将它绑起来也不足以阻止它的运动）

(in which Balzac proves that one key to imposing your point of view on a book is to remember that the book is not a fixed object, and that even tying it up with string will not be sufficient to stop its motion)

因此，只要你有勇气，就没有理由不坦白地说你没有读过任何一本书，也没有理由不表达你对它的想法。没有读过一本书的经历是最常见的情况，只有毫无羞耻地接受我们不读书的事实，我们才能开始对真正重要的事感兴趣，这不是一本书，而是一个复杂的人际情境，这本书与其说是对象，不如说是结果。

AS LONG AS you have the courage, therefore, there is no reason not to say frankly that you haven’t read any particular book, nor to abstain from expressing your thoughts about it. The experience of not having read a book is the most common of scenarios, and only in accepting our non-reading without shame can we begin to take an interest in what is actually at stake, which is not a book but a complex interpersonal situation of which the book is less the object than the consequence.

事实上，书籍并非对周围所说的话不敏感，而是可能在我们交谈的瞬间就被改变。文本的这种流动性是虚拟图书馆这个模糊领域的第二大不确定性。它加剧了我们刚刚考察的不确定性——我们不确定那些谈论书籍的人到底有多了解书籍——这对于我们确定在这些情况下应采取什么策略至关重要。这些策略将更加重要，因为它们不依赖于书籍作为固定对象的形象，而是假设快速讨论的参与者，特别是如果他们有能力强加自己的观点，可以改变文本本身。

Books are not insensitive to what is said around them, in fact, but may be changed by it in just the time it takes us to have a conversation. This mobility of the text is the second great uncertainty of the ambiguous realm that is the virtual library. It compounds the kind of uncertainty we have just examined—our uncertainty about how well those who talk about books actually know them—and will be crucial to our delineation of what strategies to adopt in these situations. These strategies will be all the more relevant in that they will not depend on an image of books as fixed objects, but instead assume that the participants in a fast-moving discussion, especially if they have the strength to impose their own points of view, can change the text itself.

巴尔扎克小说《幻灭的幻想》1中的主人公吕西安·沙尔东是昂古莱姆一位药剂师的儿子，他梦想着找回母亲的贵族姓氏，他的母亲出生时姓鲁班普雷。他爱上了当地贵族巴日东夫人，并跟随她来到巴黎，留下了他最好的朋友、印刷工大卫·塞夏尔，后者娶了吕西安的妹妹伊芙。但他前往首都也是为了在文学界成名，他带来了他的第一批作品，一本名为《玛格丽特》2的诗集和一部名为《查理九世的射手》3的历史小说。

Lucien Chardon, the hero of Balzac’s novel Lost Illusions,1 is the son of an apothecary from Angoulême who dreams of retrieving the aristocratic name of his mother, who was born de Rubempré. Having fallen in love with a woman of the local nobility, Madame de Bargeton, he follows her to Paris, leaving behind his best friend, the printer David Séchard, who has married Lucien’s sister Eve. But he is also heading for the capital with an eye to making his name in the world of letters, and he brings with him his first texts, a collection of poems called Les Marguerites2 and a historical novel called L’Archer de Charles IX.3

在巴黎，吕西安进入了控制出版和新闻界的知识分子小圈子，并很快发现了文学和艺术产生的环境的现实——与他的幻想相去甚远。在与他的一位新朋友、记者艾蒂安·卢斯托的一次谈话中，他残酷地揭示了文学和艺术的真实本质。卢斯托缺钱，被迫将几本书转售给一个名叫巴贝特的书商。其中几本书的书页甚至没有被剪掉，尽管卢斯托曾向一家报纸的编辑承诺过对这些书进行评论：



In Paris, Lucien finds his way into the small circle of intellectuals in control of publishing and the press and quickly discovers the reality—far removed from his illusions—of the milieu in which literature and art are produced. Its true nature is brutally revealed to him in a conversation with one of his new friends, a journalist named Étienne Lousteau. Lousteau, short of money, is forced to resell several books to a bookseller named Barbet. The pages of several of them turn out to have not even been cut, even though Lousteau has promised reviews of them to the editor of a newspaper:



巴贝特浏览了这些书，仔细检查了书边和封面。

Barbet looked over the books, carefully examining the edges and the covers.

“哦！它们完好无损！”卢斯托惊呼道。“ 《埃及游记》4的书页没有被剪掉，保罗·德·科克的书页也没有被剪掉，杜康日的书页也没有被剪掉，壁炉架上的《象征主义的思考》 5也一样。我把那本书也附上，里面的神话故事太无聊了。我把它给你，这样我就不用看着成千上万的螨虫从里面爬出来了。”

“Oh! They’re in perfect condition!” exclaimed Lousteau. “The leaves of Travels in Egypt4 aren’t cut, nor the Paul de Kock, nor the Ducange, nor the one on the mantelpiece, Reflections on Symbolism.5 I’ll throw that one in, the mythology in it is so boring. I’ll give it to you so that I needn’t watch thousands of mites swarming out of it.”

“但是，”吕西安问道，“你要怎样写评论呢？”

“But,” asked Lucien, “how will you write your reviews on them?”

巴贝特惊讶地看了吕西安一眼，然后又笑着看着卢斯托。“很明显，这位先生并不是一个不幸的文人。” 6



Barbet gave Lucien a glance of profound astonishment and then looked back at Lousteau with a snigger. “It’s plain to see that this gentleman hasn’t the misfortune to be a man of letters.”6



吕西安很惊讶有人会为一本自己从未读过的书写一篇文章，他忍不住问卢斯托他打算如何履行对报纸编辑的承诺：



Surprised that one might devote an article to a book one hasn’t read, Lucien cannot resist asking Lousteau how he plans to honor his promise to the newspaper editor:



“但是你的评论文章怎么办？”当他们驱车前往皇家宫殿时，吕西安问道。

“But what about your review article?” asked Lucien as they drove away to the Palais-Royal.

“呸！你根本不知道这些文章是怎么写出来的。拿《埃及游记》来说吧：我打开书，随便读了一点，没有剪页，就发现了法语中的十一个错误。我要写一篇专栏文章，说即使作者能解释埃及鹅卵石上刻的鸭子语言，他们称之为方尖碑，但他不懂自己的语言——我会向他证明这一点。我要说，他不应该谈论自然历史和古迹，而应该只关心埃及的未来、文明的进步、如何让埃及归附法国，法国在征服埃及后又失去它，仍然可以在道德上占据优势。然后是几页爱国主义的废话，整篇文章都夹杂着对马赛、黎凡特和我们贸易利益的长篇大论。” 7



“Pooh! You’ve no idea how they’re dashed off. Take Travels in Egypt: I opened the book and read a bit here and there without cutting the pages, and I discovered eleven mistakes in the French. I shall write a column to the effect that even if the author can interpret the duck-lingo carved on the Egyptian pebbles they call obelisks, he doesn’t know his own language—and I shall prove it to him. I shall say that instead of talking about natural history and antiquities he ought only to have concerned himself with the future of Egypt, the progress of civilization, the means of winning Egypt over to France, which, after conquering it and then losing it again, could still establish a moral ascendancy over it. Then a few pages of patriotic twaddle, the whole interlarded with tirades on Marseilles, the Levant and our trading interests.”7



当吕西安问卢斯托，如果作者讨论政治，他会怎么做时，他的朋友毫不犹豫地回答说，他会责备作者用政治话题让读者感到无聊，而不是通过关注乡村风景如画的方面来关注艺术。无论如何，他最终依靠另一种方法：他让女友弗洛琳（一位女演员和“世界上最伟大的小说读者”）阅读这本书。只有当她表示自己对所谓的“作者的句子”感到厌烦时，他才开始认真对待这本书，并要求书商再买一本，以便他可以写一篇好评文章。

When Lucien asks what Lousteau would have done if the author had discussed politics, his friend replies without missing a beat that he would have reproached the writer for boring his reader with political talk, rather than concerning himself with Art by focusing on the picturesque aspects of the country. In any event, he relies in the end on another method: he gets his girlfriend, Florine, an actress and “the greatest reader of novels in the world,” to read the book. Only when she declares herself bored by what she calls “author’s sentences” does he start to take the book seriously and ask the bookseller for a new copy so that he can write a favorable article.

在这里，我们再次遇到了一些我们已经确定的不读书的类型，我们要么在完全不了解的情况下猜测一本书的内容；要么浏览它；要么根据别人的意见来形成自己的观点。尽管如此，吕西安对他朋友的批评方法还是有点惊讶，并向他坦白了自己的惊讶：

Here we encounter once again some of the varieties of non-reading that we have already identified, in which we either surmise what a book is about without knowing it at all; skim through it; or base our opinions on the opinions of others. Lucien, nonetheless, is a bit surprised by his friend’s critical method and confesses his astonishment to him:

“天哪！但是批判呢，批判的神圣任务呢？”吕西安说，他仍然深受晚会教义的影响。

“Great Heavens! But what about criticism, the sacred task of criticism?” said Lucien, still imbued with the doctrines of the Cénacle.

“我亲爱的朋友，”卢斯托说。“批评就像一把刷子，你千万不能用在脆弱的材料上——它会把它们撕成碎片。现在听着，我们别再谈正事了。你看到这个标记了吗？”他指着《玛格丽特》的手稿问道。 “我在绳子和纸张之间画了一条线。如果达里阿读了你的手稿，他肯定无法把绳子放回那条线上。所以你的手稿就像被封住了一样。对于你想要做的实验来说，这是一个不错的躲避方法。还有一件事，只要记住，你不会独自一人进入那个血汗工厂，也没有赞助商：你会像那些年轻的有抱负的人一样，他们去了十家出版商，才找到一家愿意给他们一把椅子的出版商……” 8

“My dear chap,” said Lousteau. “Criticism’s a scrubbing-brush which you mustn’t use on flimsy materials—it would tear them to shreds. Now listen, let’s stop talking shop. You see this mark?” he asked, pointing to the manuscript of Les Marguerites. “I’ve inked a line in between the string and the paper. If Dauriat reads your manuscript, he certainly won’t be able to put the string back along the line. So your manuscript is as good as sealed. It’s not a bad dodge for the experiment you want to make. One more thing, just remember that you won’t get into that sweatshop by yourself and without a sponsor: you’d be like those young hopefuls who go round to ten publishers before they find one who’ll even offer them a chair . . .”8

因此，卢斯托毫不留情地想要挫败他的朋友的幻想，他建议卢西安在将他的诗稿提交给巴黎一家最重要的出版商之前，设计一个测试——用一根沾满墨水的绳子将书装订起来——不仅可以测试达里安是否读过这本书，而且可以测试他是否打开过它。

Thus does Lousteau pitilessly pursue the task of disillusioning his friend, advising him, before Lucien submits his poetry manuscript to one of the most important publishers in Paris, to devise a test—a piece of ink-stained string that binds the book shut—of not only whether Dauriat has read it, but whether he has even opened it.

当吕西安回去见达里阿并询问他是否读过这些诗时，达里阿几乎不抱有任何出版的希望：



When Lucien returns to see Dauriat and asks whether he’s read the poems, Dauriat gives him hardly any hope of being published:



“确实如此，”达里阿特说，像东方君主一样在扶手椅上向前倾身。“我浏览了这本诗集，并找了一个有品味、有鉴赏力的人来阅读，因为我并不自称是诗歌鉴赏家。我，我的朋友，购买现成的名声就像英国人购买现成的爱情一样。我的孩子，你是一位伟大的诗人，也是一位英俊的年轻人。作为一个诚实的人——请注意，我不是说作为一个出版商——我可以保证你的十四行诗非常出色，你在其中投入了大量精力，当一个人有灵感和热情时，这是非常罕见的。简而言之，你知道如何押韵——这是现代流派的品质之一。你的《玛格丽特》是一本很好的书，但卖不出去钱，我只能从事非常大的工作。” 9

“Indeed I have,” said Dauriat, leaning forward in his armchair like an oriental potentate. “I’ve glanced through the collection of poems and got a man of taste, a good judge, to read them, for I don’t claim to be a connoisseur in poetry. I, my friend, buy ready-made reputations as an Englishman buys ready-made love. You are as great a poet, my boy, as you are a handsome youngster. On my word as an honest man—I don’t mean as a publisher, mind you— your sonnets are magnificent and you’ve put good work into them, a rare enough thing when one has inspiration and verve. In short, you know how to rhyme—one of the qualities of the modern school. Your Marguerites make a fine book, but there’s no money in them, and I can only go in for very big undertakings.”9

尽管达里阿拒绝接受手稿，也没有声称自己已经通读了整本书，但他仍然坚持认为，自己对这本书有所了解；他甚至可以对一些文体提出一些评论，例如，对韵律的质量提出一些评论。不过，卢斯托谨慎地将手稿封存起来，让两位朋友得以仔细查看：



While he rejects the manuscript and does not claim to have read it all the way through, Dauriat nevertheless maintains that he has gained some acquaintance with the book; he is even able to make a few stylistic remarks, on the quality of the rhymes, for example. But Lousteau’s precaution of sealing the manuscript enables the two friends to take a closer look:



“你带了手稿吗？”吕西安冷冷地问道。

“Have you the manuscript with you?” asked Lucien, coldly.

“就在这儿，我的朋友，”达里阿回答道，此时他正用一种异常甜美的语调和吕西安说话。

“Here it is, my friend,” repled Dauriat, who was now adopting singularly sugary tones with Lucien.

吕西安接过卷轴，没有看绳子的位置，他确信达里阿特已经读过《玛格丽特》 。他和卢斯托一起出去了，没有表现出沮丧或不满。达里阿特和两位朋友在商店里走来走去，谈论着他的报纸和卢斯托的报纸。吕西安漫不经心地摆弄着《玛格丽特》的手稿。

Lucien took the scroll without looking to see the position of the string, so certain it seemed that Dauriat had read the Marguerites. He went out with Lousteau without appearing either dismayed or discontented. Dauriat walked through the shop with the two friends talking about his newspaper and that of Lousteau. Lucien was unconcernedly toying with the manuscript of the Marguerites.

“你认为达里阿读过你的十四行诗，或者让人读过你的十四行诗吗？”艾蒂安低声问吕西安。

“Do you believe Dauriat read your sonnets or had them read?” Étienne whispered to Lucien.

“是的，”吕西安说。

“Yes,” said Lucien.

“看看那些‘海豹’！”

“Look at the ‘seals’!”

吕西安发现墨线和线已经完美地结合在一起了。10



Lucien perceived that the ink-lines and the string were in a state of perfect conjunction.10



尽管没有打开过手稿，达里阿还是毫不费力地阐述了他对这本选集的初步看法，并提供了进一步的细节：



Despite not having opened the manuscript, Dauriat has no trouble elaborating on his initial opinion of the anthology and providing further details:



“你最关注的是哪首十四行诗？”吕西安问出版商，他强忍着怒火，脸色苍白。

“Which sonnet did you most particularly notice?” Lucien asked the publisher, turning pale with suppressed rage.

“这些都值得一读，我的朋友，”达里阿回答道。“但关于雏菊的那篇非常精彩，结尾非常微妙和细腻。由此我猜想你的散文一定会获得成功。” 11

“They are all worthy of notice, my friend,” Dauriat replied. “But the one on the marguerite is delicious and ends with a very subtle and delicate thought. By that I divined what success your prose is bound to obtain.”11

卢斯托和吕西安继续对话，再次证明了谈论一本书并不需要阅读它。卢斯托向他的朋友提议，为了报复出版商的侮辱，卢西安应该写一篇煽动性的文章，攻击作家纳坦的一本书，纳坦是达里埃所推崇的作家。但这本书的质量如此明显，以至于卢西安不知道如何开始批评它。卢斯托笑着解释说，现在是时候让卢西安学习他的手艺了，并掌握将一本书的美感变成缺陷的杂技能力——也就是说，将一部杰作变成“平淡无奇的愚蠢作品” 。12

That it is not necessary to read a book to speak about it is illustrated a second time as Lucien and Lousteau continue their dialogue. Lousteau proposes to his friend that as revenge against the publisher’s insult, Lucien should write an incendiary article attacking a book by the writer Nathan, an author championed by Dauriat. But the quality of the book is so patently apparent that Lucien has no idea how to begin criticizing it. Laughing, Lousteau explains that it is time for Lucien to learn his trade, and with it the acrobatic ability to change the beauties of a book into defects—that is, to transform a masterpiece into an “insipid bit of stupidity.”12

卢斯托随后向他展示了如何诋毁一本人们最推崇的书。他的方法是发表开场白，说出“真相”并赞扬这本书。公众对这种积极的开场感到高兴，并倾向于信任，会认为批评家是公正的，并准备效仿他的做法。

Lousteau then shows him how to denigrate a book that one holds in the highest regard. His method is to make an opening statement in which one tells the “truth” and praises the book. The public, pleased by this positive beginning and inclined to be trusting, will judge the critic to be impartial and prepare to follow his lead.

在此关头，卢斯托试图表明，纳森的作品是法国文学陷入的一种趋势的典型代表。这种文学趋势的特点是过度依赖描述和对话——换句话说，过多的图像——而忽视了思想，而思想在历史上一直主导着法国文学的伟大作品。卢斯托认为，可以肯定的是，沃尔特·斯科特是杰出的，但“只有真正独创的思想才有空间”，他对后继者的影响是有害的。13

At this juncture, Lousteau endeavors to show that Nathan’s work is characteristic of a trend within which French literature has become trapped. This literary trend is characterized by an overreliance on description and dialogue—an excess of images, in other words—at the expense of thought, which has historically dominated the great works of French literature. To be sure, Lousteau argues, Walter Scott is remarkable, but “there’s room only for truly original minds,” and his influence on his successors has been deleterious.13

这种“思想文学”和“图像文学”之间的对立随后被用在了纳森身上，纳森只是一个模仿者，只有表面上的才华。如果他的作品值得称赞，那么它也是危险的，因为它通过鼓励众多小作家模仿这种肤浅的形式，将文学开放给暴民。为了与这种颓废形成对比，卢斯托建议，吕西安应该唤起那些抵制浪漫主义入侵、继续追随伏尔泰脚步、捍卫思想、反对图像的作家的斗争。

This opposition between a “literature of ideas” and a “literature of images” is then turned against Nathan, who is but an imitator and has only the outward trappings of talent. If his work is deserving, it is also dangerous, since it opens literature up to the mob by spurring a multitude of minor authors to imitate this facile form. As a counterpoint to this decadence, Lousteau suggests, Lucien should invoke the struggle of those writers resisting the romantic invasion and continuing in the footsteps of Voltaire by defending ideas against images.

这绝不是卢斯托处理一本书的唯一方法。他还向吕西安展示了其他解决方案，例如“社论”，即“将这本书扼杀在两个承诺之间”。14根据这一策略，文章首先宣布对这本书的评论，然后陷入一般性的考虑中，这迫使将真正的批评推迟到后续文章中，而后续文章永远不会出现。

And by no means is this the only method in Lousteau’s arsenal for dispatching a book. He demonstrates to Lucien other solutions as well, such as the “leading article” that entails “smothering the book between two promises.”14 According to this strategy, the article starts off by announcing a commentary on the book, then loses itself in general considerations that necessitate postponing the real critique to a subsequent article, which will never appear.

纳森的书的例子似乎与我们之前研究过的例子不同，因为吕西安试图讨论的是一本他实际上读过的书。但卢斯托在这里的策略背后的原则与吕西安未读的诗歌或《埃及游记》的原则相同：一本书的内容与这本书应得的评论几乎没有关系。在巴尔扎克的这个例子中，在某种最终的悖论或对刺激的渴望中，甚至有可能开始阅读它。

The example of Nathan’s book would seem to be a departure from the previous ones we have studied, since Lucien is trying to discuss a book that he has in fact read. But the principle behind Lousteau’s strategy here is the same one that applies to Lucien’s unread poems or to Travels in Egypt: that the content of a book has little bearing on the commentary the book deserves. In this example from Balzac, it even becomes possible, in a kind of final paradox or hunger for provocation, to begin reading it.

在巴尔扎克的《埃及游记》以及吕西安或纳森的作品中，评论都与书无关，而是与作者有关​​。作者的价值，他在文学体系中的地位，决定了书的价值。正如卢斯托明确地对吕西安说的那样，有时甚至只是出版商受到了牵连：“你在这里写的不是一篇反对纳森的文章，而是一篇反对达乌里阿的文章：这需要用镐头。镐头会擦过一篇好作品，但却能直接切入一篇坏作品：在第一种情况下，它只会伤害出版商；在第二种情况下，它为公众提供了服务。” 15

In all three cases in Balzac—for Travels in Egypt, as well as for the books by Lucien or Nathan—the commentary is not related to the book, but to the author. It is the author’s value, his place in the literary system, that determines the value of the book. As Lousteau says explicitly to Lucien, it may at times even be just the publisher who is implicated: “What you’re writing here isn’t an article against Nathan, but one against Dauriat: that calls for a pickaxe. A pickaxe glances off a fine work, but it cuts right through to a bad one: in the first case, it hurts only the publisher; in the second case, it does the public a service.”15

此外，作家在文学体系中的地位是可以改变的，这意味着一本书的价值也是可以改变的。吕西安很快就亲眼看到了这一点，因为当达里阿特读到纳森的书的文章时，出版吕西安的诗集的任何困难都消失了。书商甚至到他家签署了和平协议：



An author’s place in the literary system is eminently malleable, moreover, which means that the value of a book is malleable as well. Lucien soon sees this for himself, for as soon as Dauriat reads his article on Nathan’s book, any difficulty about publishing Lucien’s book of poems vanishes. The bookseller even travels to his home to sign their peace agreement:



他掏出一本精致的皮夹，从里面抽出三张一千法郎的钞票，放在一个盘子里，像妓女一样谄媚地递给吕西安，说：“先生，您满意了吗？”

He pulled out an elegant pocket-book, drew three thousand-franc notes from it, put them on a plate and offered them to Lucien with the obsequiousness of a courtesan and said: “Does that satisfy you, Monsieur?”

“是的，”诗人说。看到这笔意外的钱，他感到前所未有的幸福。他忍住了，但他想唱歌，想跳上跳下。他相信巫师和阿拉丁神灯的存在；简而言之，他相信他有一个天才。

“Yes,” said the poet. A wave of bliss hitherto unexperienced swept over him at the sight of this unexpected sum. He held himself in, but he wanted to sing, to leap up and down. He believed in the existence of wizards and Aladdin’s wonderful lamp; in short he believed he had a genius at his command.

“那么玛格丽特系列将属于我了？”出版商问道。“但你永远不会攻击我的任何出版物吧？”

“So the Marguerites will belong to me?” asked the publisher. “But you’ll never attack any of my publications?”

“玛格丽特是你的，但我不能抵押我的笔。它是我朋友的，就像他们的笔是我的一样。”

“The Marguerites are yours, but I can’t pledge my pen. It belongs to my friends, just as theirs belongs to me.”

“但毕竟，你正在成为我的作家之一。我所有的作家都是我的朋友。你不会在我没有收到任何攻击警告的情况下损害我的事业，以便我可以预防它们吧？”

“But after all, you are becoming one of my authors. All my authors are my friends. You’ll do no damage to my affairs without my being warned of any attacks so that I can forestall them?”

“同意。”

“Agreed.”

“祝你未来名声大噪！”达里阿举起酒杯说道。

“Here’s to your future fame!” said Dauriat, raising his glass.

“显然你读过《玛格丽特》，”吕西安说。16



“Obviously you’ve read the Marguerites,” said Lucien.16



达里阿没有受到他没有读过《玛格丽特》的暗示的影响。他对这本书的评价只是因为作者的改变而改变：



Dauriat is not at all affected by the allusion to his non-reading of Les Marguerites. His judgment of it has changed simply because the author of the work has changed:



“我的孩子，在不了解玛格丽特诗集的情况下就买下它们，这是出版商能允许自己接受的最好的奉承。六个月后，你就会成为一名伟大的诗人；人们会为你写文章。人们都怕你，所以我不需要做任何事情就能卖出你的书。今天我和四天前一样，还是那个商人。改变的不是我，而是你。上周，我根本不会为你的十四行诗买单，但你今天的地位让它们变得珍贵而稀有。”

“My boy, buying the Marguerites without knowing them is the finest flattery a publisher can permit himself. In six months you’ll be a great poet; articles will be written about you. People are afraid of you, so I need do nothing to get your book sold. I’m the same business man today as I was four days ago. It’s not I who have changed, it’s you. Last week I wouldn’t have given a fig leaf for your sonnets, but your position today turns them into something rich and rare.”

“哦，好吧，”吕西安说，他现在处于一种嘲讽和迷人的挑逗状态，因为他感受到了拥有一位美丽的情妇和获得成功的保证所带来的苏丹般的快乐。“即使你没有读过我的十四行诗，你也读过我的文章。”

“Oh well,” said Lucien, being now in a mocking and charmingly provocative frame of mind since he felt all the pleasures of a sultan in possessing a beautiful mistress and in being assured of success. “Even if you haven’t read my sonnets, you’ve read my article.”

“是的，我的朋友。不然我怎么会这么快就赶来呢？不幸的是，这篇文章写得非常好，太糟糕了。” 17

“Yes, my friend. Otherwise should I have come along so promptly? Unfortunately, it’s very fine, this terrible article.”17

吕西安的幻想还未破灭。就在文章发表的当晚，卢斯托向他解释说，他刚刚遇到了绝望的纳森，与他为敌太危险了。因此，他建议吕西安“对他大加赞赏”。18 吕西安惊讶地发现，现在有人要求他写一篇关于他刚刚批评过的一本书的正面文章，而他的朋友们再次觉得他的天真很可笑。这时，他得知其中一位朋友采取了预防措施，去了报社，将他文章上的签名改为一个最不具妥协性的字母C。因此，没有什么可以阻止吕西安为另一家报纸写另一篇文章，这次用字母L签名。

Lucien has further disillusionments yet in store. The very evening his article is published, Lousteau explains to him that he has just met Nathan, who is desperate, and that it is too dangerous to have him as one’s enemy. He thus advises Lucien to “squirt showers of praise in his face.”18 Lucien is astonished that he is now being asked for a positive article about a book he has just criticized, while his friends once again find his naïveté hilarious. At this point, he learns that one of them had taken the precaution of going by the newspaper offices and changing the signature on his article to a minimally compromising letter C. Thus there is nothing to prevent Lucien from writing another article for a different newspaper, and signing this time with the letter L.

但吕西安想不出任何可以补充他原有观点的东西。因此，他的另一位朋友布朗代就承担了证明卢斯托先前提出的论点的反面的任务，并向吕西安解释说：“每个想法都有正面和反面，没有人敢说哪一面是哪一面。在思想领域，一切都是双向的。想法是双面的。雅努斯是批评的守护神，也是天才的象征。” 19因此，布朗代建议，在第二篇文章中，吕西安应该攻击一种时髦的理论，即存在一种思想文学和另一种图像文学，而最精致的文学艺术显然承担着将两者结合起来的义务。

But Lucien can’t think of anything to add to his original opinion. It thus falls to Blondet, another of his friends, to demonstrate the reverse of the argument that Lousteau had previously offered, and to explain to Lucien that “every idea has its front side and its reverse side, and no one can presume to state which side is which. Everything is bilateral in the domain of thought. Ideas are two-sided. Janus is the tutelary deity of criticism and the symbol of genius.”19 Blondet thus suggests that in this second article, Lucien should attack the fashionable theory positing the existence of one literature of ideas and another literature of images, whereas clearly the most refined literary art assumes the obligation of combining the two.

最后，布隆代甚至建议吕西安不要只写署名“C.”和“L.”的两篇文章，还要写第三篇，署名“de Rubempré”，以调和前两篇文章，表明围绕内森这本书的争论之广确实表明了它的重要性。

As a final touch, Blondet even proposes to Lucien that he not limit himself to two articles signed “C.” and “L.” but compose a third, this time signed “de Rubempré,” which would reconcile the two others by demonstrating that the breadth of the debates about Nathan’s book are a sure sign of its importance.

巴尔扎克的这些场景将我所说的虚拟图书馆的特征放大到了漫画的程度。在巴尔扎克所描述的知识分子环境中，唯一重要的是演员的社会地位。书籍本身被视为作者的影子，没有干预，也没有人在做出判断之前努力阅读它们，无论是评论家还是出版商。事实上，书籍本身并没有受到威胁；它们已被其他中介对象所取代，这些中介对象本身没有内容，仅由轰炸它们的不稳定的社会和心理力量定义。

These scenes from Balzac magnify the features of what I have called the virtual library to the point of caricature. In the intellectual milieu that Balzac describes, the only thing that matters is the social positions of the actors. Treated as mere shadows of their authors, the books themselves make no intervention, and nor does anyone make the effort to read them before issuing a judgment, whether as critic or publisher. Indeed, the books themselves are not at stake; they have been replaced by other intermediary objects that have no content in themselves, and which are defined solely by the unstable social and psychological forces that bombard them.

就像洛奇的游戏一样，羞耻感仍然是虚拟图书馆组织的重要组成部分，但讽刺的是，在这种情况下，它的功能却被颠倒了。羞辱不再威胁那些没有读过书的人，而是威胁那些读过书的人；阅读被视为一项有辱人格的任务，可以留给半上流社会的女人去做。但这个空间仍然围绕着羞耻感组织起来，由此产生的世界，除了表面上的嬉戏之外，在心理上是非常暴力的。

As in Lodge’s game, shame remains an essential component in the organization of the virtual library, but in this case its function is ironically reversed. Humiliation no longer threatens the individual who hasn’t read a book, but the one who has; reading is seen as a degrading task that may be left to a woman of the demimonde. But this space still remains organized around the feeling of shame, and the resulting world, beyond its apparent playfulness, is remarkably psychically violent.

在巴尔扎克和洛奇的作品中，权力都是争夺权力的。权力在文本接受中的重要性在《幻灭》中显而易见，因为它与一本书的文学价值直接相关。好评有助于权力，反之，权力保证好评。它甚至可以证实文本的质量，就像吕西安的例子一样。

In Balzac as in Lodge, the game is played for positions of power. The importance of power in the reception of texts is easy to perceive in Lost Illusions, for it is directly and immediately connected to a book’s literary value. A favorable review contributes to power, while inversely, power guarantees favorable reviews. It can even serve to confirm, as in Lucien’s case, the quality of the text.

某种程度上，巴尔扎克所描述的世界与洛奇的世界截然相反。英国学术界以不读书为禁忌（以至于敢于炫耀这种禁忌的人立即被排除在文化空间之外），而巴尔扎克对禁忌的超越是如此普遍，以至于不读书成为规则，而读书最终也成为一种禁忌，这被认为是一种耻辱。

In a way, the universe described by Balzac is the reverse of Lodge’s. Whereas the world of the British academic is characterized by the taboo of non-reading (so much so that the character who dares to flaunt it is promptly excluded from the cultural space), the transgression of the taboo is so generalized in Balzac that non-reading becomes the rule, and a kind of taboo ends up being placed on reading, which is considered humiliating.

这个世界普遍存在两种越轨行为。首先，批评家们不打开书本就谈论书籍是被允许的，甚至被推荐，而当吕西安提出情况可以有所不同时，他遭到了嘲笑。不读书的越轨行为在这里如此普遍，以至于最终它不再是一种越轨行为；甚至没有人再想过读书了。只有当一个不熟悉新闻行为的人进入文学界时，文学界的常客才会暂时唤起阅读的可能性——然后又立即拒绝它。

Two forms of transgression are pervasive in this world. First, it is permitted, and even recommended, that critics should speak about books without opening them, and Lucien is subjected to ridicule when he suggests that the situation could proceed otherwise. The transgression of non-reading is such a commonplace here that in the end it is no longer a transgression; no one even thinks of reading a book anymore. Only when a person unacquainted with journalistic behavior enters the world of letters do its habitués momentarily evoke the possibility of reading—and then only to reject it immediately.

第一种越轨行为是普遍不读书，第二种越轨行为则更为严重，即坚持你对一本书的任何看法都是同样有效的。在这个世界上，打开一本书来谈论它是可笑的，但只要你能为它辩护，任何观点都是可以的。从某种意义上说，书籍本身已经沦为纯粹的借口，不复存在了。

This first transgression, that of universal non-reading, is compounded by a second one, which insists that any opinion you sustain about a book is equally valid. In a world where opening a book in order to talk about it is laughable, any opinion is fine as long as you can defend it. The book itself, reduced to pure pretext, has, in a sense, ceased to exist.

这种对谈论书籍的传统规则的双重违反是一个反常社会的标志，在这个社会里，所有的书籍，以及对书籍的所有无休止的可逆判断，最终都与其他书籍等同。但在这种情况下，吕西安的朋友所持的立场，即使看起来像诡辩，也揭示了关于阅读和我们谈论书籍的方式的某些真理。

This double transgression of the conventional rules of talking about books is a sign of a perverse society wherein all books, and all the endlessly reversible judgments of books, end up being the equivalent of any others. But the position held by Lucien’s friends in this case, even if it resembles sophistry, nevertheless reveals certain truths about reading and the way we talk about books.

如果这两篇文章是关于同一本书的话，卢斯托和布朗代鼓励吕西安写出相互矛盾的文章的态度会令人震惊。巴尔扎克的意思是，在这两种情况下，情况并不完全相同。可以肯定的是，实体书本身仍然与它本身相同，但一旦纳森的社会地位发生变化，它就不再代表相同的关系纽带。同样，一旦吕西安获得了一定的社会地位，他的《玛格丽特》就变成了一本完全不同的诗集。

Lousteau and Blondet’s attitude in encouraging Lucien to write contradictory articles would be shocking if the two articles were about exactly the same book. What Balzac is suggesting is that it is not exactly the same in the two cases. To be sure, the physical book remains identical to itself, but no longer represents the same knot of relationships once Nathan’s position in society evolves. Similarly, once Lucien has attained a certain social position, his Marguerites becomes a rather different collection of poems.

在每种情况下，书籍都不会发生实质性变化，但它会根据集体图书馆中的情况进行调整。巴尔扎克提醒我们注意的是背景的重要性。当然，他讽刺了这种重要性，但他的描绘同样具有展示背景决定性的价值。让背景成为等式的一部分意味着要记住，一本书并不是一劳永逸地固定下来的，而是一个移动的物体，它的移动性在一定程度上取决于围绕它编织的权力关系集。

In each case, the book does not change materially, but it undergoes modifications to its situation in the collective library. What Balzac is calling our attention to is the importance of context. He caricatures this importance, certainly, but his portrait has the merit all the same of showing how determining it can be. To allow context to become part of the equation means remembering that a book is not fixed once and for all but is a moving object, and that its mobility is in part a function of the set of power relations woven around it.

如果作者变了，书也变了，我们至少可以说我们面对的始终是同一个读者吗？从吕西安在与卢斯托交谈后对内森这本书的看法迅速改变来看，这一点再清楚不过了：



If the author changes and the book changes as well, can it at least be said that we are always dealing with the same reader? Nothing is less clear, judging by the speed with which Lucien alters his opinion of Nathan’s book after his talk with Lousteau:



吕西安听了卢斯托的话，惊呆了：他突然明白了一切，意识到了一些他从未猜到过的文学真理。

Lucien was stupefied as he listened to Lousteau’s words: the scales fell from his eyes and he became alive to literary truths of which he had not even guessed.

“但是你告诉我的，”他大声说道，“充满了理由和意义。”

“But what you tell me,” he exclaimed, “is full of reason and relevance.”

“如果不是，你怎么能攻击内森的书呢？”卢斯托说。20



“If it were not, how could you make an attack on Nathan’s book?” said Lousteau.20



因此，与卢斯托的简短交谈足以让吕西安对纳森的书产生不同的看法，甚至无需重新阅读。因此，问题不在于这本书本身（因为吕西安不知道如果他重读这本书会有什么感觉），而在于社会上对这本书的评论。这个新观点已经成为他自己的观点，他再也无法修改它了，当卢斯托向他提议他应该写第二篇好评时，他试图回避，声称他现在连一句赞美的话都写不出来。然而，他的朋友们介入，再次让他心烦意乱，让他重新回到最初的观点：



A brief conversation with Lousteau is thus sufficient for Lucien to form a different opinion about Nathan’s book, and that without even looking at it anew. It is not the book as such that is in play, therefore (since Lucien cannot know what he would feel if he were to reread it), but the interplay of comments about it in society. That new opinion becomes so much his own that he can no longer modify it, and when Lousteau proposes to him that he ought to write a second, favorable article, he tries to recuse himself, claiming that he is now incapable of writing a single word of praise. His friends, however, intervene to unsettle him once more and give him fresh access to his initial sentiment:



第二天早上，发现前一天的想法又萌芽了，就像所有头脑充满活力但能力尚未得到充分锻炼的人一样。吕西安从构思这篇新文章中获得了乐趣，并满怀热情地开始写作。他笔下流淌着所有源于悖论的精彩妙语。他诙谐幽默，甚至对文学中的情感、思想和意象有了新的思考。为了赞美内森，他巧妙地捕捉了人们对这本书的第一印象…… 21

Next morning, it turned out that the previous day’s ideas had germinated, as happens with all minds which are bursting with sap and whose faculties have as yet had little exercise. Lucien derived pleasure from thinking out this new article and set about it with enthusiasm. From his pen flowed all the fine sallies born of paradox. He was witty and mocking, he even rose to new reflexions on feeling, ideas, and imagery in literature. With subtle ingenuity, in order to praise Nathan, he captured the first impressions about the book . . . 21

因此，我们可能会想，吕西安是否更担心的是他自己的内在流动性以及他正在一点一点发现的内在流动性，而不是书籍的流动性。他可以毫无伤害地、连续地甚至同时地采取布隆代向他提出的不同的智力和心理立场。令人不安的不是他朋友对书籍的蔑视，而是他自己对他人和自己的不忠诚，这种不忠诚最终将导致他的垮台。22

We may thus wonder whether Lucien is anxious less about the mobility of the book than about his own inner mobility and what he is little by little discovering about it. He can assume the different intellectual and psychic positions that Blondet proposes to him without any harm, successively and even simultaneously. It is less his friends’ contempt for books that is unsettling than his own unfaithfulness both to others and to himself, an unfaithfulness that will, in the end, lead to his downfall.22

承认书籍是流动的物体而非固定的文本确实会造成不稳定，因为它反映了我们自己的不确定性——也就是说，我们的愚蠢。然而，通过比吕西安更直率地面对这一对抗，我们或许能够同时接触作品的丰富性并减少讨论时的尴尬。

The acknowledgment that books are mobile objects rather than fixed texts is indeed destabilizing, since it reflects back our own uncertainty—which is to say, our folly. In facing that confrontation more forthrightly than Lucien, however, we may be able to simultaneously approach works in their richness and reduce the awkwardness of our discussions about them.

事实上，承认文本的流动性和我们自身的流动性是一大优势，它赋予我们极大的自由，让我们可以将自己对书籍的判断强加于他人。巴尔扎克笔下的英雄们展示了虚拟图书馆的非凡可塑性，以及它可以轻松适应任何人（无论是否读过书）的要求，只要他决心坚持所谓的读者的评论，以坚持自己的看法的真相。



Indeed, to acknowledge both the mobility of a text and our own mobility is a major advantage, one that confers great freedom to impose our judgments of books on others. Balzac’s heroes demonstrate the remarkable plasticity of the virtual library and the ease with which it can be bent to the requirements of anyone who—having read a book or not—is determined to persevere through the remarks of so-called readers to assert the truth of his perceptions.

十一、

发明书籍

XI

Inventing Books

（在阅读 S seki 时，我们听从了一只猫和一位戴金边眼镜的艺术家的建议，他们各自在不同的领域中宣扬发明的必要性）

(in which, reading Sseki, we follow the advice of a cat and an artist in gold-rimmed spectacles, who each, in different fields of activity, proclaim the necessity of invention)

如果一本书不仅仅是一本书，更是关于这本书的整个讨论，那么我们必须关注这一讨论，才能在不阅读这本书的情况下谈论这本书。因为问题不在于这本书本身，而在于它在它介入并不断转变的批判空间中变成了什么。正是这个移动的物体，一个文本与存在之间柔韧的关系结构，人们必须能够在正确的时刻对它做出准确的陈述。

IF A BOOK is less a book than it is the whole of the discussion about it, we must pay attention to that discussion in order to talk about the book without reading it. For it is not the book itself that is at stake, but what it has become within the critical space in which it intervenes and is continually transformed. It is this moving object, a supple fabric of relations between texts and beings, about which one must be in a position to formulate accurate statements at the right moment.

书籍的不断修改不仅影响其价值（我们在巴尔扎克的例子中已经看到，随着作者在文学政治中的地位变化，价值也会迅速变化），还影响其内容，内容不再稳定，会随着人们对其的评价而发生明显的变化。文本的这种流动性不应被理解为一种缺点。相反，对于准备利用它的人来说，它提供了一个绝佳的机会，可以成为他未读过的书的创作者。

The constant modification of books affects not only their value (we have seen in the example from Balzac how quickly this may shift along with the place of the author in literary politics), but also their content, which is no more stable, and which undergoes palpable variation as a result of the things said about it. This mobility of the text should not be understood as a drawback. To the contrary, for someone prepared to turn it to his advantage, it offers a remarkable opportunity to become the creator of the books he hasn’t read.

日本作家夏目漱石在其最著名的作品《我是一只猫》1中，将自己的故事讲述给了一只猫，这只猫用以下的话作为自传的开头：



In the novel I Am a Cat,1 perhaps his best-known work, the Japanese writer Natsume Sseki entrusts the narration of his tale to a cat, who begins his autobiography with these words:



我是一只猫，但我还没有名字。

I am a cat but as yet I have no name.

我完全不知道自己出生在哪儿。我记得的第一件事是，我在一个阴暗潮湿的地方哭着“喵喵喵”。在那里，我生平第一次遇见了一个人。虽然我是后来才知道这一切的，但我得知这个人叫学生，是人类中最凶猛的一个。2



I haven’t the faintest idea of where I was born. The first thing I do remember is that I was crying “meow, meow,” somewhere in a gloomy damp place. It was there that I met a human being for the first time in my life. Though I found this all out at a later date, I learned that this human being was called a Student, one of the most ferocious of the human race.2



小说的猫叙述者将在整个作品中保持匿名，在与人类的首次接触中运气不佳。他遇到了一个虐待他的学生，醒来后神志恍惚，远离家乡。然后他溜进一所不知名的房子，幸运的是，他受到了主人——一位教授的欢迎。《我是一只猫》致力于讲述他在这所房子里的生活，他在那里居住。

The novel’s feline narrator, who will remain anonymous throughout the work, has little luck in this first encounter with the human species. He encounters a student who mistreats him, and he wakes up delirious and far from home. He then slips inside an unknown house, where he is fortunate enough to be welcomed by the owner, a professor. I Am a Cat is devoted to recounting his life in that house, where he takes up residence.

虽然本书以猫的叙述者——猫科动物的视角为主，但读者可以相对复杂地了解猫的世界。事实上，叙述者并不是一只未经驯化的动物，而是一只拥有许多技能的猫，比如能够听懂对话，甚至会阅读。

Although the point of view of our cat narrator—the feline point of view—is dominant in the book, the reader is granted a relatively complex perspective of his world. The narrator, in fact, is not an uncultivated animal, but a cat endowed with a number of skills, such as the ability to follow a conversation and even to read.

但猫咪没有忘记自己的出身，它依然与猫科动物世界保持着联系。因此，它与新邻居的两只猫——母猫麦克和公猫库洛——建立了长期的关系。库洛是这个地区的统治者，用身体力量迫使其他人尊重它。但它在小说中也占据着一个特殊的位置，作为一系列人物的动物象征，这些人物的共同特点是自吹自擂。库洛的吹嘘集中在对猫来说很重要的各个领域，比如抓到的老鼠数量，在这个领域，它毫不犹豫地夸大了自己的能力。

But the cat does not forget his origins; he remains connected to the feline world. He thus enters into protracted relations with two cats from his new neighborhood, the female cat Mike and the male cat Kuro. Kuro is the reigning master of the area, forcing others to respect him through physical strength. But he also occupies a special position in the novel as the animal emblem of a whole series of characters whose common characteristic is boastfulness. Kuro’s bragging centers on various domains important to cats, such as the number of mice caught, an area in which he shows no qualms about exaggerating his prowess.

Kuro 在经常光顾教授家的人类中有一个对应者。叙述者猫称这个人 M. 为“戴金边眼镜的艺术家”，他有一个奇怪的习惯，就是讲述他脑海中浮现的任何故事，纯粹是为了将听众引入歧途而获得乐趣。

Kuro has a counterpart among the humans who frequent the professor’s house. The narrator cat refers to that individual, M., as “the artist in gold-rimmed spectacles,” and he has the peculiar habit of recounting whatever stories come into his head, for the sheer pleasure of leading his listener astray.

在书的开头，M. 看到教授对绘画很感兴趣，并想自己画一些，就向他介绍了意大利画家安德烈亚·德尔·萨托，并告诉他德尔·萨托会建议尽可能模仿自然进行绘画，并首先学习如何素描。教授相信了这个建议，但未能成为一名画家。艺术家随后向他透露，他实际上编造了安德烈亚·德尔·萨托的所有所谓言论，并且他经常以编造故事和利用人们的轻信为乐：



At the beginning of the book, seeing that the professor is interested in painting and would like to do some himself, M. tells him about the Italian painter Andrea del Sarto and shares with him the theory that del Sarto would have recommended painting as much as possible in imitation of nature and learning first of all how to sketch. The professor puts his trust in this advice, but fails to become a painter. The artist then reveals to him that he has in fact invented all the alleged remarks of Andrea del Sarto and that he often takes pleasure in making up stories and playing on people’s credulity:



艺术家玩得不亦乐乎。我在阳台上听着这些，不禁想知道老师会在日记里怎么记下这段对话。艺术家是个喜欢捉弄别人的人。他好像没有意识到自己对安德烈亚·德尔·萨托的玩笑伤害了我的老师，还夸耀道：“有些人开玩笑的时候，会把玩笑当真，以至于会显示出极大的喜剧美，这很有趣。前几天我告诉一个学生，尼古拉斯·尼克尔贝曾建议吉本把他的伟大著作《法国大革命史》从一本法语教科书中翻译出来，并以自己的名义出版。这个学生记忆力极好，在日本文学圈做了一次演讲，引用了我告诉他的一切。听众大约有一百人，他们都听得很认真。”



The artist was greatly enjoying himself. Listening to all this from the veranda, I couldn’t help wondering what my master would write in his diary about that conversation. The artist was a person who took great pleasure in fooling others. As if he did not realize how his joke about Andrea del Sarto hurt my master, he boasted more: “When playing jokes, some people take them so seriously that they reveal great comic beauty, and it’s a lot of fun. The other day I told a student that Nicholas Nickleby had advised Gibbon to translate his great History of the French Revolution3 from a French textbook and to have it published under his own name. This student has an extremely good memory and made a speech at the Japanese Literary Circle quoting everything I had told him. There were about a hundred people in the audience and they all listened very attentively.”4



尼克尔贝的故事在两个层面上是荒诞的。首先，虚构人物尼古拉斯·尼克尔贝很难向爱德华·吉本——一位完全真实的英国历史学家——提供建议。其次，即使这两个人确实属于同一个宇宙，他们仍然无法进行对话，因为尼克尔贝于 1838 年首次出现在文学界，而那时吉本已经去世近五十年了。

The Nickleby story is absurd on two levels. For one thing, it would be more than a little difficult for the fictional character Nicholas Nickleby to give advice to Edward Gibbon, an entirely real British historian. Second, even if the two men did belong to the same universe, they would still not have been able to enter into dialogue, since Nickleby appeared for the first time in the world of letters in 1838, by which date Gibbon had already been dead for nearly fifty years.

如果在这第一个例子里，艺术家毫无顾忌地编造故事，那么在他给出的下一个例子中，情况会稍有不同，这直接关系到我们对未读书籍的考虑：



If, in this first example, the artist makes up stories without compunction, the situation is slightly different in the next one he gives, which directly concerns our consideration of unread books:



“还有一次。一天晚上，在一次作家聚会上，话题转到了哈里森的历史小说《西奥法诺》。5 我说这是有史以来最好的历史小说之一，尤其是女主角死亡的部分。‘这真的让你毛骨悚然’——我就是这么说的。坐在我对面的一位作家是那种不能也不会拒绝任何事情的人。他立即表示这是最著名的一段。我马上就知道他读过的故事比我多。” 6



“Then there’s another time. One evening, at a gathering of writers, the conversation turned to Harrison’s historical novel Theophano.5 I said that it was one of the best historical novels ever written, especially the part where the heroine dies. ‘That really gives you the creeps’— that’s what I said. An author who was sitting opposite me was one of those types who cannot and will not say no to anything. He immediately voiced the opinion that that was a most famous passage. I knew right away that he had never read any more of the story than I had.”6



这种愤世嫉俗的态度引发了几个问题，其中一个是教授立即问艺术家的：



This kind of cynicism raises several questions, one of which the professor asks the artist immediately:



老师睁大眼睛，紧张又难受地问道：“如果对方真的读了这个故事，你会怎么做？”

With wide eyes, my nervous and weak-stomached master asked, “What would you have done if the other man had really read the story?”

艺术家没有表现出任何兴奋。他不认为愚弄他人有什么意义。唯一重要的是不要被当场抓住。

The artist did not show any excitement. He thought nothing of fooling other people. The only thing that counted was not to be caught in the act.

“我只需要说我在标题上犯了一个错误或类似的东西。”他继续笑着。7



“All I would have to do is to say that I had made a mistake in the title or something to that effect.” He kept on laughing.7



如果你开始轻率地谈论一本书，而你的评论受到质疑，没有什么可以阻止你回头并宣布你犯了一个错误。我们的不读书或遗忘起着如此重要的作用，以至于宣布自己是因读书（或不读书）而导致的众多记忆失误之一的受害者，几乎没有风险。即使是一本我们能非常准确地回忆起的书，在某种意义上也是一本屏幕书，我们自己的内心书隐藏在屏幕书后面。但在这种特殊情况下，承认错误真的是艺术家最好的解决方案吗？

If you have begun talking about a book imprudently and your remarks are challenged, nothing prevents you from backtracking and declaring that you’ve made a mistake. Our unreading or forgetting plays such a significant role that there is little risk in declaring yourself the victim of one of the many lapses in memory induced by our reading— and non-reading—of books. Even a book that we recall with great precision is in some sense a screen book, behind which our own inner book is concealed. But in this particular case, is it really the best solution for the artist to admit his error?

事实上，S seki 的文本提出了一个有趣的逻辑问题。这位戴金边眼镜的艺术家虚构了一个关于女主角死亡的场景，因此，当哈里森的书中没有质疑这样的场景的存在，而是赞许地说这确实很精彩时，他被认为也撒了谎。但如果艺术家自己从未读过这本小说，他怎么能确定他面对的是一个不读书的人呢？

In fact, Sseki’s text raises an interesting problem of logic. The artist with gold-rimmed spectacles invents a scene about the death of the heroine, so when, instead of challenging the existence of such a scene in Harrison’s book, the other man says approvingly that it is splendid indeed, he is presumed to be revealed as a liar as well. But how can the artist know for sure that he is dealing with a non-reader if he himself has never read the novel?

在 S seki 所描述的情形中，两个不读同一本书的人就这本书展开对话，实际上这两个不读书的人都不可能知道对方是否在撒谎。如果对话双方中至少有一个人不了解这本书，或者至少对这本书有一个模糊的概念，那么就不可能确信有人在谈论一本书时撒谎。

In the situation described by Sseki, where two non-readers of the same book carry on a dialogue about it, it is actually impossible for either of the non-readers to know whether the other is lying. There can be no conviction that anyone is lying in a conversation about a book without at least one of the participants knowing the book or having at least a vague idea of it.

但是，当两个谈话者中的一人或两人都“读过”这本书时，情况会有所不同吗？S seki 的轶事，就像 Lodge 中的真相游戏一样，提醒我们虚拟图书馆的两个不确定性中的第一个，即读者的能力。很难，甚至不可能知道与你谈论一本书的人在多大程度上撒谎说自己读过这本书。这不仅是因为几乎没有其他领域有如此明显的虚伪，而且最重要的是，因为每个说话者都不可能知道对方与这本书的历史，因此，如果他们认为自己可以回答这个问题，那就是自欺欺人。

But is the situation different when one of the two conversationalists, or both, have “read” the book? Sseki’s anecdote, like the game of truth in Lodge, has the merit of reminding us of the first of the two uncertainties of the virtual library, which concerns the competence of readers. It is difficult, if not impossible, to know the extent to which the person with whom you are speaking about a book is lying about having read it. Not only because there is hardly another domain in which such pronounced hypocrisy holds sway, but above all because each speaker cannot possibly know the other person’s history with the book and they are thus deluding themselves if they think they can answer the question.

这样的对话相当于一场欺骗游戏，参与者在欺骗他人之前先欺骗自己，他们对书籍的记忆将根据当前情况的利害关系而改变。毕竟，试图将读过某本书的人和对这本书一无所知的人分成两个阵营是对阅读行为的误解，洛奇教授愚蠢地试图这样做。所谓的读者和所谓的非读者都误解了阅读行为，前者忽视了每次阅读都会带来的抹去和损失，而后者忽视了每次与书本相遇时可能产生的创作冲动。

Such a conversation amounts to a game of dupes, in which the participants fool themselves even before fooling others, and in which their memories of books will be marked by the stakes of the situation at hand. It would, after all, be a misunderstanding of the act of reading to try to separate those who have read a certain book and those who are ignorant of it into two camps, as Lodge’s professor foolishly tried to do. It is a misunderstanding both by so-called readers, who disregard the erasure and loss that accompanies every act of reading, and so-called non-readers, who ignore the creative impulse that can arise from every encounter with a book.

因此，摆脱“他人知道我们是否在撒谎”的想法（他人就是我们自己），是能够优雅地谈论书籍的主要条件之一，无论我们是否读过这些书。事实上，我们在评论书籍时所涉及的知识本质上是不确定的。与此同时，“他人”是我们投射到听众身上的一种不赞同的自我形象，这种形象是我们基于一种如此详尽的文化而内化的，这种文化的重要性在学校里被如此坚定地灌输给我们，以至于它阻碍了我们的生活和思考。

To liberate ourselves from the idea that the Other knows whether we’re lying—the Other being just as much ourselves—is thus one of the primary conditions for being able to talk about books with grace, whether we’ve read them or not. In truth, of course, the knowledge at stake in our comments on books is intrinsically uncertain. And the Other, meanwhile, is a disapproving image of ourselves that we project onto our listeners, an image we have internalized based on a culture so exhaustive, and whose importance is so firmly drummed into us in school, that it impedes us from living and thinking.

但是，面对他人的知识，我们感到焦虑，这是对书籍所有真正创造力的阻碍。认为他人读过一切，因此比我们更了解情况，这种想法将创造力降低为非读者在紧急情况下可能求助的权宜之计。事实上，读者和非读者都陷入了无休止的发明书籍的过程中，无论他们喜欢与否，真正的问题不是如何逃离这个过程，而是如何增加它的活力和范围。

But our anxiety in the face of the Other’s knowledge is an obstacle to all genuine creativity about books. The idea that the Other has read everything, and thus is better informed than us, reduces creativity to a mere stopgap that non-readers might resort to in a pinch. In truth, readers and non-readers alike are caught up in an endless process of inventing books, whether they like it or not, and the real question is not how to escape that process, but how to increase its dynamism and its range.

这种对我们交谈对象能力的最初不确定性，加上另一种不确定性，这种不确定性在巴尔扎克的作品中已经有所体现，但在这里被强调得与书本身息息相关。如果很难确定对方知道什么，我们自己知道什么，这在一定程度上是因为要知道文本中的内容并不容易。这种怀疑不仅与它的价值有关，就像在巴尔扎克的作品中一样，还延伸到它所谓的内容。

This initial uncertainty about the competence of the people we’re speaking to is compounded by another kind of uncertainty, already observed in Balzac, but here emphasized such that it bears on the book itself. If it is difficult to ascertain what the other person knows and what we know ourselves, this is true in part because it is not that easy to know what is in a text. This doubt not only concerns its value, as in Balzac, but extends to its so-called content as well.

弗雷德里克·哈里森的小说《狄奥法诺》8就是这种情况 ，根据这位戴金边眼镜的艺术家的说法，从理论上讲，人们可能会误解或误导他人。这部小说出版于 1904 年，属于可以称为拜占庭小说的文学体裁。它始于公元 956 年，一直延续到 969 年，讲述了君士坦丁堡皇帝尼基弗鲁斯·福卡斯领导的对伊斯兰教的胜利反攻。

Such is the case for Frederic Harrison’s novel Theophano,8 about which, according to the artist with gold-rimmed spectacles, one might theoretically be wrong or mislead someone else. Published in 1904, it belongs to the literary genre that might be called the Byzantine novel. It begins in AD 956 and continues to 969, and it tells of the victorious counteroffensive against Islam led by the emperor of Constantinople, Nicephorus Phocas.

随之而来的问题就是，艺术家是否通过评论女主角的戏剧性死亡来编造故事（此外，这也是怀疑 S seki 是否在谈论一本他没有读过的书的另一种方式）。我们能说女主角死了吗？如果答案是肯定的，那么她的死亡是否足以让人不寒而栗？

The question then arises of whether the artist is making up stories by commenting on the dramatic death of the heroine (which is, moreover, another way of wondering whether Sseki is talking about a book he hasn’t read). Can one say that the heroine dies, and if the answer is yes, might her death be sufficiently moving to send chills down one’s spine?

这个问题并不那么容易回答。人们往往认为是女主角的历史人物——狄奥法诺，皇帝尼基弗鲁斯的妻子，她帮助暗杀了皇帝——并没有死，但在小说的最后一页，她被监禁和流放了。9因此，我们面对的是一种死亡，或者至少是一种失踪。读过这本书的读者可能会真诚地忘记她被消灭的具体情况，只记得她遭遇了不幸，而不能说他没有读过这本书。

This question is not so simple to answer. The historical character one would tend to regard as the heroine— Theophano, the wife of Emperor Nicephorus, whom she helps to assassinate—does not die, but on the last page of the novel, she is imprisoned and exiled.9 We are thus dealing with a kind of death, or at least a disappearance. A reader who had read the book might in good faith forget the precise circumstances of her elimination and simply remember that a misfortune befalls her, without it being possible to say that he hadn’t read the book.

问题进一步复杂化，因为小说中不止一位女主角，而是两位。第二位是阿加莎公主，一位谨慎而令人钦佩的女主角，在得知她心爱的人、皇帝的同伴巴西尔·迪吉内斯在战斗中死亡后，她退居修道院。关于这一事件的段落避免了过多的抒情，而且这样做更加成功。因此，女性角色的失踪是一个相当感人的例子，而一位所谓的读者对她已经死亡的回忆似乎很难成为评估他是否真的读过这本书的理由。

The problem is further complicated by the observation that there is not one heroine, but two, in the novel. The second is Princess Agatha, a discreet and admirable heroine who withdraws to a convent upon learning of the death in combat of her beloved, the emperor’s companion Basil Digenes. The passage about this incident refrains from lyrical excess and is all the more successful for doing so. Thus there is a quite moving case of the disappearance of a female character, and an alleged reader’s recollection that she had died would hardly seem like grounds for an evaluation of whether he had really read the book.

在与女主角是否死亡这一事实问题完全不同的层面上，艺术家完全有理由赞扬描述此类事件的段落的质量，因为在某种意义上，他觉得这很正确，至少作为一种未实现的可能性。这个时期的冒险小说很少不包含女性角色，而且很难想象如果没有爱情故事，读者的兴趣怎么会持续很长时间。在这种情况下，除非讲述一个结局圆满的故事，否则怎么会不让女主角死去呢？文学作品很少倾向于这样做。10

At an entirely different level than the factual question of whether the heroine dies, the artist is perfectly justified in praising the quality of the passage describing such an event, since in a certain sense it feels right to him, at least as an unrealized possibility. Few adventure novels of this period do not include a female character, and it is hard to see how the reader’s interest might be sustained for any great length of time without including a love story. And how, in that case, would one not have the heroine die, unless one were telling a story with a happy ending, which literature is rarely inclined to do?10

因此，很难知道这位艺术家是否读过《狄奥法诺》。首先，说这本书描写了女主角的死亡并不为过，即使“消失”这个词可能更合适。此外，在这一点上犯错并不能证明他没有读过这本书。女主角死亡的文化幻想如此强烈，以至于他读完后会把它与书联系起来，甚至成为书中不可分割的一部分，这并不奇怪。

It is thus doubly difficult to know whether the artist has read Theophano. In the first place, it is not that far off to say that the book features the death of a heroine, even if the word disappearance might be more appropriate. Moreover, being wrong on this point in no way proves that he hasn’t read it. This cultural fantasy of the heroine’s death is so potent that it is unsurprising that he would associate it with the book once his reading is complete, even to the point where it becomes an integral part of the book for him.

换句话说，我们谈论的书籍不仅仅是在完整客观地阅读人类图书馆时发现的实际书籍，而且还有幻影书籍，这些书籍在每本书未实现的可能性与我们的潜意识相遇时浮现出来。这些幻影书籍为我们的白日梦和对话提供了动力，远比理论上是其来源的真实物体更能激发我们的白日梦和对话。11

The books we talk about, in other words, are not just the actual books that would be uncovered in a complete and objective reading of the human library, but also phantom books that surface where the unrealized possibilities of each book meet our unconscious. These phantom books fuel our daydreams and conversations, far more than the real objects that are theoretically their source.11

我们看到，对一本书的讨论直接将我们引向这样一个境地：与戴金边眼镜的艺术家所认为的相反，真与假的概念失去了其大部分有效性。首先，我们很难知道我们自己是否读过一本书，因为我们的阅读转瞬即逝。其次，我们几乎不可能知道其他人是否读过这本书，因为这首先意味着他们知道这样的事情。最后，文本的内容是如此不稳定，以至于很难肯定地断言其中没有发现某些东西。

One sees how directly the discussion of a book leads us to a point where the notions of true and false, contrary to what the artist with gold-rimmed spectacles believes, lose much of their validity. It is first difficult to know whether we ourselves have read a book, so evanescent is our reading. Second, it is more or less impossible to know whether others have read it, since this would first entail their knowing such a thing. Finally, the content of a text is so fluid that it is difficult to assert with certainty that something is not found in it.

因此，虚拟的图书讨论空间具有极大的不确定性，参与者无法严格地陈述他们读过的内容，讨论的目标也不断变化，这同样如此。但这种不确定性并非完全是不利的；如果对话者抓住时机，它也可以提供一个机会，将虚拟图书馆变成一个真实的小说世界。

The virtual space of discussion about books is thus characterized by extraordinary uncertainty, which applies to the participants, incapable of stating rigorously what they have read, as much as to the moving target of their discussion. But this uncertainty is not entirely disadvantageous; it can also provide the opportunity, if those in the conversation seize the moment, to transform the virtual library into an authentic realm of fiction.

小说，在这里，不应被贬义地理解。我的意思是，如果虚拟图书馆的规则得到使用者的尊重，它就能够促进一种原创的创造力。这种创造力可以源自一本书在那些没有读过这本书的人心中引起的共鸣。它可以是个人的，也可以是集体的。它的目的是构建一本更适合非读者所处境遇的书——这本书可能与原著只有微弱的联系（究竟是什么？），但它尽可能接近各种内部书籍的假设交汇点。

Fiction, here, should not be understood pejoratively. What I mean to say is that if its rules are respected by the occupants, the virtual library is in a position to advance an original kind of creativity. Such creativity can arise from the resonances that a book calls up in those who haven’t read it. It can be individual or collective. Its aim is to construct a book more propitious to the situation in which the non-readers find themselves—a book that may have only feeble links to the original (which would be what, exactly?), but one that is as close as possible to the hypothetical meeting point of various inner books.

在他的另一本书《路边的草》中，12 S seki 描绘了一位画家隐居在山中，总结他的艺术。一天，女房东的女儿走进他的房间，看到他拿着一本书，问他在读什么。画家回答说他不知道，因为他的做法是随意打开书，阅读眼前的一页，而对书的其余部分一无所知。面对年轻女子的惊讶，画家向她解释说，对他来说，以这种方式进行更有趣：“我随意打开这本书，就像一场机会游戏，我读到最后出现在我面前的那一页，这才是有趣的。” 13

In another of his books, Grass on the Wayside,12 Sseki depicts a painter who has retreated to the mountains to produce a summation of his art. One day his landlady’s daughter comes into his room and, seeing him with a book, asks him what he is reading. The painter answers that he doesn’t know, since his practice is to open the book at random and read the page before his eyes without knowing anything of the rest of the book. Reacting to the young woman’s surprise, the painter explains to her that it is more interesting for him to proceed in this manner: “I open the book at random as though it were a game of chance, and I read the page that ends up in front of me, and that’s what is interesting.”13

女人建议他向她展示他的方法，他同意了，最后将手中的英文书中的一段话翻译成了日语。书中的主人公是一男一女，除了知道他们在威尼斯的一艘船上之外，其他人一无所知。当年轻女子问起这些人物是谁时，画家回答说他一点也不知道，因为他没有读过这本书，并坚持不再追问：



The woman suggests that he show her his method, which he agrees to do, eventually translating a passage from the English book in his hand into Japanese for her. The subject is a man and a woman of whom nothing is known other than that they are in a boat in Venice. When the young woman asks who these characters are, the painter replies that he hasn’t the slightest idea, since he hasn’t read the book and insists on not finding out any more:



“那个男人和那个女人是谁？”

“Who are that man and that woman?”

“我不知道。但这正是它有趣的地方。在那之前我们没必要关心他们的关系。就像你和我在一起时一样，只有当下才是最重要的。” 14



“I have no idea. But that’s precisely why it’s interesting. We have no need to be concerned with their relations until then. Just like you and I finding ourselves together, it’s only the present moment that counts.”14



书中重要的东西是外在的，因为它只是讨论的借口或载体：谈论一本书与其说是关于书本身，不如说是关于为它而进行的对话。真正的关系不是小说中的两个人物之间，而是一对“读者”之间。但如果后者不受书的限制，如果允许书保留其模糊性，他们将能够更好地交流。这就是我们内心的书有机会像《土拨鼠日》中那样，在哪怕短暂的一刻结合在一起所付出的代价。

What is important in the book is external to it, since it is only a pretext or vehicle for this moment of discussion: talking about a book is less about the book itself than about the moment of conversation devoted to it. The real relationship is not between the novel’s two characters, but between its pair of “readers.” But the latter couple will be better able to communicate if they are less constrained by the book and if it is allowed to retain its ambiguity. Such is the price paid for our inner books to have some chance, as in the distended temporality of Groundhog Day, of joining together for even one brief moment.

因此，明智的做法是避免对遇到的书籍做出过于精确的评论，从而贬低它们的价值，而是欢迎它们的所有多面性。这样，我们就不会错过它们的任何潜力，并开放书中的内容——标题、片段、真或假的引文，或者在这种情况下，威尼斯船上的情侣的照片——以在那一刻建立人与人之间联系的所有可能性。

We would thus be wise to avoid diminishing the books that surface in our encounters by making overly precise comments about them, but rather to welcome them in all their polyvalence. In this way, we allow none of their potential to be lost, and we open up what comes from the book—title, fragment, genuine or fake quotation, or in this case the image of the couple on a boat in Venice—to all the possibilities of connection that can be created, at that moment, between people.

这种模糊性与精神分析中解释的模糊性有某种相似之处。因为解释可以用不同的方式来理解，所以它有机会被它所针对的对象理解，而如果它太清楚，它可能会被视为一种对他人的暴力。和分析解释一样，关于一本书的陈述严格依赖于它被陈述的确切时刻，并且只有在那一刻才有意义。

This ambiguity has a certain kinship with the ambiguity of interpretation in psychoanalysis. It is because interpretation can be understood in different ways that it stands a chance of being understood by the subject to whom it is addressed, whereas if it were too clear, it might be experienced as a kind of violence against the other. And like analytic interpretation, a statement about a book is narrowly dependent on the exact moment when it is made and has meaning only in that moment.

关于一本未读的书的真正有效的陈述还需要有意识的、理性的思考，这种悬置再次让人联想到心理分析。如果我们没有过多地思考，我们能够说出的关于我们与一本书的亲密关系的话会更有说服力。相反，我们只需要让我们的潜意识在我们内心表达自己，并在语言开放的这一特殊时刻，说出将我们与书联系在一起的秘密纽带，从而将我们与我们自己联系在一起。

A truly effective statement about an unread book also involves a bracketing of conscious, rational thought, a suspension that is once again reminiscent of psychoanalysis. What we are able to say about our intimate relation with a book will have more force if we have not thought about it excessively. Instead, we need only let our unconscious express itself within us and give voice, in this privileged moment of openness in language, to the secret ties that bind us to the book, and thereby to ourselves.

让书籍保持模糊性并不与坚持己见和将自己的观点强加于书籍的必要性相矛盾，正如我们在巴尔扎克的小说中看到的那样。这甚至可能是它的另一面。这是一种表明你已经掌握了对话空间的具体性质和每个参与者的独特性的方式。即使每个人都在讨论一本屏幕书，最好也不要破坏共同的空间，而是让我们的幻影书保持完整，以及我们不读书和做梦的潜力。

Letting books keep their ambiguity does not contradict the necessity to be assertive and impose your point of view on a book, as we saw in Balzac’s novel. It might even be its flip side. It is a way of showing that you have grasped the specific nature of the conversational space and the singularity of each participant. Even if it is a screen book that each person is discussing, it is better not to shatter the common space, but instead to leave our phantom books intact, along with our potential to non-read and to dream.

鉴于这些情况，人们可能会得出这样的结论：当我在本书前面决定拯救《玫瑰之名》中的图书馆免遭大火、让罗洛·马丁斯和哈里·莱姆的女友团聚，或者逼迫戴维·洛奇笔下不幸的英雄自杀时，我并没有虚构任何东西。当然，这些事实并没有直接写在文本中。但就像我在讨论的作品中向读者提供的所有事实一样，在我看来，它们与我认为的每个文本的可能逻辑相对应，因此，就我而言，它们是文本不可分割的一部分。

Given these circumstances, one might well conclude that ultimately I invented nothing when I decided earlier in this book to save the library in The Name of the Rose from the flames, to unite Rollo Martins and Harry Lime’s girlfriend, or to drive David Lodge’s unhappy hero to suicide. To be sure, these facts are not directly stated in the texts. But like all the facts I have offered the reader in the works I have discussed, they correspond for me to what I see as the likely logic of each text and thus, as far as I’m concerned, are an integral part of them.

毫无疑问，我会像那位戴金边眼镜的艺术家一样，因为谈论我没读过的书，或者讲述那些实际上不属于书中的事件而受到指责。然而，我感觉我并不是在撒谎，而是在尽可能准确地描述我对这些书的看法，忠实于当时和当时我觉得需要援引这些书的自己，说出了主观事实。



No doubt I will be reproached, as was the artist with gold-rimmed spectacles, for talking about books I haven’t read, or for recounting events that, literally speaking, are not part of the books. However, it felt to me not as if I were lying, but rather that I was uttering a subjective truth by describing with the greatest possible accuracy what I had perceived of these books, being faithful to myself at the moment and in the circumstances when I felt the need to invoke them.
