10.在世界文学中，有无数的书籍将“女主角之死”视为最美丽的段落之一。

10. There is no end to the number of books in world literature in which the “death of the heroine” is one of the most beautiful passages.

11.我在这里介绍的第三种书是幻影书，即我们在谈论一本书时，以书面或口头形式所称的可移动且不可抓取的物体。它位于读者的各种屏幕书的交汇处——读者根据他们的内心书构建的屏幕书。幻影书属于我们交流的虚拟图书馆，正如屏幕书属于集体图书馆，内心书属于内心图书馆一样。

11. The third type of book I am introducing here, the phantom book, is that mobile and ungraspable object that we call into being, in writing or in speech, when we talk about a book. It is located at the point where readers’ various screen books meet—screen books that readers have constructed based on their inner books. The phantom book belongs to the virtual library of our exchanges, as the screen book belongs to the collective library and the inner book belongs to the inner library.

12. SB++。

12. SB++.

13.《路边的草》（Michikusa），Edwin McClellan译（J.Mehlman修订）（芝加哥：芝加哥大学出版社，1969年）。

13. Grass on the Wayside (Michikusa), translated by Edwin McClellan (revised by J. Mehlman) (Chicago:University of Chicago Press, 1969).

14.同上，第102页。

14. Ibid., p. 102.

XII

谈论你自己

XII

Speaking About Yourself

（我们与奥斯卡·王尔德一致认为，阅读一本书的适当时间是十分钟，十分钟之后，您就会忘记，阅读这本书主要是为您撰写自传找借口）

(in which we conclude, along with Oscar Wilde, that the appropriate time span for reading a book is ten minutes, after which you risk forgetting that the encounter is primarily a pretext for writing your autobiography)

我们认为，谈论未读书籍的义务不应被视为消极的事情，不应成为焦虑或悔恨的根源。对于知道如何将其视为积极事物、设法减轻内疚负担并关注自己所处具体情况的潜力的人来说，谈论未读书籍会让我们进入一个真正的创造力领域。我们应该学会欢迎进入这个虚拟图书馆的机会，并拥抱它所有丰富的可能性。

AS WE SEE, the obligation to talk about unread books should not be experienced as something negative, a source of anxiety or remorse. To the person who knows how to experience it as positive, who manages to lift the burden of his guilt and pay attention to the potential of the concrete situation in which he finds himself, talking about unread books invites us into a realm of authentic creativity. We should learn to welcome the opportunity to enter this virtual library and embrace all its rich possibility.

无论如何，这都是奥斯卡·王尔德关于这个主题的著作中值得借鉴的重要教训。这些文本特别关注一种我们可能被引导谈论我们没有读过的书的情况——文学批评——但他的建议很容易扩展到其他情况，例如社交或学术环境中的对话。

That, in any event, is the major lesson to be drawn from Oscar Wilde’s writings on the subject. These texts concentrate especially on one type of situation in which we may be led to talk about books we haven’t read—that of literary criticism—but his suggestions may easily be extended to other situations, such as dialogues in social or academic settings.

奥斯卡·王尔德是一位如饥似渴的读者，而且是一位博学多识的人，但他也是一位坚决不读书的人。早在穆齐尔或瓦莱里之前，王尔德就勇于警告有文化的人读书的危险。

A voracious reader if ever there was one and a man of vast culture, Oscar Wilde was also a resolute non-reader. Long before Musil or Valéry, Wilde had the courage to warn of the dangers of reading for the cultivated individual.

王尔德对非读书研究最重要的贡献之一，是因为它开辟了新的渠道，发表在一篇名为《读书，还是不读书》的文章中。这篇文章发表在《Pall Mall Gazette》上，这是王尔德经常为该报撰稿的一份报纸。在回答关于可以推荐的 100 本最佳书籍的问题时，王尔德建议将集体图书馆的内容分为三类。

One of Wilde’s most important contributions to the study of non-reading, because of the new channels it opens up, appeared in an article called “To read, or not to read”1. in the Pall Mall Gazette, a newspaper for which he wrote regularly. Responding to an inquiry about the hundred best books it was possible to recommend, Wilde proposed dividing the contents of the collective library into three categories.

第一类是值得阅读的书籍，王尔德将西塞罗的书信、苏埃托尼乌斯、瓦萨里的画家传记、2本韦努托·切利尼的自传、3约翰·曼德维尔、马可·波罗、圣西门的回忆录、4蒙森和格罗特的希腊史归入这一类别。5第二类同样值得一读，包括柏拉图和济慈等值得一读的书籍。在“诗歌领域”，王尔德添加了“大师，而不是吟游诗人”；在哲学领域，添加了“预言家，而不是学者”。6王尔德，上文，第 12 页。

The first would consist of books to be read, a category in which Wilde places Cicero’s letters, Suetonius, Vasari’s lives of the painters,2 Benvenuto Cellini’s autobiography,3 John Mandeville, Marco Polo, Saint-Simon’s memoirs,4 Mommsen, and Grote’s history of Greece.5 The second category, equally expected, would comprise books worth rereading, such as Plato and Keats. In the “sphere of poetry,” Wilde adds “the masters, not the minstrels”; in that of philosophy, “the seers, not the savants.”6. Wilde, op. cit., p. 12.

除了这些相当平庸的类别之外，王尔德还增加了第三个更令人惊讶的类别。它包括那些需要劝阻公众阅读的书籍。对王尔德来说，这种劝阻活动至关重要，甚至应该成为大学的官方使命之一。他指出：“在我们这个时代，这个时代阅读太多，以至于没有时间欣赏，写作太多，以至于没有时间思考，这个时代非常需要这种使命。无论谁能从我们现代课程的混乱中选出‘最糟糕的一百本书’并公布一份名单，都将给新一代带来真正而持久的益处。” 7

To these rather banal categories, Wilde adds a third that is more surprising. It consists of books it is important to dissuade the public from reading. For Wilde, such dissuasive activity is crucial and should even figure among the official missions of universities. “This mission,” he notes, “is eminently needed in this age of ours, an age that reads so much that it has no time to admire, and writes so much that it has no time to think. Whoever will select out of the chaos of our modern curricula ‘The Worst Hundred Books’ and publish a list of them, will confer on the rising generation a real and lasting benefit.”7

不幸的是，王尔德没有给我们留下一份必须让学生远离的 100 本书的清单。然而，这份清单显然不如阅读并不总是有益的活动，反而可能有害这一观点重要。阅读的危害如此之大，以至于在其他文本中，要禁止阅读的书籍名单似乎无限延长，我们需要警惕的不仅是 100 本书，而是所有书籍。

Unfortunately, Wilde did not leave us the list of the hundred books it would be important to keep away from students. However, the list is manifestly less important than the idea that reading is not always a beneficial activity, but can turn out to be harmful. So menacing is reading perceived to be that in other texts, the list of books to be proscribed seems to have been extended ad infinitum, and it is not only a hundred books that we need to be wary of, but all of them.

王尔德最重要的关于他对阅读持谨慎态度的文章是《作为艺术家的批评家》。8 这篇文章的结构是两部分的对话，有两个角色，欧内斯特和吉尔伯特。吉尔伯特可能是最尖锐地表达作者非常原创的立场的人。

Wilde’s most important text about his wariness toward reading is called “The Critic as Artist.”8 Structured as a dialogue in two parts, it features two characters, Ernest and Gilbert. It is likely Gilbert who articulates the author’s very original positions most trenchantly.

吉尔伯特提出的第一个论点是为了反驳欧内斯特的断言，即在古希腊等最伟大的艺术时代，没有艺术评论家。为了反驳这一说法，吉尔伯特引用了亚里士多德的《诗学》等例子，以证明对于希腊人来说，创作与对艺术的一般考虑密不可分，因此创作者已经扮演了评论家的角色。

The first thesis developed by Gilbert is intended to counter Ernest’s assertion that in the greatest artistic epochs, such as ancient Greece, there were no art critics. Refuting that statement, Gilbert cites such examples as Aristotle’s Poetics to establish that for the Greeks, creation was inseparable from general considerations about art, and creators were thus already performing the role of critics.

这句话是对吉尔伯特另一段话的引言，在这段话中，吉尔伯特展示了艺术创作和批评如何远非独立的活动，实际上也无法分离：



This assertion serves as an introduction to a passage in which Gilbert shows how artistic creation and criticism, far from being separate activities, cannot in reality be disjoined:



欧内斯特：正如你所指出的，希腊人是一个艺术评论家的民族。我承认这一点，我为他们感到有点遗憾。因为创造能力高于批评能力。他们之间真的没有可比性。



Ernest: The Greeks were, as you have pointed out, a nation of art-critics. I acknowledge it, and I feel a little sorry for them. For the creative faculty is higher than the critical. There is really no comparison between them.



吉尔伯特：两者之间的对立完全是武断的。没有批判能力，就根本不存在名副其实的艺术创作。你刚才谈到了艺术家为我们实现生活并赋予其瞬间完美性的那种精妙的选择精神和微妙的选择本能。好吧，那种选择精神，那种微妙的省略策略，实际上是批判能力最具特征的一种，没有这种批判能力的人根本无法在艺术上创造任何东西。9



Gilbert: The antithesis between them is entirely arbitrary. Without the critical faculty, there is no artistic creation at all, worthy of the name. You spoke a little while ago of that fine spirit of choice and delicate instinct of selection by which the artist realises life for us, and gives to it a momentary perfection. Well, that spirit of choice, that subtle tact of omission, is really the critical faculty in one of its most characteristic moods, and no one who does not possess this critical faculty can create anything at all in art.9



因此，艺术创作与批评之间没有区别，任何伟大的创作都离不开批评，正如希腊人的例子所表明的那样。但反之亦然，批评本身也是一种艺术形式：



There is thus no separation between artistic creation and criticism, nor can there be any great creation without its share of criticism, as the example of the Greeks reveals. But the inverse is equally true, and criticism itself is a form of art:



欧内斯特：你一直在说批评是创造精神的重要组成部分，现在我完全接受你的理论。但是，创作之外的批评又如何呢？我有一个愚蠢的阅读期刊的习惯，在我看来，大多数现代批评都是毫无价值的。10



Ernest: You have been talking of criticism as an essential part of the creative spirit, and I now fully accept your theory. But what of criticism outside creation? I have a foolish habit of reading periodicals, and it seems to me that most modern criticism is perfectly valueless.10



吉尔伯特为批评家辩护，反对这种无足轻重的指责，他断言批评家比他们所评论的作者更有文化，批评需要的文化比艺术创作多得多。在为批评是一门艺术辩护时，首先出现了对不读书的辩护：



Defending critics against this accusation of insignificance, Gilbert asserts that they are far more cultured than the authors they review, and that criticism demands infinitely more culture than artistic creation. In this defense of criticism as an art, an apologia for non-reading first appears:



可怜的评论家们显然沦落为文学法庭的记者，艺术惯犯的记录者。有时人们说他们没有通读他们被要求批评的作品。他们没有。或者至少他们不应该。如果他们这样做，他们就会成为坚定的厌世者[……] 也没有必要。要知道一瓶酒的年份和质量，不必喝掉整桶酒。在半小时内判断一本书是否有价值或一文不值一定是非常容易的。如果一个人有形式感，十分钟真的足够了。谁想费力地读一本枯燥的书？一个人品尝它，这就足够了——我想，绰绰有余。11



The poor reviewers are apparently reduced to be the reporters of the police-court of literature, the chroniclers of the doings of the habitual criminals of art. It is sometimes said of them that they do not read all through the works they are called upon to criticise. They do not. Or at least they should not. If they did so, they would become confirmed misanthropes [ . . . ] Nor is it necessary. To know the vintage and quality of a wine one need not drink the whole cask. It must be perfectly easy in half an hour to say whether a book is worth anything or worth nothing. Ten minutes are really sufficient, if one has the instinct for form. Who wants to wade through a dull volume? One tastes it, and that is quite enough—more than enough, I should imagine.11



只需十分钟就能熟悉一本书——甚至更少，因为吉尔伯特一开始就理所当然地认为评论家不会阅读他们提交的书——这一断言出现在对评论家的辩护中，评论家的文化素养应该让他们能够迅速洞察一本书的精髓。因此，对不读书的辩护作为批评探究的一个分支进入了讨论；不读书据说只是专家获得的一种力量，一种把握本质的特殊能力。但本文的其余部分让我们明白，不读书也是一种责任，评论家花太多时间阅读他要谈论的书确实存在风险。或者，如果你愿意的话，在我们与书籍的接触中，有比简单的时间问题更具有决定性的因素。

The assertion that it takes only ten minutes to familiarize oneself with a book—or even considerably less, since Gilbert begins by assuming as a matter of course that critics don’t read the books submitted to them—thus surfaces in a defense of critics, whose cultural sophistication should allow them to perceive the essence of a book quickly. The defense of non-reading thus enters the discussion as an offshoot of the inquiry into criticism; non-reading is said simply to be a power acquired by specialists, a particular ability to grasp what is essential. But the remainder of the text gives us to understand that non-reading is also a duty, and that there is a true risk for the critic in spending too much time reading the book he is to talk about. Or, if you prefer, there are more decisive factors in our encounters with books than the simple question of time.

在本文的其余部分，王尔德越来越强调艺术与批评之间的这种联系，以至于他流露出对阅读的真正不信任。

Over the rest of the text, Wilde elaborates on this articulation between art and criticism with increasing emphasis, to the point where he reveals a veritable distrust of reading.

吉尔伯特继续为批评辩护，他断言谈论某件事比做某件事更困难。他首先从历史中举例，表明那些讲述古代英雄事迹的诗人比英雄更有功绩。行动“在其能量耗尽时就消亡了”，是“对事实的卑鄙让步，而世界是由歌手为梦想家创造的。” 12

Continuing his defense of criticism, Gilbert asserts that it is more difficult to speak about a thing than to do it. He begins by taking examples from history and showing that the poets who related the exploits of the heroes of antiquity were more meritorious than the heroes. Whereas action “dies at the moment of its energy” and is “a base concession to fact, the world is made by the singer for the dreamer.”12

恩内斯特反驳说，在将创造性艺术家提升到如此高度时，批评家的地位也有可能相应降低。作为回应，吉尔伯特回到了他的批评艺术理论：



Ernest retorts that in elevating the creative artist to such a height, there is a risk of proportionate abasement to the critic. In response, Gilbert returns to his theory of criticism as an art:



批评本身就是一门艺术。正如艺术创作需要批判能力的发挥，事实上，没有批判能力就不能说艺术创作存在，批评也确实具有最高意义上的创造性。事实上，批评既具有创造性，又具有独立性。13



Criticism is itself an art. And just as artistic creation implies the working of the critical faculty, and, indeed, without it cannot be said to exist at all, so Criticism is really creative in the highest sense of the word. Criticism is, in fact, both creative and independent.13



独立性的概念在这里至关重要，因为它将批评活动从文学和艺术中常常被赋予的次要和贬值的功能中解放出来。相反，它赋予批评一定程度的真正自主权：



The idea of independence is crucial here, since it liberates critical activity from the secondary and devalued function, with relation to literature and art, to which it is often consigned. Instead, it confers on criticism a measure of true autonomy:



是的，独立。批评不应以模仿或相似等低标准来评判，就像诗人或雕塑家的作品一样。批评家与他批评的艺术作品的关系，就像艺术家与可见的形式和色彩世界或看不见的激情和思想世界的关系一样。他甚至不需要最好的材料来完善他的艺术。任何东西都可以达到他的目的。14



Yes; independent. Criticism is no more to be judged by any low standard of imitation or resemblance than is the work of poet or sculptor. The critic occupies the same relation to the work of art that he criticises as the artist does to the visible world of form and colour, or the unseen world of passion and of thought. He does not even require for the perfection of his art the finest materials. Anything will serve his purpose.14



被批评的作品可以完全缺乏趣味，但这并不影响批评的进行，因为作品的存在只是一个借口：



The work being critiqued can be totally lacking in interest, then, without impairing the critical exercise, since the work is there only as a pretext:



就像古斯塔夫·福楼拜能够从鲁昂附近肮脏的永维尔修道院村一位乡村医生的傻妻子的肮脏和感伤的爱情中创造出经典之作，创造出风格独特的杰作一样，从不重要的主题，例如今年皇家艺术学院或任何一年皇家艺术学院的绘画，刘易斯·莫里斯先生的诗歌，奥奈特先生的小说，或亨利·亚瑟·琼斯先生的戏剧，真正的批评家，如果愿意的话，可以这样引导或浪费他的沉思能力，创作出美感十足、充满智慧敏锐性的作品。为什么不呢？愚钝总是对才华的不可抗拒的诱惑，愚蠢是永恒的野兽，它把智慧从洞穴中召唤出来。对于像批评家这样富有创造力的艺术家来说，主题意味着什么？小说家和画家也是如此。和他们一样，他可以在任何地方找到自己的动机。治疗就是考验。没有任何东西不包含建议或挑战。15



And just as out of the sordid and sentimental amours of the silly wife of a small country doctor in the squalid village of Yonville-l’Abbaye, near Rouen, Gustave Flaubert was able to create a classic, and make a masterpiece of style, so, from subjects of little or of no importance, such as the pictures in this year’s Royal Academy, or in any year’s Royal Academy for that matter, Mr. Lewis Morris’s poems, M. Ohnet’s novels, or the plays of Mr. Henry Arthur Jones, the true critic can, if it be his pleasure so to direct or waste his faculty of contemplation, produce work that will be flawless in beauty and instinct with intellectual subtlety. Why not? Dullness is always an irresistible temptation for brilliancy, and stupidity is the permanent Bestia Trionfans that calls wisdom from its cave. To an artist so creative as the critic, what does subject-matter signify? No more and no less than it does to the novelist and the painter. Like them, he can find his motives everywhere. Treatment is the test. There is nothing that has not in it suggestion or challenge.15



在王尔德举出的例子中，最显著的无疑是福楼拜，他夸耀自己写了一本“关于包法利夫人”的“无所事事的书”，将​​小说献给了永镇的居民。虽然福楼拜的作品经常被称为“现实主义”，但对他来说，文学与世界是独立的，遵循自己的规则。艺术不需要关心现实，即使现实仍然存在于背景中，它也要在自身中找到自己的连贯性。

Among the examples given by Wilde, the most significant is no doubt that of Flaubert, who boasted of Madame Bovary16 that he had written a “book about nothing,” by devoting his novel to the inhabitants of Yonville. Though Flaubert’s work is often called “realist,” literature for him was autonomous in relation to the world and obeyed its own rules. Art had no need to concern itself with reality, even if it remained present in the background, and was to find its own coherence in itself.

如果王尔德没有完全打破作品与批评之间的联系，那么他通过将作品简化为主题性质而大大削弱了这种联系，然后根据对主题的处理而不是对作品的忠实性来判断批评文本。专注于批评对象的主题性质使原文与艺术更加接近（艺术也可能将现实视为借口），同时它主张批评的优越性，批评对待艺术作品的方式就像艺术对待现实一样。

If Wilde does not break the link completely between the work and criticism, he strains it significantly by reducing the work to its thematic nature, with the critical text then being judged on the basis of its treatment of those themes and not for its faithfulness. Concentrating on the thematic nature of the object of criticism aligns this original text more closely with art (which may also treat reality as no more than a pretext), at the same time that it asserts the superiority of criticism, which treats works of art the way art treats reality.

从这个角度来看，批评文本并不比小说更关乎作品，正如福楼拜所说的小说并不关乎现实。我试图在这本书中质疑“关乎”这个词，以减轻遗忘这个词时的愧疚感。王尔德建议我们花十分钟阅读一本书，就是为了将这个概念完全抛在一边。这样做，我们让批评回归自身——回归它的孤独，但幸运的是，也回归它的创造能力。

From this perspective, the critical text is no more about the work than the novel, according to Flaubert, is about reality. What I have attempted to call into question in this book is this word about, in an effort to alleviate the guilt experienced when it is forgotten. The ten minutes that Wilde recommends we accord to a book are a function of setting that concept firmly aside. In doing so, we return criticism to itself— to its solitude, that is, but also, happily, to its capacity for invention.

因此，对于批评家来说，文学或艺术的地位就如同自然对于作家或画家一样次要。它们的作用不是作为批评家作品的对象，而是激励他写作。因为批评的唯一真正对象不是它所讨论的作品，而是它本身。

For the critic, thus, literature or art occupy the same secondary position as nature for the writer or painter. Their function is not to serve as the object of his work, but to stimulate him to write. For the only true object of criticism is not the work it discusses, but itself.

如果不清楚地了解创作主体在其中的位置，就不可能理解王尔德对批评和阅读的理解。根据王尔德的说法，批评的作者占据了最重要的地位：



To understand anything of Wilde’s conception of criticism and reading is impossible without a clear view of the location of the creative subject within it. According to Wilde, it is the writer of criticism who occupies the foreground:



不，更重要的是，我要说，最高级别的批评，作为个人印象的最纯粹形式，在某种程度上比创造更具创造性，因为它最少参考任何外部标准，事实上，它本身就是它存在的理由，而且，正如希腊人所说，它本身就是目的。17



Nay, more, I would say that the highest Criticism, being the purest form of personal impression, is in its way more creative than creation, as it has least reference to any standard external to itself, and is, in fact, its own reason for existing, and, as the Greeks would put it, in itself, and to itself, an end.17



最终，当批评不再与作品有任何关系时，它就达到了理想的形式。王尔德的悖论在于使批评成为一种没有支撑的不及物活动，或者更确切地说，是彻底取代了其支撑。换句话说，它的对象不是作品（因为任何作品都可以，就像福楼拜眼中的乡下家庭主妇一样），而是批评家本人：



Ultimately, criticism attains its ideal form when it no longer has any relation with a work. Wilde’s paradox lies in making criticism an intransitive activity without support, or rather in radically displacing its support. To put it another way, its object is not a work (since any work would do, just as any provincial housewife for Flaubert), but the critic himself:



我总是对当今那些作家和艺术家的愚蠢虚荣心感到好笑，他们似乎认为批评家的主要职责就是喋喋不休地谈论他们的二流作品。18



I am always amused by the silly vanity of those writers and artists of our day who seem to imagine that the primary function of the critic is to chatter about their second-rate work.18



因此，批评在切断与受到限制的作品的联系后，最终揭示了它与最强调主题的文学体裁，即自传的关系：



Thus does criticism, having cut its ties to a work whose constraints handicapped it, end up revealing its relation to the literary genre that most emphatically foregrounds the subject, namely autobiography:



这才是最高批评的真正意义，即一个人自己灵魂的记录。它比历史更迷人，因为它只关心自己。它比哲学更令人愉快，因为它的主题是具体的而不是抽象的，是真实的而不是模糊的。它是唯一文明的自传形式…… 19



That is what the highest criticism really is, the record of one’s own soul. It is more fascinating than history, as it is concerned simply with oneself. It is more delightful than philosophy, as its subject is concrete and not abstract, real and not vague. It is the only civilised form of autobiography . . . 19



批评是灵魂的记录，而灵魂是批评的深层对象，而不是支撑这一追求的短暂文学作品。至于瓦莱里，文学作品对王尔德来说是一种障碍，但原因不同。对瓦莱里来说，作品本身阻碍了批评家把握文学的本质，相对于文学，书籍只是一个偶然的对象。对王尔德来说，作品使批评家远离了批评家，而批评家实际上是整个批评活动存在的理由。但对他们每个人来说，好好读书就是远离作品。

Criticism is the record of a soul, and that soul is its deep object, not the transitory literary works that serve as supports in that quest. As for Valéry, the literary work is for Wilde a handicap, but for different reasons. For Valéry, the work itself prevents a critic from grasping the essence of literature, in relation to which the book is merely a contingent object. For Wilde, the work leads away from the critic, who is in fact the raison d’être of the whole critical exercise. But for each of them, to read well is to turn away from the work.

因此，对王尔德来说，谈论我们自己才是我们批评活动的最终目标。从这个角度来看，批评应该不惜一切代价，避免受到作品的束缚，否则可能会偏离这一目标。

Speaking about ourselves, then, is to Wilde what should be the ultimate aim of our critical activity. From this perspective, criticism should be protected at all cost from the grips of the work, which might otherwise distract it from that goal.

因此，在王尔德看来，文学作品应该沦为借口（“对批评家来说，艺术作品只是对他自己新作品的暗示，不一定与它所批评的东西有任何明显的相似之处”），20 但如果我们不小心，它很容易演变成一种障碍。因此，我们不应该对许多现代作品流连忘返，不仅是因为许多现代作品没什么意思——事实上，伟大的作品也是如此——还因为过于专注的阅读，忘记了读者的兴趣，可能会使读者远离自己。而对自我的反思是批评活动的主要理由，只有这样才能将批评提升到艺术的高度。

As a result, from Wilde’s perspective, the literary work should be reduced to mere pretext (“To the critic the work of art is simply a suggestion for a new work of his own, that need not necessarily bear any obvious resemblance to the thing it criticizes”),20 but if we’re not careful, it can easily metamorphose into an obstacle. So it is not only because many modern works are of little interest that we shouldn’t linger over them—the same, indeed, holds true for great works—but because an overly attentive reading, forgetful of the interests of the reader, may distance him from himself. Reflection on the self, meanwhile, is the primary justification for critical activity, and this alone can elevate criticism to the level of an art.

因此，与作品保持距离是王尔德思考阅读和文学批评的主旨。这使他得出了这一具有挑衅性的表述，他的大部分作品都说明了这一点：“我从不读一本我必须评论的书；它会让你产生偏见。” 21一本书可以激发读者的思考，同时也会将读者与他身上最原始的东西分开。因此，王尔德的悖论不仅仅与坏书有关；对于好书来说，它甚至更加有效。当你为了批评一本书而进入它时，你可能会失去最属于你自己的东西——这对书的假设有益，但对你自己却有害。

Keeping the work at a distance is thus a leitmotif of Wilde’s thinking about reading and literary criticism. It leads him to this provocative formulation, which a large part of his work serves to illustrate: “I never read a book I must review; it prejudices you so.”21 At the same time that a book may stimulate the reader’s thinking, it can also separate him from what, in him, is most original. Wilde’s paradox is thus not concerned solely with bad books; it is even more valid for good ones. When you enter a book in order to critique it, you risk losing what is most yourself—to the hypothetical benefit of the book, but to your own detriment.

阅读的悖论在于，通往自我的道路需要通过书籍，但这必须始终是一条通道。优秀的读者会进行书籍的穿越——他知道每本书都承载着他的一部分自我，只要他有智慧不在那里结束他的旅程，他就能接触到它。我们在瓦莱里、罗洛·马丁斯或我的某些学生等各式各样、充满灵感的读者身上都观察到了这种类型的穿越，当他们抓住一部他们只知其然或知之甚少的作品中的一个元素时，他们会不顾其他任何事情，追求自己的反思，从而注意不要忘记自己。

The paradox of reading is that the path toward ourselves passes through books, but that this must remain a passage. It is a traversal of books that a good reader engages in—a reader who knows that every book is the bearer of part of himself and can give him access to it, if only he has the wisdom not to end his journey there. And it is a traversal of just this type that we have observed in readers as diverse and as inspired as Valéry, Rollo Martins, or certain of my students who, when latching onto a single element from a work they know only vaguely or not at all, pursue their own reflection with no concern for anything else and thus take care not to lose sight of themselves.

如果我们记住，在我们分析的众多复杂情况下，最重要的是谈论我们自己而不是谈论书籍，或者通过书籍谈论我们自己（这很可能是谈论书籍的唯一好方法），我们对这些情况的看法就会发生显著变化。事实上，在有限的可用数据的基础上，迫切需要突出作品与我们之间的许多接触点。作品的标题、它在集体图书馆中的位置、向我们讲述作品的人的性质、书面或口头交流中建立的氛围，以及许多其他可能的情况，都为书籍本身提供了替代方案，使我们能够谈论自己而不必过于关注作品。

If we bear in mind, in the numerous complex situations we have analyzed, that what is essential is to speak about ourselves and not about books, or to speak about ourselves by way of books (which is the only way, in all probability, to speak well about them), our perception of these situations changes strikingly. In fact, it is the many points of encounter between the work and ourselves that it is urgent to bring to the fore, on the basis of the limited available data. The title of the work, its place in the collective library, the nature of the person who tells us about it, the atmosphere established in the written or spoken exchange, among many other possible instances, offer alternatives to the book itself that allow us to talk about ourselves without dwelling upon the work too closely.

与此同时，作品本身消失在围绕它的讨论中，让位于一个转瞬即逝的幻觉对象，一本幻影书，它吸引着我们的每一个投射，并随着我们对它的每一次评论而改变形状。因此，我们最好主要使用这本幻影书来支持我们对自己所做的工作，利用其可用的元素来撰写我们内心书籍的段落，并留意那些揭示我们内心深处不可替代的东西的元素。我们应该倾听我们自己，而不是“实际”的书——即使它有时会给我们动力——我们必须毫不动摇地追求自我写作。

The work itself, meanwhile, vanishes into the discourse around it and gives way to a fleeting, hallucinatory object, a phantom book that attracts our every projection and shifts its shape with each remark we make about it. We would do well, therefore, to use this phantom book primarily to support the work we do on ourselves, drawing on its available elements to compose passages of our inner books and taking heed of those elements that reveal something intimate and irreplaceable about us. It is ourselves we should be listening to, not the “actual” book—even if it sometimes provides us momentum—and it is the writing of self that we must pursue without swerving.

在任何特定背景下发明的书籍，如果源自主体的真实性，并铭刻在其内心世界的精心设计中，那么它就是可信的。例如，如果蒂夫人提议对《哈姆雷特》进行强有力的解读，尽管莎士比亚的戏剧对他们来说似乎完全陌生，那是因为他们在祖先信仰的真实性中感到如此深深的谴责，以至于他们准备用短暂的生命来激活他们发明的幻影书。最后，我们不必担心对文本撒谎，而只需担心对自己撒谎。

The book invented in any given context will be credible if it emerges from the truth of the subject and is inscribed within the elaboration of his inner universe. If the Tiv, for example, propose a strong reading of Hamlet, even though Shakespeare’s play would appear to be totally foreign to them, it is because they feel so deeply accused in the truth of their ancestral beliefs that they are prepared to animate the phantom book they have invented with a transitory life. In the end, we need not fear lying about the text, but only lying about ourselves.

除了所有的防御性之外，我们对未读书籍的讨论为那些知道如何抓住它的人提供了一个自我发现的宝贵机会，类似于自传。在这些对话中，无论是书面还是口头，语言都从其指涉世界的义务中解放出来，并通过穿越书籍，找到一种方式来谈论我们通常无法理解的事情。

Beyond all defensiveness, our discussion of unread books offers a privileged opportunity for self-discovery, akin to that of autobiography, to those who know how to seize it. In these conversations, whether written or spoken, language is liberated from its obligation to refer to the world and, through its traversal of books, can find a way to speak about what ordinarily eludes us.

除了自我发现的可能性之外，对未读书籍的讨论将我们置于创作过程的核心，引领我们回到创作的源头。谈论未读书籍就是在创作主体的诞生。在这个书本与自我分离的开端时刻，读者终于摆脱了他人话语的重负，找到了创作自己文本的力量，在那一刻，他自己也成为了一名作家。



Beyond the possibility of self-discovery, the discussion of unread books places us at the heart of the creative process, by leading us back to its source. To talk about unread books is to be present at the birth of the creative subject. In this inaugural moment when book and self separate, the reader, free at last from the weight of the words of others, may find the strength to invent his own text, and in that moment, he becomes a writer himself.

结语



Epilogue



我们对本书中遇到的微妙情况的分析表明，在准备面对此类对抗时，我们别无选择，只能接受我们心理的某种进化。仅仅学会如何在这些情况下保持镇定是不够的；我们必须深刻地改变我们与书籍的关系。

OUR ANALYSIS OF the delicate situations encountered in this book suggests that we have no other choice, in preparing to face such confrontations ourselves, than to accept a kind of evolution of our psychology. It is not enough for us simply to learn how to remain unflustered in these situations; we must profoundly transform our relationship to books.

首先，这种演变意味着我们要摆脱一系列几乎无意识的禁忌，这些禁忌束缚着我们对书籍的观念。从上学开始，我们就被鼓励将书籍视为不可触碰的物品，一想到要对它们进行改造，我们就感到内疚。

To begin with, such an evolution implies extricating ourselves from a whole series of mostly unconscious taboos that burden our notion of books. Encouraged from our school years onward to think of books as untouchable objects, we feel guilty at the very thought of subjecting them to transformation.

必须打破这些禁忌，才能真正开始倾听文学文本这个无限流动的对象。文本的流动性在参与对话或书面交流时得到增强，因为每个读者的主观性和他与他人的对话会激发文本的活力，而真诚地倾听文本意味着对书籍在这种情况下承担的所有可能性产生特殊的敏感性。

It is necessary to lift these taboos to begin to truly listen to the infinitely mobile object that is a literary text. The text’s mobility is enhanced whenever it participates in a conversation or a written exchange, where it is animated by the subjectivity of each reader and his dialogue with others, and to genuinely listen to it implies developing a particular sensitivity to all the possibilities that the book takes on in such circumstances.

但同样有必要做出这种努力去改变，以便我们能够倾听自己的声音，而不会错过将我们与每部作品联系在一起、根植于我们历史深处的私人共鸣。如果经历这种接触的人从内心深处汲取灵感，那么与未读书籍的接触将更加丰富——并且可以与他人分享。

But it is equally necessary to make this effort to change so that we can listen to ourselves, without missing the private resonances that connect us to every work and whose roots go deep in our history. The encounter with unread books will be more enriching—and sharable with others—if the person undergoing it draws his inspiration from deep within himself.

这种聆听文本和自己的不同模式再次让人想起了精神分析的合理预期，其主要功能是将患者从内心的束缚中解放出来，并在患者成为唯一主人的旅程结束时，为他打开所有的创造可能性。

This different mode of listening to texts and to oneself again recalls what may reasonably be expected from psychoanalysis, the primary function of which is to free the patient from his inner constraints and, by the end of a journey over which he remains the sole master, to open him up to all his creative possibilities.

自己成为一名创造者：这是我们通过从一系列例子中得出的观察结果而得出的计划，只有内心进化已完全摆脱罪恶感的人才可以参与其中。

To become a creator yourself: this is the project to which we have been brought by the observations drawn from our series of examples, and it is a project accessible only to those whose inner evolution has freed them from guilt completely.

这些人知道，谈论自己没读过的书是一种真正的创造性活动，与那些更受社会认可的活动一样有价值——即使它进行得更谨慎。事实上，对传统艺术实践的关注导致了对其他本质上以某种秘密方式进行的艺术实践的某种忽视甚至误解。

These people know that talking about books you haven’t read is an authentically creative activity, as worthy—even if it takes place more discreetly—as those that are more socially acknowledged. The attention accorded to traditional artistic practices has resulted, in fact, in a certain neglect and even misperception of those others that by their nature transpire in a kind of secrecy.

然而，我们怎么能否认谈论自己没读过的书是一种真正的创造性活动，它与其他形式的艺术有着同样的要求呢？只要想想它所需要的所有技能——倾听作品的潜力、分析不断变化的背景、关注他人及其反应、掌控扣人心弦的叙述——你一定会被说服。

How can one deny, however, that talking about books you haven’t read constitutes an authentic creative activity, making the same demands as other forms of art? Just think of all the skills it calls into play—listening to the potentialities of a work, analyzing its ever-changing context, paying attention to others and their reactions, taking charge of a gripping narrative—and you will surely find yourself convinced.

此外，我们的新创造力可能远远超出了我们对未读书籍的评论。在更高层次上，任何类型的创造力，无论其对象是什么，都需要与书籍保持一定的距离。正如奥斯卡·王尔德所言，阅读和创造之间存在一种矛盾，因为每个读者都冒着迷失在别人的书中而远离自己个人世界的风险。如果对未读过的书的评论是一种创造，那么反之亦然：创造意味着不要在书上停留太久。

Furthermore, our new creativity may go far beyond our comments on unread books. At a higher level, any kind of creativity, whatever its object, entails a certain detachment from books. For as illustrated by Oscar Wilde, there is a kind of antinomy between reading and creating, since every reader runs the risk, lost as he is in someone else’s book, of distancing himself from his personal universe. And if commentary on books one hasn’t read is a kind of creation, the converse is also true: creation implies not lingering too long over books.

因此，成为我们自己作品的创作者是学徒期对我们未读过的书进行评论的合理且理想的延伸。这种创造力是自我征服和摆脱文化负担的一步，文化负担可能会阻碍那些未受过文化训练的人的生存，从而阻碍他们赋予作品生命的能力。

Becoming the creators of our own works is thus the logical and desirable extension of an apprenticeship in commenting on books we haven’t read. This creativity is one step along the path to self-conquest and to our liberation from the burden of culture, which may impede the existence of those who haven’t been trained in its mastery, and thus in the ability to bring life to their works.

如果学习谈论你没读过的书是许多人第一次接触创作的要求，那么教师就负有特殊的责任。鉴于教师的地位和个人经验，他们是在学生中推广这种做法的理想人选。

If learning to talk about books you haven’t read is for many people their first encounter with the demands of creation, particular responsibility lies with those who teach. Given their position and personal experience, teachers are ideally placed to advance this practice among their students.

尽管学生在接受教育时就被灌输了阅读的艺术，甚至被教导如何谈论书籍，但谈论他们没有读过的书的艺术却在我们的课程中缺席，好像从来没有人想过质疑必须读过一本书才能谈论它这一前提。那么，当他们在考试中被问到一本他们“不了解”的书而无法回答时，我们为什么对他们的苦恼感到惊讶呢？

Although students are initiated during their education into the art of reading and are even taught how to talk about books, the art of talking about books they haven’t read is singularly absent from our curricula, as though no one had ever thought to question the premise that it is necessary to have read a book in order to talk about it. So why are we astonished by their distress when they are questioned on an exam about a book they don’t “know” and cannot find the wherewithal to reply?

我们的教育制度显然未能履行其神圣化职责，结果，我们的学生仍然无法主张发明书籍的权利。由于对文本应有的尊重和对文本的禁止修改，太多学生被迫背诵文本或记住文本“包含的内容”，他们失去了逃避的能力，禁止自己在想象力非常有用的情况下发挥想象力。

Our educational system is clearly failing to fulfill its duties of deconsecration, and as a result, our students remain unable to claim the right to invent books. Paralyzed by the respect due to texts and the prohibition against modifying them, forced to learn them by heart or to memorize what they “contain,” too many students lose their capacity for escape and forbid themselves to call on their imagination in circumstances where that faculty would be extraordinarily useful.

相反，向他们展示一本书在每一次阅读中都会得到重新创造，这将使他们能够毫发无损地摆脱许多困难的情况，甚至从中受益。因为知道如何巧妙地谈论我们不熟悉的事情，其价值远远超出了书本的范畴。正如我们看到的众多作家所体现的那样，我们的整个文化都向那些能够切断话语与对象之间的联系并谈论自己的人开放。

To show them, instead, that a book is reinvented with every reading would give them the means to emerge unscathed, and even with some benefit, from a multitude of difficult situations. For knowing how to speak with finesse about something with which we are unacquainted has value far beyond the realm of books. As we have seen exemplified by numerous authors, the entirety of our culture opens up to those with the ability to cut the bonds between discourse and its object, and to speak about themselves.

归根结底，关键在于向学生揭示真正重要的东西：他们自己创造的世界。除了让学生对发明艺术（即自我发明）敏感之外，你还能给学生什么更好的礼物呢？所有教育都应努力帮助接受教育的人在艺术作品方面获得足够的自由，使他们自己成为作家和艺术家。

The key, in the end, is to reveal to students what is truly essential: the world of their own creation. What better gift could you make to a student than to render him sensitive to the art of invention—which is to say, self-invention? All education should strive to help those receiving it to gain enough freedom in relation to works of art to themselves become writers and artists.

鉴于本书中所提出的所有理由，我将继续不让批评偏离我的道路，始终如一地、平静地谈论我未读过的书。

For all the reasons evoked in this book, I shall, for my part, continue, without allowing criticism to divert me from my path, to speak consistently and serenely about books I haven’t read.

如果我选择其他方式，再次加入被动阅读的人群，我会觉得背叛了自己，因为我不忠于我所处的环境，不忠于我为了创作而不得不走的书籍之路，也不忠于我今天所感受到的责任，即帮助其他人克服对文化的恐惧，并敢于抛弃文化开始写作。

Were I to proceed otherwise and again join the mob of passive readers, I would feel that I was betraying myself by being unfaithful to the milieu from which I came; to the path among books I have been obliged to take in order to create; and to the duty I feel today to assist others in overcoming their fear of culture, and in daring to leave it behind to begin to write.

A Note on the Author

皮埃尔·巴亚尔是巴黎第八大学的法国文学教授，也是一名心理分析学家。他是《谁杀了罗杰·艾克罗伊德？》等多部著作的作者。



PIERRE BAYARD is a professor of French literature at the University of Paris VIII and a psychoanalyst. He is the author of Who Killed Roger Ackroyd? and of many other books.



J EFFREY M EHLMAN是波士顿大学的法国文学教授，著有《Emigré New York》等多部著作。他翻译过德里达、拉康、布朗肖等作家的作品。

JEFFREY MEHLMAN is a professor of French literature at Boston University and the author of a number of books, including Emigré New York. He has translated works by Derrida, Lacan, Blanchot, and other authors.

A Note on the Author

皮埃尔·巴亚尔是巴黎第八大学的法国文学教授，也是一名心理分析学家。他是《谁杀了罗杰·艾克罗伊德？》等多部著作的作者。

J EFFREY M EHLMAN是波士顿大学的法国文学教授，著有《Emigré New York》等多部著作。他翻译过德里达、拉康、布朗肖等作家的作品。

JEFFREY MEHLMAN is a professor of French literature at Boston University and the author of a number of books, including Emigré New York. He has translated works by Derrida, Lacan, Blanchot, and other authors.

《如何谈论你还没读过的书》获得好评



Praise for How to Talk About Books You Haven’t Read



“作为一名文学老师，[拜亚德] 似乎认为他的最终目标是鼓励创造力。他写道：‘所有教育都应该努力帮助接受教育的人在艺术作品方面获得足够的自由，使他们自己成为作家和艺术家。’这是一个迷人但最终令人恐惧的前景——一个充满作家和艺术家的世界。在拜亚德的非阅读乌托邦中，印刷机永远不会被发明，更不用说青霉素或 MacBook 了。我非常怀疑假装读过这本书会提升你的创造力。另一方面，阅读它可能会让你想起你为什么喜欢阅读。”

“As a teacher of literature, [Bayard] seems to believe that his ultimate goal is to encourage creativity. ‘All education,’ he writes, ‘should strive to help those receiving it to gain enough freedom in relation to works of art to themselves become writers and artists.’ It’s a charming but ultimately terrifying prospect—a world full of writers and artists. In Bayard’s nonreading utopia the printing press would never have been invented, let alone penicillin or the MacBook. I seriously doubt that pretending to have read this book will boost your creativity. On the other hand, reading it may remind you why you love reading.”

—杰伊·麦金纳尼，《纽约时报书评》

—Jay McInerney, New York Times Book Review

“我可能不应该提起这些，但拜尔德先生认为读书的最好理由之一是它能让你谈论自己。《如何谈论你没读过的书》是一篇有趣的论文，探讨了如何以一种舒适的方式建立文化素养。这本书略带讽刺，但提出了一些严肃的问题：我们读书的真正动机是什么？读书有客观的方法吗？我们从读过的书中学到了什么？”

“I probably shouldn’t bring any of this up, but Mr. Bayard holds that one of the best reasons for reading a book is that it allows you to talk about yourself. How to Talk About Books You Haven’t Read is an amusing disquisition on what is required to establish cultural literacy in a comfortable way. Lightly laced with irony, the book nonetheless raises such serious questions as: What are our true motives for reading? Is there an objective way to read a book? What do we retain from the books we’ve read?”

—约瑟夫·爱泼斯坦，《华尔街日报》

—Joseph Epstein, Wall Street Journal

“他拯救了法国喜剧文学，因为他的书非常有趣，而且有点棘手。”

“He has redeemed French comic literature, because his book is very funny, in a tricky sort of way.”

—简·斯迈利，《洛杉矶时报》

—Jane Smiley, Los Angeles Times

“我们读书是为了了解自己；我们与他人分享我们的阅读经历，以了解他人。然而，在皮埃尔·巴亚尔看来，读书和不读书但讨论书籍并不一定互相排斥。在这篇半认真半调皮的论述阅读意义的文章中，不读书成为了阅读的另一种形式。以典型的法国方式，巴亚尔设计了一种巧妙的方法，让人们可以毫无羞耻地明智地谈论书籍：浏览；阅读评论；编造一些自己读过但忘记的东西；然后，如果一个人完全不知道该说什么关于那本书，巴亚尔建议谈谈自己。在他讽刺的评论之下（让人想起阿兰·德波顿关于旅行和建筑的哲学书籍），巴亚尔将阅读视为与世界进行更广泛的社会话语的一个组成部分；通过二手渠道谈论书籍，既不会欺骗别人，也不会贬低作者，毕竟作者只是想知道人们是否喜欢他的书。”

“We read to understand ourselves; we share our reading with others to understand them. Yet, in Pierre Bayard’s view, reading books and not reading but discussing them, anyway, are not necessarily mutually exclusive. In this half-serious, half-mischievous treatise on what reading means, non-reading becomes another form of reading. In quintessential French fashion, Bayard has devised a felicitous methodology to permit one to converse intelligently about books without shame: there’s skimming; reading reviews; making up stuff about what one has read and forgotten; and then, if one has completely run out of things to say about the book in question, Bayard suggests talking about oneself. Beneath his wry commentary (reminiscent of Alain de Botton’s philosophical books on travel and architecture), Bayard views reading as one component of a larger social discourse with the world; to be able to chat about books via second-hand means is neither duplicitous to others nor demeaning to the author, who, after all, really only wants to know that one likes his book.”

—史蒂夫·夏皮罗，《雨天图书》（NPR晨间版评论）

—Steve Shapiro, Rainy Day Books (reviewed on NPR’s Morning Edition)

“这是一本关于书籍的诙谐指南，它将长久地留在爱书人的心中。”

“One of those witty guides to thinking about books that long will linger in the minds of booklovers.”

—苏珊·拉森，《新奥尔良时报》

—Susan Larson, New Orleans Times-Picayune

“对这个禁忌话题的颠覆性、漫不经心的‘沉思’，是文学创作中伪造的……就像哈里·G·法兰克福 2005 年的散文集《论胡说八道》一样，拜尔德作品的乐趣之一就是与之争论……很有趣。”

“A subversive, insouciant ‘meditation on this forbidden subject,’ the literary act of faking it . . . Like Harry G. Frankfurt’s sleeper 2005 essay book, On Bullshit, part of the pleasure of Bayard’s work is arguing with it . . . Entertaining.”

—凯伦·R·朗，《克利夫兰诚恳报》

—Karen R. Long, Cleveland Plain Dealer

“机智、迷人而且充满乐趣。”

“Witty and charming and often fun.”

— 萨姆·安德森，纽约

—Sam Anderson, New York

“在这部充满灵感的胡言乱语的作品中——尽管如此，它还是唤起了我们对文化知识差距的真正不安全感——阅读不仅是多余的，而且毫无意义。我们只需要显得博览群书即可。”

“In this work of inspired nonsense—which nevertheless evokes our very real sense of insecurity about the gaps in our cultural knowledge— reading is not only superfluous, it is meaningless. Our need to appear well-read is all.”

—莎拉·戈尔德，《芝加哥论坛报》

—Sarah Gold, Chicago Tribune

“《如何谈论你没读过的书》令人愉快，甚至富有洞察力。我们不需要读过《哈姆雷特》就知道这是一部关于优柔寡断的王子的莎士比亚故事。多亏了巴亚尔，“读还是不读？”这个问题再也不会像以前那样显得那么原始或愚蠢。这位迷人的教授在解除自己对书籍以及王尔德、瓦莱里和蒙田的知识武装时，让我们对自己微不足道的武器库更加放心……对于那些仍然相信艺术的新一代人来说，应该阅读、沉思、大笑，并屈服于记忆的消逝。”

“How to Talk About Books You Haven’t Read is delightful—and even insightful. We need not have read Hamlet to know it’s a Shakespeare story about a vacillating prince. Thanks to Bayard, ‘To read or not to read?’ will never seem as primitive or stupid a question as it once did. And the charming professor, in disarming his own knowledge of books, as well as Wilde’s, Valery’s, and Montaigne’s, makes us more comfortable with our petty arsenal . . . For those in the rising generation who still believe in art, Bayard’s prescription should be read, mused over, laughed through, and surrendered to memory’s fade.”

—Garin K. Hovannisian，《国家评论》

—Garin K. Hovannisian, National Review

“挑逗而迷人……与其引人注目的标题相反，拜尔的这本薄薄的书并不是一本油嘴滑舌的说明书，针对的是那些渴望在鸡尾酒会上给更有文化的朋友留下深刻印象的俗人。相反，它是对我们与文字接触的无数方式的深刻、常常幽默的沉思，以及我们与文本互动的过程如何不仅塑造了我们对作者作品的看法，而且最终通过真正的创造性行为改变了我们的内心生活……拜尔的书可能给一些人留下颠覆性甚至是危险的印象。尽管如此，我相信狂热的读者（我相信这一类别描述了该出版物的大多数订阅者）可能不会很快放弃蜷缩着读一本好书的简单行为所带来的基本乐趣。”

“Provocative and charming . . . Contrary to its attention-grabbing title, Bayard’s slim book isn’t a glib instruction manual aimed at philistines hungry for quick tips to impress their more literate friends at cocktail parties. Instead, it’s a thoughtful, often humorous, meditation on the myriad ways in which we encounter the written word and how the process by which we interact with text not only shapes our perceptions of an author’s work but also ultimately transforms our inner lives in a true act of creativity . . . Bayard’s book may strike some as a subversive, even dangerous, work. Still, I doubt avid readers—a category I trust describes most subscribers to this publication—are likely to forsake any time soon the elemental pleasure that attaches to the simple act of curling up with a good book.”

—Harvey Freedenberg，《货架意识》

—Harvey Freedenberg, Shelf Awareness

“巴黎大学法国文学教授巴亚尔（《谁杀了罗杰·艾克罗伊德？》）公开（尽管并非完全令人信服）承认自己没有时间也没有意愿读书。但他非常清楚，在他的职业中，人们通常希望人们阅读自己正在教授或与同事讨论的文学作品。在这篇法国畅销书的长篇论文中，巴亚尔认为阅读行为不如了解一本书的社会和思想背景重要。他对此深信不疑，他声称与一个同样不熟悉自己没有读过的书的人讨论这本书会带来很大的乐趣——甚至是启发。尽管表面上如此，巴亚尔的这本书并不是一本自助书籍或伟大文学的虚张声势指南，而是警告人们不要试图用自己读过多少书来打动别人。事实上，他们大多数时候都在撒谎，他声称，在完全阅读和完全不阅读之间有很多等级，包括听说过一本书、略读过它并忘记它的内容。过多晦涩难懂的精神分析术语有时会压倒拜亚德的论点，但拜亚德关于不读书的论点至少是半开玩笑的，值得一读。”

“Bayard (Who Killed Roger Ackroyd?), a professor of French literature at the University of Paris openly (if not entirely convincingly), confesses to having neither the time nor the inclination to do much reading. Yet he is all too aware that in his profession, one is often expected to have read the literature one is teaching or talking about with colleagues. In this extended essay, a bestseller in France, Bayard argues that the act of reading is less important than knowing the social and intellectual context of a book. He is so convinced of this that he claims there is great enjoyment—and even enlightenment—in discussing a book one has not read with someone equally unfamiliar with it. Despite appearances, Bayard’s volume is not a self-help book or a bluffer’s guide to great literature, but instead serves to warn people not to try to impress others with how much they have read. The truth is, most of the time they’re fibbing and there are many gradations between total reading and complete non-reading, he declares, including hearing about a book, skimming it and forgetting its contents. A little too much impenetrable psychoanalytic jargon sometimes threatens to overwhelm Bayard’s argument, but Bayard’s at least partly tongue-in-cheek argument about not reading is well worth reading.”

—《出版人周刊》

—Publishers Weekly

“在这部滑稽而精巧的讽刺作品中，拜尔德再次证明了博学多识和幽默风趣绝不是互相排斥的。作者以斯威夫特式的风格，坚定地伪造了对他所谓的“不读书”艺术的辩护，在这种艺术中，人们必须声称自己有权谈论自己浏览过、忘记或根本没有读过的书。他半开玩笑地认为，熟悉一本书的声誉，尤其是了解它在书目等级中的位置，就足够了——事实上，在几乎所有方面都是更好的选择。毕竟，有多少评论家真正读过普鲁斯特的小说？正如拜尔德所说，保罗·瓦莱里肯定没有读过，但这并没有阻止他详细讨论它。这里弥漫着一丝法国解构理论的幸灾乐祸的反常气息，但这本书真正的天使是奥斯卡·王尔德，他的俏皮话为巴亚尔提供了一个模拟的战斗口号：“我从来没有读过一本我必须评论的书；它会让你产生偏见。”

“In this hilarious and elaborate spoof, Bayard proves once again that being almost ridiculously erudite and screamingly funny are by no means mutually exclusive. In grand Swiftian style, the author offers a staunch pseudo defense of the art of what he calls ‘non-reading,’ in which one must claim as all but divine the right to hold forth about books that one has skimmed, forgotten, or failed to read at all. With tongue firmly in cheek, he argues that it’s more than enough—indeed, preferable in virtually all respects—to be familiar with a book’s reputation and in particular to understand its place in the bibliographic pecking order. What percentage of commentators, after all, has actually read Proust’s novel? Paul Valery certainly hadn’t, as Bayard notes, but it didn’t stop him from discoursing upon it at length. There’s a whiff of the gleeful perversity of French deconstruction theory here, but the book’s true angel is Oscar Wilde, whose witticism provides Bayard with a mock rallying cry: ‘I never read a book I must review; it prejudices you so.’ ”

—书单

—Booklist

“我读过并喜欢皮埃尔·拜尔的书。这本书风趣、睿智、真实——巧妙地结合了精妙的法式哲学和诙谐幽默，并诚实地评价了阅读的意义和意义。”

“I read and adored Pierre Bayard’s book. It’s funny, smart, and so true— a wonderful combination of slick French philosophizing and tongue-in-cheek wit, and an honest appraisal of what it means, or doesn’t mean, to read.”

—克莱尔·梅苏德， 《皇帝的孩子》作者

—Clare Messud, author of The Emperor’s Children

“一本关于喧闹阶层生活的生存指南……显然我们非常需要它。”

“A survivor’s guide to life in the chattering classes . . . evidently much in need.”

-纽约时报

—New York Times

“拜尔德以罕见的幽默感，自由地重新思考了文学的社会用途和读者的地位……阅读或浏览《如何谈论你没读过的书》 ……或者只是听听人们对此的看法，这样你就可以轻松地谈论它。无论哪种方式，你都可能无法忘记它。”

“With rare humor, Bayard liberally rethinks the social use [of literature] and the position of the reader . . . Read or skim How to Talk About Books You Haven’t Read. Or simply listen to what people say about it so that you can talk about it with ease. In either case, you may not be able to forget it.”

—Les Inrockuptibles

—Les Inrockuptibles

“书商们对一些顾客的这种令人困惑却又令人羡慕的假设并不陌生，他们认为自己已经读完了书店里的每一本书。为什么要破坏这种幻想呢？这本精彩、生动、搞笑的书断言，了解一本书在更广泛的文学世界中的位置，了解人们对它的反应，以及简单的无耻就是你所需要的一切。拜尔德（碰巧是巴黎大学的法国文学教授）显然很看重阅读，但他也不太看重直觉反应、即兴创作和未经证实的观点。他认为谈论书籍是表达自己和“内心书籍”的一种方式。我很高兴地阅读了《如何谈论你没读过的书》的每一个字，但我再也不会觉得有义务对其他任何书这样做了！”

“Booksellers are familiar with the baffling yet flattering assumption on the part of some customers that they’ve read every book in the store. Why ruin the illusion? This brilliant, vibrant, and hilarious book asserts that knowing where a book is situated in the larger world of literature, knowing people’s reactions to it, and just plain shamelessness are all you need. Bayard (who happens to be a professor of French literature at the University of Paris) clearly values reading, but less typically he also values gut reactions, improvisation, and uninformed opinions. He sees talking about books as a way of expressing yourself and your ‘inner book.’ I joyfully read every word of How to Talk About Books You Haven’t Read, and yet will never feel obligated to do so to any other book again!”

—奥黛丽·布罗克豪斯，舒勒图书与音乐奥克莫斯

—Audrey Brockhaus, Schuler Books & Music Okemos
